Proxy Marriage: Guardian Marrying His Ward to Himself
Inter-madhhab dispute on guardian/proxy self-marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a guardian or proxy may marry his ward to himself, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A guardian or proxy is an intermediary, so he can act for both sides in marriage.

This passage tackles a key point of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can the same person represent both the marriage offer and acceptance? The Hanafi school permits it based on the concept of the guardian or proxy as a mere intermediary (safir). We will unpack the arguments from the text and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text presents two scenarios: a guardian (paternal cousin) marrying his ward to himself, and a proxy (wakil) marrying his female client to himself. Both involve the same legal question: can one person act as both parties in a marriage contract?
The guardian must have legal guardianship (wilayah) over the woman.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and procedure
The Hanafi ruling is that it is valid. The procedure: the guardian says 'I have married So-and-so to myself' or 'I have married her, so bear witness.' Acceptance (qabul) is not needed because the statement covers both sides.
The text emphasizes that the declaration includes the meaning of both offer and acceptance.
3
Identify the opposing position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) hold it is invalid. Their proof: one person cannot be both the transferor (mumallik) and the transferee (mutamallik) in a contract.
Zufar is an early Hanafi jurist who sometimes differed from the majority.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the guardian is not acting as a true party; he is an intermediary (safir) conveying the statements from both sides. Therefore, the single person can serve as the vessel for both sides.
The term 'safir' is key: he is a messenger, not a principal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi practice, a guardian can directly marry his ward to himself without a separate acceptance. In Shafi'i practice, such a marriage would be invalid and would require a different guardian to act for the woman.
This difference arises from the conceptualisation of the guardian's role.

Commentary
This passage discusses two related issues in proxy marriage: first, whether a paternal cousin (who is a guardian) can marry his female cousin to himself; second, whether a proxy (wakil) can marry his female client to himself.

For the first issue, the text states that it is permissible for the guardian (e.g., a paternal uncle's son who has guardianship) to marry his ward to himself. The procedure is that he says, 'I have married so-and-so to myself' or 'I have married her, so bear witness.' Acceptance is not needed because the declaration includes both the offer and acceptance. The Shafi'i school and Zufar (from Hanafi school) object, arguing that one person cannot act as both the one who transfers ownership (mumallik) and the one who receives it (mutamallik). The Hanafi response is that the guardian is merely an intermediary (safir) acting on behalf of both parties, so it is permissible. This shows a fundamental difference: Hanafis view the guardian as an agent for both sides, while Shafi'is see a conflict of interest.

The second issue is about a proxy (not the guardian) marrying his client. The text says it is permissible. The analogy is similar: the proxy, though an agent, can be an intermediary from both sides.

The passage also includes a continuation of the earlier discussion about the guardian's right to separate due to deficient mahr, but that is part of the previous section. This lesson focuses on the proxy issue which begins with the heading 'فصل: في بيان الوكالة بالنكاح'.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakīl): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another, in this context specifically to perform a marriage contract for the client.
الولي (al-walī): The guardian of a woman, who has the authority to contract her marriage; in this passage, it includes paternal relatives who are 'asaba.
سفير (safīr): Intermediary or messenger who conveys the statements of both parties in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the marriage is considered a gift.
D) Because the proxy is a separate party.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a guardian or proxy to marry his ward to himself because he acts as an intermediary representing both sides.

Father's Authority in Minor Marriage – Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on father's authority in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father marrying his minor child with deficient mahr or to a non-kuf' spouse, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the definition of ghabn fahish.

Core Idea
Fathers may marry minor children with deficient mahr; other guardians cannot.

Guardians in marriage wield significant authority, but how far does that authority extend when it comes to the financial interests of a minor? This lesson examines a specific case: a father marrying his minor child with a mahr significantly below the proper amount (ghabn fahish) or to a non-compatible spouse. Abu Hanifa upholds the father's discretion, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, dissent. By analyzing their proofs, we uncover deeper principles about the role of custom, analogy, and the unique status of the father and grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the legal act under discussion? It is a father (or grandfather) marrying his minor child to a non-kuf' spouse or with a mahr that is excessively low (ghabn fahish). According to Abu Hanifa, this contract is valid (sahih). According to the Sahibayn, it is invalid (la yajuz).
The validity is specific to the father and grandfather; other guardians cannot do this by consensus.
2
Define 'ghabn fahish'
The passage defines ghabn fahish as marrying a minor daughter for 10 dirhams when her proper mahr is 1000, or marrying a minor son for 1000 when his proper mahr is 10. Anything less than half the proper mahr is considered ghabn fahish.
Lesser deficiencies are tolerated (ghabn yasir) and do not affect validity.
3
Trace the arguments
The Sahibayn argue by analogy (qiyas) to financial guardianship: just as a guardian cannot diminish a ward's property, he cannot diminish the child's mahr. Abu Hanifa counters that marriage has other purposes beyond mahr, such as compatibility and benefit, and that fathers may sacrifice mahr for a better match. He also uses an analogy to kafa'ah: guardians feel pride in high mahr and shame in low mahr, similar to the pride in having a kuf' match.
Abu Hanifa's view is the mufta bihi (operative ruling).
4
Note restrictions on the father's authority
Even Abu Hanifa restricts the father: he cannot marry the child if he is drunk or corrupt (fasiq), nor can he cause obvious harm. Similarly, the grandfather is treated like the father. Other guardians (e.g., brother, uncle) are completely prohibited from such marriages.
These restrictions protect the child from neglect or exploitation.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider a father marrying his minor daughter to a wealthy but non-kuf' suitor (e.g., a non-Arab) with a low mahr. Under Abu Hanifa's view, the marriage is valid. The Sahibayn would object. Understanding this dispute helps a mufti weigh the father's discretion against the child's financial rights.
The mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa) gives the father wide latitude.

The father is complete in opinion, he chooses benefit for his child, and likewise the grandfather. Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) regarding the authority of a father or grandfather to marry off a minor child with a significant deficiency in mahr (ghabn fahish) or to a non-compatible (non-kuf') spouse. The text establishes that for the father and grandfather, such a marriage is valid according to Abu Hanifa, because the father has complete discretion and looks out for the child's benefit, even if the mahr is much less than the proper mahr. The Sahibayn disagree, analogizing it to financial transactions where guardians cannot diminish the ward's property. The text also clarifies that 'ghabn fahish' is when the mahr is less than half the proper mahr. For other guardians (like a brother or uncle), such a marriage is invalid by consensus, as they lack the father's complete authority. The passage then transitions to a new chapter on agency in marriage.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Excessive deceit in mahr, defined as marrying with less than half the proper mahr.
غير كفؤ (ghayr kuf'): A spouse not equal in social status, e.g., a free man marrying a slave woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The marriage is void ab initio.

Key Takeaway
A father may marry his minor child with deficient mahr or to a non-kuf' spouse by virtue of his broader authority, but other guardians cannot, and the father himself is restricted if he is corrupt or drunk.

Self-Marriage by a Guardian or Agent: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Zufar
Rulings and disputes on self-marriage by a guardian-agent in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on self-marriage by a cousin-guardian and an agent, explain the Hanafi proof (safir argument), and compare it with the Shafi'i/Zufar objection to identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A guardian or agent can marry himself to his ward or principal because he acts as a messenger representing both sides.

This lesson examines a specific dispute in marriage agency: can a man who is either a guardian (like a cousin) or an agent marry himself to the woman he represents? The Hanafi school says yes if properly authorized, relying on the concept of the representative as a messenger (safir). The Shafi'i school and Zufar disagree, arguing that one person cannot be both giver and receiver. We'll explore the proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two scenarios: (1) a cousin who is a guardian marrying his female cousin to himself; (2) an agent marrying his principal to herself when specifically authorized. State that the Hanafi school rules both as valid.
The cousin does not need separate acceptance because his statement contains both parts.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl hold it invalid. Shafi'i has a nuanced opinion: if the person is a guardian (wali), it may be valid; if an agent (wakil), it is not.
Zufar rejects both cases entirely.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the opponents' reasoning: one person cannot be both the giver (mumallik) and the receiver (mutamallik) in a contract.
This is a logical argument against self-contracting.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the cousin/agent is not acting as a principal but as a messenger (safir) or intermediary. A messenger can represent both sides, just as a grandfather can marry his grandchildren.
Hanafi law recognizes the capacity to represent multiple parties in marriage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, such marriages are valid without separate acceptance, whereas under Shafi'i/Zufar they are invalid. This affects whether the couple must repeat the contract or separate.
The disagreement has real consequences for marital validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: في بيان الوكالة بالنكاح وغيرها [رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] لا بن العم أن يزوج بنت عمه من نفسه: إذا كانت الولاية له وصورته أن يقول: زوجت فلانة من نفسي أو تزوجتها فاشهدوا، ولا يحتاج إلى القبول؛ لأنه قد تضمن معنى الشطرين، وقال الشافعي وزفر : لا يجوز؛ لأن الواحد لا يكون مملكاً ومتملكاً، ولنا : أنه معبر وسفير فصلح سفيراً من الجانبين، وقوله: "الوكيل أن يزوج إلخ" وصورته أن يقول: اشهدوا أني زوجت فلانة من نفسي. رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] والمراد من الوكيل الذي وكلته المرأة أن يزوجها من نفسه حتى لو وكلته أن يزوجها من رجل لم يجز له أن يتزوجها؛ لأن المعرفة لا يدخل في النكرة، وقال زفر: لا يجوز فيهما، وفي أحد قولي الشافعي إن كان وليا لها يجوز وإن كان وكيلا لا. (مسكين، مستخلص)
Chapter: On the explanation of agency in marriage and other matters. It is permissible for the cousin to marry his paternal uncle's daughter to himself: when he has guardianship, and its form is that he says: 'I have married so-and-so to myself' or 'I have married her, so bear witness,' and acceptance is not needed because it contains the meaning of both parts. Al-Shafi'i and Zufar said: it is not permissible because one person cannot be both giver and receiver. Our proof: he is an intermediary and a messenger, so he is fit as a messenger from both sides. And his statement: 'the agent may marry etc.'; its form is that he says: 'Bear witness that I have married so-and-so to myself.' And what is meant is the agent whom the woman authorized to marry her to himself; even if she authorized him to marry her to a man, he may not marry her himself because the definite does not enter into the indefinite. Zufar said: it is not permissible in both cases. And in one of al-Shafi'i's two opinions, if he is her guardian, it is permissible; if he is an agent, it is not.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning agency in marriage. It first addresses the cousin's marriage to his female cousin (where he is the guardian). The Hanafi position, supported by the text, is that this is valid because the cousin acts as a representative (safir) from both sides, thus no separate acceptance is needed. Shafi'i and Zufar argue that one person cannot be both the one who gives in marriage and the one who receives (tamlik). The Hanafi response is that he is a messenger, not a principal. Next, the text discusses an agent authorized by a woman to marry her to himself: this is valid if the authorization is specific (definite). If she authorized him to marry her to someone else (indefinite), he cannot marry her himself. Zufar rejects both, while Shafi'i distinguishes between guardian and agent. The Hanafi school follows the ruling that such self-marriage is valid when properly authorized.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent authorized to contract marriage on behalf of another; here, specifically for self-marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a woman says to a man, 'I appoint you as my agent to marry me to yourself,' the marriage is:
A) Invalid because one cannot be both agent and spouse.
B) Valid if he says 'I marry you to myself' in the presence of witnesses.
C) Valid only if her guardian also consents.
D) Invalid because it requires a separate acceptance from her.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates self-marriage by a guardian or agent when the authorization is specific, based on the concept of the representative as a messenger (safir).

Slave and Fuduli Marriage: Suspended or Void?
Rulings on suspended marriage contracts for slaves and unauthorized third parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that slave and fuduli marriages are suspended (mawquf) and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a marriage contracted without proper authority is suspended, not void — awaiting approval.

This passage addresses two cases where a marriage contract lacks immediate authorization: a slave marrying without the master's permission, and a stranger (fuduli) marrying parties without their consent. The Hanafi school holds both contracts as suspended (mawquf) — neither valid nor void until approval is given. This view is contrasted with the Shafi'i position that such contracts are void ab initio and the Maliki view that a slave's marriage is valid outright.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on slave marriage
Identify the ruling: if a slave or slave-woman marries without the master's permission, the marriage is suspended on the master's approval. The master's permission is a condition that can be supplied later.
This applies to all categories: umm walad, mukatab, mudabbar, etc.
2
Identify the opposing views on slave marriage
Malik considers it valid automatically; some Hanafis (author of al-Majma') consider it void based on the hadith 'Any slave who marries without his master's permission is a fornicator.'
The author of this text prefers the suspended view, calling it 'ahsan' (better).
3
State the Hanafi position on fuduli marriage
A fuduli (unauthorized third party) who marries a man to a woman without their permission also creates a suspended marriage. Approval from the parties makes it valid.
Fuduli is defined as one who is neither an agent nor a guardian.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i position and Hanafi response
Shafi'i argues that such contracts are void for lack of authority (wilaya). Hanafi responds that the contract is from qualified persons and can be completed by subsequent approval, analogous to a sale with an option.
The hadith of the woman approving her father's action is cited as evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi, if approval is given, the marriage is valid retroactively. In Shafi'i, the contract is void and must be re-contracted. In Maliki for slaves, it is valid without any need for approval.
The practical consequence affects the legal status of marriages and children.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأمة ولو أم ولد ومثلها المكاتبة والمستسعاة والمدبرة والمبعضة. (ط) موقوف : أي إذا تزوج العبد أو الأمة بغير إذن مولاهما فنكاحهما موقوف إن أجازه المولى جاز وإن رده المولى بطل، وكذا نكاح المكاتب والمدبر وأم الولد، قال مالك: يصح نكاح العبد بغير إذن المولى، وقال صاحب "المجمع" لا يصح نكاح العبد والأمة؛ لقوله علية: "أيما عبد تزوج بغير إذن مولاه فهو عاهر"، رواه أبو داود والترمذي وعبارة المصنف أحسن: لأن عدم جواز نكاح هؤلاء لحق المولى، فإذا رضي فقد جاز. رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] (مستخلص) كنكاح الفضولي [صفة لمصدر محذوف تقديره: موقوف وقفا وقف نكاح الفضولي. (ع)] "الفضولي" بضم الفاء، في اللغة: من يشتغل بما لا يعنيه منسوب إلى الفضول جمع فضل بمعنى الزيادة المطلقة، وقد غلب الجمع على ما لا خير فيه، وفي عرف الفقهاء من ليس بوكيل ولا رسول ومعناه كما يتوقف نكاح الفضولي، فإنه إذا زوج رجلاً بغير إذنه أو امرأة بغير إذنها ينعقد موقوفاً، فإن أجازه جاز، وإلا بطل، وهو قول مالك وأهل المدينة والحسن وسعيد ابن المسيب والنخعي، غير أن مالكاً جعل التفرقة طلاقاً، وهذا يدل على نفوذه من غير لزوم. وقال الشافعي: نكاح الفضولي باطل؛ لعدم الولاية؛ لأن المباشر لا يقدر على إثبات الحكم – وهو الملك فيلغو؛ لعدم الفائدة، ولنا ما روي أنه عليها جعل أمر المرأة التي زوجها أبوها بغير إذنها إليها، فقالت: قد أجزت صنع أبي إنما أردت لأعلم هل للنساء من الأمر شيء؟ وأجاز نكاح امرأة زوجتها أمها؛ ولأن العقد صدر من أهله مضافاً إلى محله ولا ضرر في انعقاده فوجب القول بانعقاده حتى إن رأى المصلحة أجازه، وقد يتراخى حكم العقد عنه كالبيع بشرط الخيار فيتم صونا لكلام المتعاقدين، ويتوقف حكمه دفعاً للضرر عنه، وبه قال أحمد في رواية. (عيني وفتح)
And the slave-woman, even if umm walad, and similar are the mukatabah, mustas'ah, mudabbarah, and muba''adah. (It is) suspended: i.e., if a male slave or female slave marries without the permission of their master, their marriage is suspended; if the master permits it, it is valid; if he rejects it, it is void. Likewise the marriage of a mukatab, mudabbar, and umm walad. Malik said: the marriage of a slave without the master's permission is valid. The author of al-Majma' said: the marriage of a male slave and female slave is not valid because of his statement: 'Any slave who marries without his master's permission is a fornicator.' The author's expression is better: because the prohibition of their marriage is due to the master's right; so if he is pleased, it is permitted. Like the fuduli marriage. 'Al-fuduli' (with damma on the fa') in language is one who busies himself with what does not concern him; in the terminology of jurists, it is one who is neither an agent nor a messenger. Its meaning is that the fuduli marriage is suspended: if he marries a man without his permission or a woman without her permission, it is contracted suspended; if they approve, it is valid; otherwise it is void. This is the view of Malik and the people of Medina. Al-Shafi'i said: the fuduli marriage is void due to lack of authority. Our proof: the hadith that the Prophet left the matter to the woman whose father married her without her permission, and she said 'I approve'; and because the contract emanated from one who is qualified and added to its proper place, so it should be considered valid pending approval.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage addresses two related topics: the marriage of slaves without the master's permission, and the fuduli marriage (by a third party without authorization). For slaves, the Hanafi view is that the marriage is suspended (mawquf) on the master's approval, because the right of the master is involved. This is opposed to Malik who holds it valid outright, and some Hanafis who quote a hadith that such a slave is a fornicator. The author prefers the suspended view. For the fuduli marriage, the Hanafi position (and that of Malik) is that it is also suspended, pending approval of the parties. Shafi'i argues it is absolutely void. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith of the woman whose father married her without consent, and the principle that a contract from a qualified person added to its proper place should be given effect, similar to a sale with an option. The passage concludes with a note that Ahmad also holds the suspended view in one narration.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): A person who contracts on behalf of another without any authorization (not an agent or guardian).
موقوف (mawquf): A contract that is neither valid nor invalid, but its final status depends on subsequent approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a stranger (fuduli) marries a woman to a man without either party's authorization, the marriage is:
A) Void ab initio.
B) Valid if the parties are compatible.
C) Suspended (mawquf) pending their approval.
D) Valid only if the stranger is a relative.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, slave and fuduli marriages are suspended (mawquf), not void, because the missing authority can be supplied by subsequent approval.

Marriage of an Absent Party: Void or Suspended?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on absent-party marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage of absent parties, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad from Abu Yusuf, and apply the principle that shatr al-‘aqd must occur in the same council.

Core Idea
A marriage contract for an absent party is void unless acceptance occurs in the same council – the contract cannot be suspended beyond the majlis.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a marriage contract made for two absent individuals without their command. The central question is whether such a contract is absolutely void (batil) or merely suspended (mawquf) pending their subsequent approval. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of the essential requirement that offer and acceptance be connected in the same session (majlis).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and default ruling
The passage describes a person who declares, 'Bear witness that I have married so-and-so to so-and-so' while both parties are absent and without their permission. Determine the initial ruling stated.
The text begins with 'هذا باطل' (this is void), indicating the default position.
2
Locate the basis for the ruling
The reason given is that acceptance (qabul) is 'shatr al-‘aqd' (a part of the contract) and cannot be postponed beyond the council. Identify the principle: offer and acceptance must occur in the same sitting.
The text: 'لأنه شطر العقد، وهو لا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس'.
3
Identify the dissenting view and its analogy
Abu Yusuf holds that the contract is suspended (mawquf) on the parties' subsequent approval. He analogizes to cases where one person can act for both sides, e.g., a grandfather marrying grandchildren or a cousin marrying his minor cousin. Understand the analogy.
The text: 'وقال أبو يوسف: ينعقد موقوفاً على إجازتهما؛ لأن الواحد يصلح عاقداً من الجانبين'.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference: Under the majority view, if acceptance does not occur in the council, the contract is void ab initio and cannot be revived later. Under Abu Yusuf's view, it can be validated if the absent parties later approve.
This affects whether a new contract is needed or just approval.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text says 'هذا عند الطرفين' (this is according to the two sides), indicating that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree, and their view is the relied-upon position in the school. Abu Yusuf's view is not taken for fatwa.
Mufta bihi: void (batil) unless acceptance in the same council.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ناكح غائب صورته أن يقول: اشهدوا أني زوجت فلانة من فلان وهما غائبان بغير أمرهما، فهذا باطل لا ينعقد إلا أن يقبل أحدهما في المجلس؛ لأنه شطر العقد، وهو لا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس وهذا عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: ينعقد موقوفاً على إجازتهما؛ لأن الواحد يصلح عاقداً من الجانبين، والأصل فيه أن الواحد يصلح وكيلاً من الجانبين أو ولياً من الجانبين كالجد يزوج ابن ابنه ببنت ابنه الآخر بعد موتهما أو جنونهما، أو أصيلا من وولياً من جانب كابن العم يتزوج بنت عمه الصغيرة، أو وكيلاً من جانب وأصيلاً من جانب كما لو وكلت جانب
Marriage of an absent party: its form is that he says, 'Bear witness that I have married so-and-so to so-and-so' while both are absent without their command. This is void and does not contract unless one of them accepts in the council, because it is part of the contract and it does not suspend on what is beyond the council. This is according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: it contracts suspended on their approval, because one person can serve as contractor from both sides, and the principle is that one person can serve as agent from both sides or guardian from both sides, like the grandfather marrying his son's son to his other son's daughter after their death or insanity, or as a principal and guardian from one side like the cousin marrying his minor female cousin, or as agent from one side and principal from the other as if one side appoints an agent.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a marriage contract made for two absent parties without their authorization. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that such a contract is absolutely void (batil) unless one of the parties accepts in the same council, because the declaration (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) must be linked in the same session. The acceptance cannot be postponed beyond the council. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the contract is suspended (mawquf) on their subsequent approval, analogizing it to cases where one person can act for both sides (e.g., a grandfather marrying grandchildren, or a cousin marrying his minor female cousin). The text leans toward the view that a single person can act in multiple capacities, but the majority view (the 'two sides') is that the contract is void if no acceptance occurs in the council.

Key Terms
شطر العقد (shatr al-'aqd): A part of the contract, here specifically the acceptance (qabul) which must occur in the same session as the offer.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is not immediately binding but can be validated by subsequent approval.
باطل (batil): Void ab initio; has no legal effect and cannot be rectified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a man says 'I marry my daughter to Zayd' while Zayd is absent and unaware, the marriage is:
A) Valid if Zayd later accepts.
B) Suspended on Zayd's approval.
C) Void unless Zayd accepts in the same council.
D) Valid immediately because the father has authority.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a marriage contract for an absent party is void unless acceptance occurs in the same council; delayed approval cannot cure the defect.

Agent Marrying His Principal: The Definite vs. Indefinite
Ruling and dispute on marriage agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid scenarios when a woman's agent marries her to himself, applying the Hanafi linguistic principle of definite vs. indefinite.

Core Idea
An agent cannot marry his principal if she appointed him for an indefinite man; the definite is not included in the indefinite.

This passage addresses a critical point in marriage agency: can a woman's agent marry her to himself? The answer depends on the wording of her appointment. The Hanafi school relies on a linguistic principle to draw the line, while other scholars differ. Let's explore the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The agent is appointed either (a) specifically to marry her to himself, or (b) generally to marry her to 'a man'. Note the difference in wording.
2
Apply the linguistic principle
In scenario (b), the request is indefinite ('a man'), which does not include the specific agent. So he cannot marry her.
Principle: al-ma'rifah la yadkhulu fi al-nakirah.
3
Contrast with scenario (a)
If she says 'marry me to yourself', the agent is definite and the marriage is valid.
4
Consider the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar holds it invalid in both cases, possibly to avoid conflict of interest.
Zufar's view is contrary to the mainstream Hanafi position.
5
Note the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i distinguishes guardian vs. agent; a guardian may marry his ward to himself, but a mere agent cannot.
This is one of two opinions from al-Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشهدوا أني زوجت فلانة من نفسي. والمراد من الوكيل الذي وكلته المرأة أن يزوجها من نفسه حتى لو وكلته أن يزوجها من رجل لم يجز له أن يتزوجها؛ لأن المعرفة لا يدخل في النكرة، وقال زفر: لا يجوز فيهما، وفي أحد قولي الشافعي إن كان وليا لها يجوز وإن كان وكيلا لا. (مسكين، مستخلص)
Bear witness that I have married so-and-so to myself. And the meaning is: the agent whom the woman appointed to marry her to himself, so if she appointed him to marry her to a man, it is not permissible for him to marry her, because the definite does not enter into the indefinite. Zufar said: It is not valid in either case. And in one of al-Shafi'i's two opinions: if he is her guardian it is valid, but if he is an agent it is not.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage concerns the legal capacity of an agent in a marriage contract. The text first presents the formula 'I have married so-and-so to myself' which applies when the agent himself is the groom. The ruling is: if a woman specifically appoints an agent to marry her to himself (saying 'marry me to yourself'), it is valid because the agent is definite and known. However, if she appoints him to marry her to a man (indefinite), he cannot marry her to himself because the definite is not included in the indefinite—a linguistic principle. Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, holds that it is invalid in both cases. Imam al-Shafi'i has two opinions: (1) if the agent is also her guardian (wali), it is valid; (2) if he is merely an agent (wakil), it is not. The relied-upon Hanafi position is the one given in the text: the agent may marry her to himself only when she specifically appoints him to himself.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): A person appointed by another (the principal) to act on their behalf, here specifically in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman tells her agent, 'Marry me to a man', can the agent marry her to himself according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because he is a man
B) No, because the definite (the agent) is not included in the indefinite (a man)
C) Yes, with her permission
D) No, unless he is her guardian

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists on explicit appointment: a general request to marry 'a man' does not allow the agent to become the groom.

Slave Marriage Without Permission Is Suspended
Ruling on the validity of slave marriage without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's marriage without permission, explain the hadith proof, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Imam Malik and the author of al-Mujma'.

Core Idea
A slave's marriage without master's permission is not void but suspended (muquf) – valid if master ratifies, void if he rejects.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical issue in slave marriage: what happens when a slave marries without the master's consent? The Hanafi school classifies such a marriage as 'muquf' (suspended), meaning it is valid in itself but dependent on the master's approval. The author explains the ruling, applies it to various categories of slaves, and defends it against opposing views using the hadith and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the first part of the passage to determine the legal status of a slave's marriage without permission. Note that the ruling applies to both male and female slaves, and extends to specific categories: umm walad, mukatabah, mustas'ah, mudabbara, muba'ada, and the corresponding male forms.
The ruling is 'muquf' (suspended).
2
Classify the ruling as muquf
Understand that 'muquf' means the contract is valid (sahih) but its legal effects are contingent on ratification by the master. This is distinct from batil (void) or fasid (irregular).
If the master permits, the marriage is valid; if he rejects, it becomes void.
3
Locate the hadith proof
Find the hadith cited by the author of al-Mujma': 'Any male slave who marries without the permission of his master is a fornicator.' This hadith is used to argue that the marriage is invalid.
The Hanafi response is that the prohibition is due to the master's right, which can be waived.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to opposing views
Examine the text's preference for the wording of the author of Kanz: the non-permissibility is because of the master's right, so if he agrees, it becomes permissible. This reconciles the hadith with the concept of suspension.
Imam Malik holds the marriage valid outright, while al-Mujma' holds it invalid. The Hanafi position mediates.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position is that the marriage is suspended, as stated by the author of Kanz and supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأمة ولو أم ولد ومثلها المكاتبة والمستسعاة والمدبرة والمبعضة. (ط) موقوف : أي إذا تزوج العبد أو الأمة بغير إذن مولاهما فنكاحهما موقوف إن أجازه المولى جاز وإن رده المولى بطل، وكذا نكاح المكاتب والمدبر وأم الولد، قال مالك: يصح نكاح العبد بغير إذن المولى، وقال صاحب "المجمع" لا يصح نكاح العبد والأمة؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "أيما عبد تزوج بغير إذن مولاه فهو عاهر"، رواه أبو داود والترمذي وعبارة المصنف أحسن: لأن عدم جواز نكاح هؤلاء لحق المولى، فإذا رضي فقد جاز. رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] (مستخلص)
And the slave woman, even if she is an umm walad, and like her is the mukatabah, the mustas'ah, the mudabbara, and the muba'ada. (T) Suspended: meaning that if a male slave or a female slave marries without the permission of their master, their marriage is suspended: if the master permits it, it is valid; if the master rejects it, it is void. Likewise the marriage of the mukatab, the mudabbar, and the umm walad. Malik said: The marriage of a male slave without the master's permission is valid. And the author of al-Mujma' said: The marriage of a male slave and a slave woman is not valid, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Any male slave who marries without the permission of his master is a fornicator' – reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. And the wording of the author [of Kanz] is better because the non-permissibility of the marriage of these individuals is due to the right of the master; so if he is pleased, it is valid.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage deals with the marriage of slaves and similar categories. The text classifies the marriage as 'muquf' (suspended) when a slave or slave woman marries without the master's permission. This means the contract is valid but contingent on the master's ratification. If the master permits, it is valid; if he rejects, it becomes void. This ruling also applies to the mukatab (a slave contracted for manumission), the mudabbar (a slave whose manumission is deferred until the master's death), and the umm walad (a slave woman who has borne her master's child). Imam Malik holds that such a marriage is valid outright without the need for permission. The text refutes the view of the author of al-Mujma' (a Hanafi scholar) who cites the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) declaring the slave's marriage without permission to be fornication. The text prefers the wording of the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, as it explains that the prohibition is due to the master's right, which can be waived by his consent, making the marriage valid upon ratification.

Key Terms
موقوف (muquf): A contract that is valid in itself but whose legal effect is suspended upon the approval of a third party (here the master).
أمة (amah): Female slave.
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave under a contract of manumission (kitabah) – she will be freed upon paying agreed installments.
مدبرة (mudabbara): A female slave whose manumission is deferred until the master's death (tadbir).
مستسعاة (mustas'ah): A female slave permitted to work and earn money to purchase her freedom.
مبعضة (muba'ada): A female slave who is partially free and partially slave.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne her master's child; she becomes free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the effect of the master's explicit rejection of a slave's marriage contracted without permission?
A) The marriage becomes fasid (irregular) and needs renewal
B) The marriage becomes void (batil)
C) The marriage remains suspended indefinitely
D) The marriage is automatically valid after a waiting period

Key Takeaway
A slave's marriage without permission is suspended, not void; it becomes valid upon master's ratification, and void upon his rejection.

Marriage by an Unauthorized Person (Fuduli) Is Suspended
Ruling on the nikah of a fuduli (unauthorized third party)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the marriage of a fuduli and explain why it is muquf, contrasting it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A marriage by a fuduli is valid upon ratification — the contract is suspended, not void.

We now examine a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding marriage contracts. The Hanafi school, supported by hadith and analogy, holds that a marriage conducted by an unauthorized third party (fuduli) is not automatically void but is suspended, awaiting the ratification of the person whose permission was lacking. This ruling balances the validity of the contract with the protection of the parties' interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Recognize that the act is marriage (nikah) performed by a fuduli (person without authority). The dispute is whether such a contract is void (batil) or valid but suspended (muquf).
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school rules that the marriage is muquf — contracted but dependent on ratification. The primary proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a woman the choice to ratify her father's marriage contract for her. Analogically, it is like a sale with an option for the seller.
The dalil is a marfu' hadith; its transmission is zanni but its meaning is clear.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Al-Shafi'i rules that the marriage is batil (void) because the fuduli lacks wilayah (guardianship) and cannot establish ownership. The contract is futile due to lack of benefit.
For Shafi'is, the person who lacks authority cannot validly contract marriage on behalf of another.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the contract is from qualified individuals (husband and wife) and is connected to its proper place. There is no harm in its conclusion, so it must be considered valid but suspended to protect the parties from harm until ratification.
The analogy with a sale with option further supports delaying the effect of the contract.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: under Hanafi, ratification makes the marriage valid from the start; under Shafi'i, a new contract must be concluded. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view that the marriage is muquf.
The text explicitly adopts the Hanafi position with supporting evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كنكاح الفضولي [صفة لمصدر محذوف تقديره: موقوف وقفا وقف نكاح الفضولي. (ع)] "الفضولي" بضم الفاء، في اللغة: من يشتغل بما لا يعنيه منسوب إلى الفضول جمع فضل بمعنى الزيادة المطلقة، وقد غلب الجمع على ما لا خير فيه، وفي عرف الفقهاء من ليس بوكيل ولا رسول ومعناه كما يتوقف نكاح الفضولي، فإنه إذا زوج رجلاً بغير إذنه أو امرأة بغير إذنها ينعقد موقوفاً، فإن أجازه جاز، وإلا بطل، وهو قول مالك وأهل المدينة والحسن وسعيد ابن المسيب والنخعي، غير أن مالكاً جعل التفرقة طلاقاً، وهذا يدل على نفوذه من غير لزوم. ما وقال الشافعي: نكاح الفضولي باطل؛ لعدم الولاية؛ لأن المباشر لا يقدر على إثبات الحكم – وهو الملك فيلغو؛ لعدم الفائدة، ولنا ما روي أنه عليها جعل أمر المرأة التي زوجها أبوها بغير إذنها إليها، فقالت: قد أجزت صنع أبي إنما أردت لأعلم هل للنساء من الأمر شيء؟ وأجاز نكاح امرأة زوجتها أمها؛ ولأن العقد صدر من أهله مضافاً إلى محله ولا ضرر في انعقاده فوجب القول بانعقاده حتى إن رأى المصلحة أجازه، وقد يتراخى حكم العقد عنه كالبيع بشرط الخيار فيتم صونا لكلام المتعاقدين، ويتوقف حكمه دفعاً للضرر عنه، وبه قال أحمد في رواية. (عيني وفتح)
Like the marriage of the fuduli (unauthorized person). [Attribute for an omitted source, its estimation: suspended like the suspension of the marriage of the fuduli.] 'Al-fuduli' with a damma on the fa: in language, one who busies himself with what does not concern him, attributed to al-fudul, plural of fadl meaning absolute excess. In the custom of jurists, it is one who is neither an agent nor a messenger. Its meaning: as the marriage of the fuduli is suspended, for if he marries a man without his permission or a woman without her permission, it is contracted as suspended; if he permits it, it is valid, otherwise it is void. This is the statement of Malik and the people of Madinah, al-Hasan, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, and al-Nakha'i, except that Malik made separation [by the husband or wife?] a divorce, which indicates its effectiveness without binding. (Then) al-Shafi'i said: The marriage of the fuduli is void, because of lack of guardianship; because the direct agent cannot establish the ruling – which is ownership – so it is meaningless, because of lack of benefit. And our proof is what was narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) referred the matter of the woman whose father married her without her permission to her, and she said: 'I have approved the action of my father; I only wanted to know whether women have any say in the matter.' And he validated the marriage of a woman whose mother married her. And because the contract originated from one who is qualified (the husband and wife) and is connected to its place, and there is no harm in its conclusion, so it must be considered valid, so that if he sees the benefit he can ratify it. And the ruling of the contract may be delayed from it, like a sale with a condition of option, so it is completed to protect the speech of the contracting parties, and its ruling is suspended to prevent harm. And Ahmad [ibn Hanbal] said so in one narration.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage discusses the nikah of a fuduli, a person who acts as a marriage contractor without having any authority (neither as a wakil nor a wali). The text first defines 'fuduli' linguistically and technically. The Hanafi ruling, which is also held by Malik and many Madinan scholars, is that such a marriage is 'muquf' (suspended): it is contracted but its validity depends on the ratification of the party (the man or the woman) on whose behalf the fuduli acted. If the party ratifies, it is valid; otherwise, void. Imam Malik adds that if the married couple separate, it counts as a divorce, indicating the marriage was effective. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, rules that the marriage is completely void (batil) because the fuduli has no legal authority (wilayah) to conclude a valid marriage contract; the contract is futile since it lacks a necessary condition. The Hanafi response is based on a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a woman whose father had married her without her consent the choice to ratify or reject, and she ratified it. Additionally, a marriage contracted by a mother was approved. The Hanafi reasoning is that a marriage contract emanates from those who are capable of it (the husband and wife) and is directed at its proper subject matter; there is no harm in its conclusion, so it should be considered valid but suspended to protect the parties from harm until ratification. This is analogous to a sale with an option for the seller, where the contract is valid but the transfer of ownership is delayed.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): One who acts as a marriage contractor without any authority (wakil or wali) from the parties.
موقوف (muquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid in itself but its legal effect is conditioned on ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a marriage conducted by a fuduli (person without authority)?
A) It is void (batil) from the start.
B) It is suspended (muquf) pending ratification.
C) It is valid only if the fuduli is also a guardian.
D) It is valid if the parties are present and consent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a marriage by an unauthorized person (fuduli) is suspended (muquf) and becomes valid upon ratification of the concerned party.

Marriage of a Missing Spouse and One-Person-Acting-for-Both
Ruling on a marriage contract made by one person for two absent parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one person contracts marriage for two absent parties without authorization, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A marriage contract requires both offer and acceptance in the same sitting; one person acting for both absent parties without authorization renders it void.

This passage examines a contested case in Hanafi marriage law: when a single individual attempts to contract a marriage for two absent parties who have not authorized him. The ruling hinges on whether the contract is considered 'half' (shart) or a complete but suspended act. Understanding the positions of the early Hanafi imams helps clarify the importance of mutual consent and presence in contract formation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and disputing parties
Read the passage to identify the specific case: one person says 'I marry so-and-so to so-and-so' while both spouses are absent without their command. Note that the three main Hanafi imams are involved: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
The absence is critical; the person is a fuduli (unauthorized).
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to the majority (al-tarafayn), the marriage is void (batil) because the contract is only half (offer) and acceptance must occur in the same sitting. Since the absent parties cannot accept in the majlis, the contract fails.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the contract is valid but suspended (muquf) upon the subsequent ratification of the parties. He argues that one person can legally act for both sides, citing various valid cases (e.g., grandfather marrying grandchildren).
Thamarah: under Abu Yusuf, ratification can perfect the marriage; under the majority, a new contract is required.
4
Examine the agreed cases (ittifaq)
The passage lists several scenarios where the three imams agree that a single person can validly act for both sides: grandfather as guardian, cousin as guardian, agent-principal combinations. These involve proper authority (guardianship or agency), not fuduli.
Distinguish these from the contested case: authority matters.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: under the majority view, the marriage is void ab initio; under Abu Yusuf, it can be cured by ratification. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because it aligns with the requirement of acceptance in the sitting.
Zufar and Shafi'i reject a single person's utterance entirely, except for the grandfather's necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ناكح غائب صورته أن يقول: اشهدوا أني زوجت فلانة من فلان وهما غائبان بغير أمرهما، فهذا باطل لا ينعقد إلا أن يقبل أحدهما في المجلس؛ لأنه شطر العقد، وهو لا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس وهذا عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: ينعقد موقوفاً على إجازتهما؛ لأن الواحد يصلح عاقداً من الجانبين، والأصل فيه أن الواحد يصلح وكيلاً من الجانبين أو ولياً من الجانبين كالجد يزوج ابن ابنه ببنت ابنه الآخر بعد موتهما أو جنونهما، أو أصيلا من . وولياً من جانب كابن العم يتزوج بنت عمه الصغيرة، أو وكيلاً من جانب وأصيلاً من جانب كما لو وكلت رجلا أن يزوجها من نفسه، أو ولياً من جانب وكيلاً من جانب كابن العم يتزوج بنت عمه الكبير ممن وكله بالنكاح، وهذه الصور تجوز باتفاق أصحابنا الثلاثة، ولو كان الواحد فضولياً من الجانبين أو من أحدهما بطل عند الطرفين، ويتوقف عند الثاني، وعند زفر : لا يجوز النكاح بعبارة الواحد أصلاً وكذا عند الشافعي إلا إذا كان فيه ضرورة مثل الجد، فإنه يزوج ابن ابنه من بنت ابنه؛ لأنه لا يوجد أحد في درجته حتى يزوجها. والحاصل أن نكاح الفضولي عقد تام عند أبي يوسف فيتوقف؛ لأنه يصح أن يتولى الطرفين، وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد هذا النكاح شطر فيبطل. (فتح)
The case of a missing spouse (gha'ib): its form is that he says: 'Bear witness that I have married so-and-so to so-and-so' while both are absent without their command. This is void and does not contract unless one of them accepts in the sitting, because it is a half of the contract, and it does not depend on what is beyond the sitting. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: It is contracted as suspended upon their ratification, because a single person is fit to act as a contracting party from both sides. The principle is that a single person is fit to act as agent from both sides or guardian from both sides, like the grandfather marrying his son's son (grandson) to his other son's daughter after their death or insanity, or as a principal from one side and guardian from the other, like the cousin marrying his minor cousin (daughter of his uncle), or as agent from one side and principal from the other, as if a woman appointed a man to marry her to himself, or as guardian from one side and agent from the other, like the cousin marrying his adult cousin (daughter of his uncle) to the one who appointed him as agent for marriage. These cases are valid by agreement of our three imams. But if a single person is a fuduli (unauthorized) from both sides or from one side, it is void according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and suspended according to the second (Abu Yusuf). According to Zufar: the marriage by the statement of a single person is not valid at all, and likewise according to al-Shafi'i except if there is a necessity like the grandfather, for he marries his son's son to his son's daughter because there is no one in his grade to marry her. The conclusion: the marriage of a fuduli is a complete contract according to Abu Yusuf, so it is suspended; because he can properly handle both sides. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this marriage is half (shart) so it is void.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in marriage agency: a single person pronounces the marriage contract for two absent parties, saying 'I marry so-and-so to so-and-so' without their prior authorization. According to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, such a contract is void (batil) because it represents only one half of the contract (the offer), and acceptance must occur in the same sitting (majlis). Since the counterpart is absent, acceptance cannot be verified, rendering the contract invalid. Abu Yusuf, however, considers the contract valid but suspended (muquf) pending the ratification of the two parties. He argues that a single person can legally act for both sides of a contract in many situations, such as when a grandfather marries his grandchildren in certain circumstances, or when a cousin marries his minor cousin under guardianship. The three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) agree on the validity of those specific cases where the person acts with proper authority (as a guardian or agent). However, in the present case where the person is a fuduli (without authority) from both sides, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule it void, while Abu Yusuf maintains it is suspended. Zufar and al-Shafi'i go further and reject the validity of a marriage by a single person's utterance entirely, except in cases of necessity like the grandfather.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A missing person; here refers to a spouse who is not present at the marriage contract session.
شطر العقد (shatra al-'aqd): Half of the contract; the offer alone without corresponding acceptance is only half the contract.
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of others without their permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling if a single person says 'I marry so-and-so to so-and-so' while both are absent and have not authorized him?
A) The marriage is valid if the parties later accept
B) The marriage is void unless one of them accepts in the same sitting
C) The marriage is suspended pending ratification
D) The marriage is valid only if the person is a guardian

Key Takeaway
A marriage contract requires acceptance in the same sitting; a single person acting without authorization for two absent parties cannot complete the contract, rendering it void according to the majority Hanafi view.

Agent Marrying Two Women or a Slave Woman of Another
Ruling on an agent who violates instructions by marrying two women or a slave woman of another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent marries his principal to two women in one contract or to a slave woman, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding kafa'ah.

Core Idea
An agent who marries two women in one contract invalidates both; marrying a slave woman is valid only if she is kufu' (suitable) according to the mufta bihi.

This passage discusses two scenarios where an agent violates his principal's instructions in a marriage contract. First, if the agent marries him to two women in a single contract, the marriage is invalid because it is impossible to execute both without specification. Second, if he marries him to a slave woman belonging to another person, there is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa considers it valid based on the literal wording, while his two disciples require that the slave woman be a suitable match (kufu'). The fatwa follows the stricter view of the two.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the violation
Determine what the agent was commanded to do (marry one woman) and how he violated it (married two women or a slave woman).
The principal said 'marry me a woman' – the agent must comply with the specification.
2
State the ruling for the two-women case
The contract is invalid because neither marriage binds; there is no way to execute both, specify one, or choose arbitrarily.
This ruling is by consensus of the three imams.
3
Analyze the slave woman case dispute
Abu Hanifa holds it valid (the absolute wording 'woman' includes a slave); the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require that the slave be kufu' (suitable) – otherwise invalid.
The principle: Abu Hanifa uses literal interpretation; the two give weight to custom ('urf) where 'woman' normally means a free woman.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text states 'wa bihi yufata' – the fatwa is given according to the two, requiring kafa'ah.
This is the relied-upon view for practical fatwa.
5
Apply to parallel cases
The same dispute applies if the agent marries a blind, amputee, or other defective woman; but marrying his own slave woman is invalid by consensus, while marrying his own sister is valid by agreement.
The presence of suspicion (tuhma) is the decisive factor in the consensus cases.

[رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] والحاصل أن نكاح الفضولي عقد تام عند أبي يوسف فيتوقف؛ لأنه : يصح أن يتولى الطرفين، وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد هذا النكاح شطر فيبطل. (فتح) بامرأتين لا بأمة : أي من أمر رجلاً أن : يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقد واحد لم يلزم المؤكل نكاح واحدة منهما؛ لأنه لا وجه في تنفيذ نكاحهما معاً للمخالفة، ولا إلى تنفيذ إحداهما غير معينة، فتحقق الجهالة، ولا ) إلى التعيين أيضاً؛ لعدم الأولوية فتعين التفريق، وإن زوجه أمة لغيره جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: لا يجوز إلا أن كفؤاً، وبه يفتى، والأصل أن إطلاق اللفظ معتبر عنده في باب الوكالة وعندهما: المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل المعتاد، وقيدنا بـ "أمة الغير"؛ لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه لا يجوز إجماعاً؛ لتمكن التهمة، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا زوجه عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، ولو زوجه أمته الكبيرة لا يجوز عنده، خلافاً لهما، ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة جاز بالاتفاق؛ لعدم التهمة. (عيني، مستخلص) يزوجه لا بأمة: أي لا يكون مخالفا للأمر بتزويجه إياه بأمة غيره ولو مكاتبته أو أم ولده. (ط) وجه
And the one who is commanded to marry a woman: if he violates by marrying two women, not a slave woman. If unspecified: a man that she appoints to marry her from himself, or guardian from one side and agent from the other, like the cousin marrying his adult cousin (daughter of his uncle) to the one who appointed him as agent for marriage – these cases are valid by agreement of our three imams. But if the single person is a fuduli from both sides or from one side, it is void according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and suspended according to the second (Abu Yusuf). And according to Zufar: the marriage by the statement of a single person is not valid at all, and likewise according to al-Shafi'i except if there is a necessity like the grandfather. The conclusion: the marriage of a fuduli is a complete contract according to Abu Yusuf, so it is suspended; because he can properly handle both sides. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this marriage is half (shart) so it is void. (Fath) 'with two women, not a slave woman': meaning if a man is commanded to marry him a woman, and he marries him two women in one contract, neither marriage binds the principal, because there is no way to execute both marriages together due to the violation, nor to execute one of them unspecified because that would be ignorance (jihala), nor to specify one due to lack of priority, so dissolution is required. And if he marries him a slave woman belonging to another, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not valid unless she is suitable (kufu'). And this is the view given for fatwa. The principle is that the absolute wording is considered with him (Abu Hanifa) in the chapter of agency, while with the two, the absolute expression applies to the complete and customary. We restricted it to 'a slave woman of another' because if he marries him his own slave woman, it is not valid by consensus due to the possibility of suspicion (tuhma). Similarly, if he marries him a blind woman, or one with amputated hands, or a woman with a vaginal obstruction (ratqa'), or a paralyzed woman, or a lunatic – the same disagreement applies. And if he marries him his own mature slave woman, it is not valid according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to the two. And if he marries him his own mature sister, it is valid by agreement because there is no suspicion. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) 'He marries him not a slave woman': meaning he does not violate the order by marrying him a slave woman belonging to another, even if she is his mukataba or umm walad. (T) Wajh (aspect).
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage deals with an agent who violates the instructions of his principal in marriage. The initial part states: if a man is commanded to marry a woman (meaning find a wife for him), but he instead marries him two women in a single contract, the marriage does not bind the principal. The reason is that executing both together violates the instruction, executing one unspecified is ignorance, and specifying one has no priority, so the contract is invalid. Then the text addresses the case where the agent marries him a slave woman belonging to someone else (not the agent's own). According to Abu Hanifa, this is valid (if she is suitable), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, require that the slave woman be kufu' (a suitable match) for the principal, otherwise it is not valid. The fatwa is given according to the two (i.e., the stricter view). The principle behind the difference is that Abu Hanifa looks at the literal wording of the appointment (he was told to marry 'a woman', so a slave woman is also a woman), while the two consider custom: the absolute expression normally refers to a free and complete woman. The text then lists other defects like blindness, amputation, etc., where the same disagreement applies. It also clarifies that if the agent marries him his own slave woman, it is invalid by consensus due to the possibility of suspicion. However, if he marries him his own sister (free), it is valid by consensus because there is no such suspicion.

Key Terms
كفؤ (kufu'): Suitable match; the condition that the husband and wife be equal in social status, lineage, profession, and financial standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man appoints an agent to marry him a woman, and the agent marries him a slave woman belonging to another person, what is the fatwa (relied-upon) ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The marriage is valid regardless
B) The marriage is invalid because she is a slave
C) The marriage is valid only if the slave woman is suitable (kufu') for the man
D) The marriage is valid only if the agent is also the guardian

Key Takeaway
An agent who marries two women in one contract invalidates both; marrying a slave woman is only valid if she is suitable (kufu'), according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Agent Exceeding Mandate: Marrying Two Women Instead of One
Ruling on agent marrying two women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an agent marries two women instead of the commanded one, and explain why neither marriage is valid due to uncertainty (jahala).

Core Idea
If an agent marries two women in one contract contrary to command, both are invalid due to jahala.

In marriage agency, the agent must follow the mandate. If he violates it by marrying two women instead of one, uncertainty arises as to which one was intended. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that neither marriage is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mandate and violation
The principal commanded marriage to one woman. The agent married two in one contract. This is a clear violation of the mandate.
2
Recognize the resulting uncertainty
Since the agent married two, it is impossible to know which one the principal intended. There is no way to execute both together due to the violation, nor to choose one without preference. Thus, jahala (uncertainty) invalidates the contract.
3
Apply the ruling
The text states: 'لم يلزم المؤكل نكاح واحدة منهما' – neither marriage takes effect for the principal. The contract is invalid and must be redone properly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوكالة بالنكاح
والمأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالف بامرأتين لا بأمة. غير معينة رجلا أن يزوجها من نفسه، أو ولياً من جانب وكيلاً من جانب كابن العم يتزوج بنت عمه الكبير ممن وكله بالنكاح، وهذه الصور تجوز باتفاق أصحابنا الثلاثة، ولو كان الواحد فضولياً من الجانبين أو من أحدهما بطل عند الطرفين، ويتوقف عند الثاني، وعند زفر: لا يجوز النكاح بعبارة الواحد أصلاً وكذا عند الشافعي إلا إذا كان فيه ضرورة مثل الجد، فإنه يزوج ابن ابنه من بنت ابنه؛ لأنه لا يوجد أحد في درجته حتى يزوجها. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] والحاصل أن نكاح الفضولي عقد تام عند أبي يوسف فيتوقف؛ لأنه: يصح أن يتولى الطرفين، وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد هذا النكاح شطر فيبطل. (فتح) بامرأتين لا بأمة: أي من أمر رجلاً أن: يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقد واحد لم يلزم المؤكل نكاح واحدة منهما؛ لأنه لا وجه في تنفيذ نكاحهما معاً للمخالفة، ولا إلى تنفيذ إحداهما غير معينة، فتحقق الجهالة، ولا) إلى التعيين أيضاً؛ لعدم الأولوية فتعين التفريق، وإن زوجه أمة لغيره جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: لا يجوز إلا أن كفؤاً، وبه يفتى، والأصل أن إطلاق اللفظ معتبر عنده في باب الوكالة وعندهما: المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل المعتاد، وقيدنا بـ "أمة الغير"؛ لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه لا يجوز إجماعاً؛ لتمكن التهمة، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا زوجه عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، ولو زوجه أمته الكبيرة لا يجوز عنده، خلافاً لهما، ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة جاز بالاتفاق؛ لعدم التهمة. (عيني، مستخلص)
يزوجه لا بأمة: أي لا يكون مخالفا للأمر بتزويجه إياه بأمة غيره ولو مكاتبته أو أم ولده. (ط)
The chapter of agency in marriage. The one commanded to marry a woman who acts contrary (to the command) by (marrying) two women, not by a slave woman. (If he is commanded to marry) an unspecified woman, (he may) marry her from himself, or a guardian from one side and an agent from the other, like a paternal cousin marrying the daughter of his paternal uncle who is older (than the agent) from the one who appointed him as agent for marriage. These forms are permissible by agreement of our three imams. If one person acts as a fuduli (unauthorized) from both sides or from one side, it is invalid according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and suspended according to the second (Abu Yusuf). According to Zufar: marriage by the expression of one person is not permissible at all, and likewise according to al-Shafi'i except when there is necessity, like the grandfather, for he marries his son's son to his son's daughter, because there is no one at his level to marry her. The conclusion is that the marriage of a fuduli is a complete contract according to Abu Yusuf, so it is suspended, because it is valid for one to act for both parties. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this marriage is half (incomplete) so it is invalid. (Fath) "With two women, not with a slave woman" means: if a man commands a man to marry him a woman, and he marries him two women in one contract, the marriage of neither takes effect for the principal, because there is no way to execute both marriages together due to the violation (of the command), nor to execute one of them unspecified, so uncertainty (jahala) materializes, nor to specify one due to lack of preference, so separation is determined. If he marries him a slave woman belonging to another, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not permissible unless she is suitable, and according to this the fatwa is given. The principle is that the absolute wording is considered according to him in the chapter of agency, while according to them the absolute (wording) refers to the complete customary (person). We restricted to "a slave woman belonging to another" because if he marries him his own slave woman, it is not permissible by consensus, due to the possibility of suspicion. And on this disagreement (applies) if he marries him a blind woman, or a woman with hands cut off, or a raqra woman (with a vaginal obstruction), or a paralyzed woman, or a mad woman. If he marries him his older slave woman, it is not permissible according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them. If he marries him his older sister, it is permissible by agreement, due to the absence of suspicion. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) "He marries him, not with a slave woman" means: he is not contrary to the command by marrying him a slave woman of another, even if she is his kitaba woman or umm walad. (Taliq)
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with agency in marriage (al-wikala bi al-nikah). It begins by stating the general rule: if an agent is commanded to marry a specific woman but instead marries two women, his action is contrary to the mandate, and the marriage does not bind the principal. However, if he is commanded to marry an unspecified woman, he may marry her from himself (if he is a qualified guardian) or appoint a sub-agent. These scenarios are valid by consensus of the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad). The text then addresses the controversial case of a single person acting as both the agent for the groom and the guardian for the bride (fuduli). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, such a marriage is invalid because one person cannot represent both sides in a contract that requires two separate consenting parties; they consider it a 'half' contract (shattr). Abu Yusuf, however, views the fuduli's contract as complete but suspended (tawaqquf) pending approval of the parties, since it is possible for one person to validly act for both in some contracts. Zufar and al-Shafi'i prohibit it outright unless there is a necessity, like a grandfather who must marry his grandchildren together when no other guardian exists. The text then elaborates on the case of two women instead of one: since the agent was commanded to marry one woman, marrying two creates uncertainty (jahala) as to which one was intended, so neither marriage is binding. Next, it discusses marrying a slave woman belonging to another person: Abu Hanifa permits it unconditionally, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require that she be suitable (kuf') for the groom; the fatwa is according to the latter view. This difference stems from their principle regarding absolute wording: Abu Hanifa considers the literal command, while the Sahibayn consider what is complete and customary. The passage concludes with analogous cases (blind, disabled, mad women) and notes that marrying one's own slave woman is unanimously invalid due to suspicion (tuhma), but marrying one's adult sister is valid by consensus because there is no suspicion.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahāla): Uncertainty or ambiguity in a contract that renders it invalid if it affects a fundamental element.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a man commands an agent to marry him a woman, and the agent marries him two women in one contract, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is valid for both women.
B) The marriage is valid for the one the principal chooses.
C) Neither marriage is valid for the principal.
D) The agent must divorce one of them.

Key Takeaway
When an agent violates the mandate by marrying two women instead of one, both marriages are invalid due to jahala.

Fuduli Marriage: One Person Acting for Both Parties
Ruling on fuduli marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf on marriage by a fuduli (unauthorized person) acting for both parties, and compare it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A marriage by one person acting as both agent for groom and guardian for bride is batil (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad) or suspended (Abu Yusuf).

The case of a single person acting as both sides in a marriage contract without prior authorization is a classic point of ikhtilaf within and across madhhabs. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi positions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Define fuduli and the scenario
A fuduli is someone who acts without prior authorization. The scenario is one person acting as both agent for the groom and guardian for the bride (e.g., a paternal cousin marrying a cousin from both sides).
2
Identify the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the contract is batil (invalid) because it is a 'half' contract. Abu Yusuf says it is valid but suspended (tawaqquf) pending approval.
3
Compare with Zufar and al-Shafi'i
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that marriage by one person is invalid even if he has authority (except necessity like grandfather). They argue that a single person cannot perform both ijab and qabul.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad see the contract as shattr (half) because one person cannot represent two consenting parties. Abu Yusuf analogizes to other contracts where one person can act for both (e.g., sale). The Shafi'i view is based on the need for two distinct expressions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (batil) for caution, though Abu Yusuf's view has practical applications in some contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with agency in marriage (al-wikala bi al-nikah). Key Terms
فضولي (fudūlī): A person who acts in a contract without prior authorization from the principal.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension; the contract is not immediately binding but awaits ratification.
شطر (shattr): Half; refers to a contract that is incomplete because one person attempts to act for both parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on a marriage conducted by a single person acting as both agent for the groom and guardian for the bride without prior authorization, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?
A) Valid but suspended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a split on fuduli marriage: batil (majority) or tawaqquf (Abu Yusuf), reflecting a deeper ikhtilaf on representation in contracts.

Marrying a Slave Woman and Analogous Cases
Ruling on marrying a slave woman of another and analogous defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on an agent marrying a slave woman of another, and apply the principle of suitability (kafa'a) as required by the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
An agent marrying a slave woman of another is permissible unconditionally (Abu Hanifa) or only if she is suitable (Sahibayn); the mufta bihi is the latter view.

When an agent is commanded to marry a woman, marrying a slave woman belonging to another raises the question of whether suitability matters. This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute and its basis in principles of absolute vs. customary interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The principal commands the agent to marry him a woman (unspecified). The agent marries him a slave woman belonging to another person. Is this permissible?
2
Identify the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: permissible unconditionally (jaza). Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): permissible only if she is suitable (kuf') for the groom. The text says 'and according to this the fatwa is given' (wa bihi yufta).
3
Understand the underlying principle
Abu Hanifa considers the absolute wording of the command (absolute release). The Sahibayn hold that the absolute wording refers to the complete customary (al-kamil al-mu'tad), i.e., a free woman, so a slave is not automatically included unless suitable.
4
Apply to analogous cases
The same ikhtilaf applies to marrying a blind woman, a woman with hands cut off, a raqra woman, a paralyzed woman, or a mad woman. Abu Hanifa permits; Sahibayn require suitability.
5
Note exceptions
Marrying one's own slave woman is unanimously invalid due to suspicion (tuhma). Marrying one's adult sister is unanimously valid because no suspicion exists.
