⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوكالة بالنكاح
والمأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالف بامرأتين لا بأمة. غير معينة رجلا أن يزوجها من نفسه، أو ولياً من جانب وكيلاً من جانب كابن العم يتزوج بنت عمه الكبير ممن وكله بالنكاح، وهذه الصور تجوز باتفاق أصحابنا الثلاثة، ولو كان الواحد فضولياً من الجانبين أو من أحدهما بطل عند الطرفين، ويتوقف عند الثاني، وعند زفر: لا يجوز النكاح بعبارة الواحد أصلاً وكذا عند الشافعي إلا إذا كان فيه ضرورة مثل الجد، فإنه يزوج ابن ابنه من بنت ابنه؛ لأنه لا يوجد أحد في درجته حتى يزوجها. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٦/١] والحاصل أن نكاح الفضولي عقد تام عند أبي يوسف فيتوقف؛ لأنه: يصح أن يتولى الطرفين، وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد هذا النكاح شطر فيبطل. (فتح) بامرأتين لا بأمة: أي من أمر رجلاً أن: يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقد واحد لم يلزم المؤكل نكاح واحدة منهما؛ لأنه لا وجه في تنفيذ نكاحهما معاً للمخالفة، ولا إلى تنفيذ إحداهما غير معينة، فتحقق الجهالة، ولا) إلى التعيين أيضاً؛ لعدم الأولوية فتعين التفريق، وإن زوجه أمة لغيره جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: لا يجوز إلا أن كفؤاً، وبه يفتى، والأصل أن إطلاق اللفظ معتبر عنده في باب الوكالة وعندهما: المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل المعتاد، وقيدنا بـ "أمة الغير"؛ لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه لا يجوز إجماعاً؛ لتمكن التهمة، وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا زوجه عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، ولو زوجه أمته الكبيرة لا يجوز عنده، خلافاً لهما، ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة جاز بالاتفاق؛ لعدم التهمة. (عيني، مستخلص)
يزوجه لا بأمة: أي لا يكون مخالفا للأمر بتزويجه إياه بأمة غيره ولو مكاتبته أو أم ولده. (ط)
The chapter of agency in marriage. The one commanded to marry a woman who acts contrary (to the command) by (marrying) two women, not by a slave woman. (If he is commanded to marry) an unspecified woman, (he may) marry her from himself, or a guardian from one side and an agent from the other, like a paternal cousin marrying the daughter of his paternal uncle who is older (than the agent) from the one who appointed him as agent for marriage. These forms are permissible by agreement of our three imams. If one person acts as a fuduli (unauthorized) from both sides or from one side, it is invalid according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and suspended according to the second (Abu Yusuf). According to Zufar: marriage by the expression of one person is not permissible at all, and likewise according to al-Shafi'i except when there is necessity, like the grandfather, for he marries his son's son to his son's daughter, because there is no one at his level to marry her. The conclusion is that the marriage of a fuduli is a complete contract according to Abu Yusuf, so it is suspended, because it is valid for one to act for both parties. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this marriage is half (incomplete) so it is invalid. (Fath) "With two women, not with a slave woman" means: if a man commands a man to marry him a woman, and he marries him two women in one contract, the marriage of neither takes effect for the principal, because there is no way to execute both marriages together due to the violation (of the command), nor to execute one of them unspecified, so uncertainty (jahala) materializes, nor to specify one due to lack of preference, so separation is determined. If he marries him a slave woman belonging to another, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not permissible unless she is suitable, and according to this the fatwa is given. The principle is that the absolute wording is considered according to him in the chapter of agency, while according to them the absolute (wording) refers to the complete customary (person). We restricted to "a slave woman belonging to another" because if he marries him his own slave woman, it is not permissible by consensus, due to the possibility of suspicion. And on this disagreement (applies) if he marries him a blind woman, or a woman with hands cut off, or a raqra woman (with a vaginal obstruction), or a paralyzed woman, or a mad woman. If he marries him his older slave woman, it is not permissible according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them. If he marries him his older sister, it is permissible by agreement, due to the absence of suspicion. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) "He marries him, not with a slave woman" means: he is not contrary to the command by marrying him a slave woman of another, even if she is his kitaba woman or umm walad. (Taliq)
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with agency in marriage (al-wikala bi al-nikah). It begins by stating the general rule: if an agent is commanded to marry a specific woman but instead marries two women, his action is contrary to the mandate, and the marriage does not bind the principal. However, if he is commanded to marry an unspecified woman, he may marry her from himself (if he is a qualified guardian) or appoint a sub-agent. These scenarios are valid by consensus of the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad). The text then addresses the controversial case of a single person acting as both the agent for the groom and the guardian for the bride (fuduli). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, such a marriage is invalid because one person cannot represent both sides in a contract that requires two separate consenting parties; they consider it a 'half' contract (shattr). Abu Yusuf, however, views the fuduli's contract as complete but suspended (tawaqquf) pending approval of the parties, since it is possible for one person to validly act for both in some contracts. Zufar and al-Shafi'i prohibit it outright unless there is a necessity, like a grandfather who must marry his grandchildren together when no other guardian exists. The text then elaborates on the case of two women instead of one: since the agent was commanded to marry one woman, marrying two creates uncertainty (jahala) as to which one was intended, so neither marriage is binding. Next, it discusses marrying a slave woman belonging to another person: Abu Hanifa permits it unconditionally, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require that she be suitable (kuf') for the groom; the fatwa is according to the latter view. This difference stems from their principle regarding absolute wording: Abu Hanifa considers the literal command, while the Sahibayn consider what is complete and customary. The passage concludes with analogous cases (blind, disabled, mad women) and notes that marrying one's own slave woman is unanimously invalid due to suspicion (tuhma), but marrying one's adult sister is valid by consensus because there is no suspicion.

Key Terms
كفؤ (kuf'): Suitability or equality in marriage, considering factors like lineage, religion, wealth, and profession.
إطلاق اللفظ (itlaq al-lafz): The absolute wording of a command, taken at face value without restriction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the text, when can an agent validly marry a slave woman of another for his principal?
A) Always, regardless of condition.
B) Only if the slave woman is suitable (kuf').
C) Never, it is invalid.
D) Only if the principal explicitly agreed to a slave.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school requires suitability when an agent marries a slave woman of another, reflecting the Sahibayn's customary interpretation of absolute commands.

Minimum Mahr: Ten Dirhams and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on minimum mahr and refutation of opposing schools with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi minimum mahr, explain why mentioning mahr is not a condition for marriage validity, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The Hanafi minimum mahr is ten dirhams — legally estimated by the nisab of theft and supported by hadith and athar.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on the dower (mahr). While marriage is valid without mentioning any mahr, once it is due, a minimum of ten dirhams is required. The passage defends this position against other schools, using hadith evidence and a principle of legal estimation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Rulings
Note that marriage is valid without mentioning mahr, and the minimum mahr is ten dirhams of a specific weight.
These two points are the foundation of the Hanafi position.
2
Understand the Weight Specification
The ten dirhams are defined as seven mithqals (each dirham = 14 qirats). This applies to both minted and unminted silver.
This distinguishes it from the nisab of theft, which requires minted coins.
3
Examine the Hanafi Justification
Mahr is legally obligated, so its minimum is tied to a legal measure: the nisab of theft (ten dirhams). The Quranic verse 33:50 supports this.
Other imams also tie mahr minimum to their view of nisab al-sariqa.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i/Hanbali Objection
They argue that any valuable item suffices, citing hadith of sawiq, sandals, and a date-stone of gold. List each evidence.
These hadith are interpreted differently by the Hanafis.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Responses
The sawiq hadith is abrogated (related to mut'a), the sandal hadith refers to an advance (mu'ajjal), and the date-stone actually weighed five dirhams.
The Hanafi hadith 'No mahr less than ten dirhams' is strengthened by multiple chains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المهر
أي في بيان أحكامه
صح النكاح بلا ذكره، وأقله عشرة دراهم، فإن سماها .
أي بلا ذكر مهر ومع نفيه
المهر
أي العشرة
باب المهر: [وهو حكم النكاح فإن مهر المثل يجب بالعقد فكان حكما له. (فتح)] لما فرغ من بيان ركن النكاح وشرطه وما هو في معنى الشرط كالكفاءة شرع في بيان حكمه وهو المهر وهو اسم لما تستحقه المرأة لعقد النكاح أو الوطء بشهوة، ويقال له الصداق والنحلة والأجر والفريضة والصدقة والهباء، وجاء في السنة تسميته بالعليقة والعقر، وقد سماه الله تعالى بالابتغاء. (فتح)
:
بلا ذكره أي يصح النكاح وإن لم يسم فيه مهر؛ لأن النكاح عقد انضمام وازدواج لغة، والمقصود منه التوالد دون المال، فيتم بالزوجين، ولا يشترط فيه ذكر المهر، ثم المهر واجب شرعاً إنابة لشرف المحل لكن لا يحتاج إلى ذكره لصحة النكاح، وكذا يصح النكاح مع نفي المهر ، وقال مالك: لا يصح مع النفي اعتباراً بالبيع، وقال بعض الشافعية: إن تزوجها بلا مهر في الحال ولا في الاستقبال لا يصح النكاح؛ لأنها تصير كالموهوبة، ولنا: ما ذكرنا؛ ولأن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، فكذا بشرط ترك المهر بخلاف البيع. (مستخلص، فتح) عشرة دراهم وزن سبعة مثاقيل كل درهم أربعة عشر قيراطا ولا فرق بين الدين والعين ولا بين مضروبة وغير مضروبة حتى يجوز وزن عشرة تبراً، وإن كان قيمته أقل، بخلاف نصاب السرقة، وكل واحد من الأئمة قدر المهر بما هو نصاب السرقة عنده، فقال مالك: مقدر بربع دينار أو ثلاثة دراهم، وقال ابن شبرمة: أقله خمسة دراهم، وقال إبراهيم النخعي: أقله أربعون درهماً، وعنه عشرون درهماً، وقال سعيد بن جبير: أقله خمسون درهماً، وكل واحد منهم قدره بنصاب السرقة عنده، وقال الشافعي وأحمد ما جاز أن يكون ثمناً جاز أن يكون مهراً؛ لحديث جابر الله أنه عليه قال: "من أعطى في صداق امرأة ملأ كفيه سويقاً أو تمراً فقد استحل"، رواه أبو داود، ولما أن امرأة تزوجت بنعلين فأجازه علي ، رواه الترمذي، ولما روي أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف أمهر زنة نواة من ذهب، ولنا ما روي في حديث جابر ه: "لا" مهر أقل من عشرة دراهم"، رواه الدار قطني. وفيه مبشر ابن عبيد وحجاج بن أرطاة وهما ضعيفان عند المحدثين، ولكن البيهقي رواه من طرق، والسهيلي رواه من طرق، والضعيف إذا روي من طرق يصير حسناً ويحتج به، ذكره النووي في شرح المهذب" عن علي له أنه قال: "أقل ما تستحل به المرأة عشرة دراهم ، ذكره البيهقي وحديث أبي داود كان في المتعة وهو منسوخ، وحديث الترمذي محمول على المعجل والنواة في حديث عبد الرحمن الذي رواه الجماعة خمسة دراهم عند الأكثر ، وعند أحمد ثلاثة دراهم، وهو يزيد على دينارين فكيف يحتج به على جواز الفلس. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۷/۱] وأيضاً قال الشافعي: إن المهر حقها فيكون التقدير إليها، ولنا أنه حق الشرع وجوباً فيقدر بما له حظ في الشرع وهو نصاب السرقة، وإنما قلنا: إنه مقدر شرعا؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿قَدْ عَلِمْنَا مَا فَرَضْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِي أَزْوَاجِهِمْ ﴾ (الأحزاب: (٥٠) (مسكين، فتح، مستخلص)
Chapter of Mahr. That is concerning the exposition of its rulings. The marriage is valid without mentioning it, and its minimum is ten dirhams. If he specifies it... That is, without mentioning a mahr and with its denial. Mahr: that is, ten dirhams. Chapter of Mahr: [It is the legal effect (hukm) of marriage, for the mahr of the like (mahr al-mithl) becomes obligatory by the contract, so it is a consequence of it. (Fath)] When he finished explaining the pillar (rukn) of marriage, its condition, and what is in the meaning of a condition like suitability (kafa'a), he began explaining its legal effect, which is the mahr. It is a name for what the woman deserves due to the marriage contract or sexual intercourse with desire. It is called sadaq, nihla, ajr, farida, sadaqa, and hiba'. In the Sunnah it is called 'aliqa and 'aqr, and Allah the Exalted named it ibtigha' (seeking). (Fath) "Without mentioning it" means that the marriage is valid even if no mahr is named in it, because marriage linguistically is a contract of joining and pairing, and its purpose is procreation, not wealth; thus it is concluded by the two spouses, and mentioning mahr is not a condition for its validity. Then the mahr is obligatory by law out of honor for the (woman's) status, but it does not need to be mentioned for the validity of the marriage. Likewise, the marriage is valid with the denial of mahr. Malik said: it is not valid with denial, by analogy to sale. Some Shafi'is said: if he marries her with no mahr at present nor in the future, the marriage is not valid, because she becomes like a gifted woman. Our evidence: what we mentioned, and because marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions, so likewise with the condition of abandoning mahr, unlike sale. (Mustakhlas, Fath) "Ten dirhams" of weight of seven mithqals, each dirham fourteen qirats. There is no difference between debt and cash, nor between minted and unminted, even if ten of bullion are weighed, even if its value is less, unlike the nisab of theft. Each of the imams estimated the mahr as his nisab of theft: Malik estimated it as a quarter dinar or three dirhams; Ibn Shubruma said its minimum is five dirhams; Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said its minimum is forty dirhams, and from him twenty dirhams; Sa'id ibn Jubayr said its minimum is fifty dirhams. Each of them estimated it by his nisab of theft. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: whatever is valid as a price is valid as a mahr, due to the hadith of Jabir that he (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever gives as sadaq to a woman a handful of sawiq or dates has made (her) lawful," narrated by Abu Dawud; and because a woman married for a pair of sandals and 'Ali validated it, narrated by al-Tirmidhi; and because it is narrated that 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf gave as mahr a weight of a date-stone of gold. Our evidence: what is narrated in the hadith of Jabir: "No mahr less than ten dirhams," narrated by al-Daraqutni. It contains Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd and Hajjaj ibn Arta'a, and they are weak according to hadith scholars. However, al-Bayhaqi narrated it through multiple chains, and al-Suhayli narrated it through multiple chains, and a weak hadith when narrated through multiple chains becomes hasan and is used as evidence. Al-Nawawi mentioned it in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. From 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: "The minimum by which a woman is made lawful is ten dirhams," al-Bayhaqi mentioned it. The hadith of Abu Dawud was about mut'a and is abrogated. The hadith of al-Tirmidhi is interpreted as (payment) in advance (mu'ajjal). And the date-stone in the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman is five dirhams according to most, and according to Ahmad three dirhams, and it is more than two dinars, so how can it be used as evidence for the permissibility of a fals (paltry amount)? [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:207] Also al-Shafi'i said: the mahr is her right, so the estimation is left to her. Our evidence: it is a right of the law by obligation, so it is estimated by what has a share in the law, which is the nisab of theft. We say it is legally estimated due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: "We know what We have prescribed for them concerning their wives" (Quran 33:50) (Miskin, Fath, Mustakhlas).
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq introduces the chapter on the mahr (dower). It opens with the fundamental ruling: marriage is valid even if no mahr is mentioned, and the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. The author defines mahr as what a woman deserves due to the marriage contract or consummation, listing various Quranic and Sunnah terms for it. The passage then explains why mention of mahr is not a condition: marriage is a contract of companionship and procreation, not a purely financial transaction. Therefore, it is valid even if the parties explicitly deny any mahr, contrary to the view of Imam Malik and some Shafi'is, who analogize it to a sale. The Hanafi response is that marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions, so the condition of no mahr does not invalidate it. The text then specifies the minimum: ten dirhams of a specific weight (seven mithqals, each dirham being 14 qirats). This minimum is derived from the nisab of theft, a principle unique to the Hanafi school. The passage enumerates various other imams' estimations (Malik, Ibn Shubruma, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Sa'id ibn Jubayr) and then addresses the Shafi'i/Hanbali position that any valuable thing can be mahr, citing hadith of a handful of sawiq, a pair of sandals, and a date-stone of gold. The author refutes these by arguing that the hadith of a handful of sawiq is abrogated (related to mut'a), the sandal hadith is about an advance (mu'ajjal), and the date-stone is actually five dirhams. The key Hanafi evidence is the hadith "No mahr less than ten dirhams" narrated by al-Daraqutni, which despite weak transmitters, is strengthened by multiple chains and considered hasan. Additionally, a saying of 'Ali supports the ten dirham minimum. The passage concludes with the Shafi'i argument that mahr is the woman's right and she can agree to any amount, but the Hanafi response is that since it is a legally obligated right, it must be estimated by a legal measure, namely the nisab of theft, supported by the Quranic verse (33:50).

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): What the woman deserves due to the marriage contract or sexual intercourse with desire; also called sadaq, nihla, ajr, farida, sadaqa, hiba'.
نصاب السرقة (nisāb al-sariqa): The minimum value (nisab) for which the hand is cut for theft. In Hanafi law, it is ten dirhams or one dinar.
فضولي (fudūlī): A person who acts in a contract without prior authorization. Not present in this lesson.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum mahr?
A) No minimum; any amount suffices.
B) Three dirhams.
C) Ten dirhams of specific weight.
D) Fifty dirhams.

Key Takeaway
Marriage is valid without mentioning mahr, but if mahr is due, it must be at least ten dirhams in the Hanafi school.

Nikah — Marriage

Minimum Dower and Validity of Marriage Without Mentioning It
Ruling on dower with proofs and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of marriage without specifying dower and the minimum dower of ten dirhams, and explain the proofs and responses to opposing schools.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid without mentioning dower; minimum dower is ten dirhams — a fixed shari'ah right, not left to negotiation.

This passage from a Hanafi manual opens the chapter on dower (mahr). It establishes two key rulings: (1) marriage is valid even if no dower is mentioned or even if the dower is explicitly negated, and (2) the minimum dower is ten dirhams. The author then defends these positions against Maliki and Shafi'i objections, grounding them in a specific hadith and the nature of marriage as a companionship contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the first lines: marriage is valid without mentioning dower and even with its negation; minimum dower is ten dirhams.
Focus on the phrase 'صح النكاح بلا ذكره، وأقله عشرة دراهم'.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Locate the hadith 'لا مهر أقل من عشرة دراهم' and note the chain and its acceptance as hasan.
The hadith is narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi through multiple chains.
3
Understand the nature of marriage vs sale
Note the argument that marriage is a companionship contract, not a property exchange, so it does not require a fixed price like a sale.
This rebuts Malik's analogy to sale.
4
Analyze opposing proofs and responses
Review the Shafi'i hadiths of small dowers and the Hanafi response: they are either abrogated (temporary marriage) or refer to prompt dower, and the date-stone weight is actually five dirhams.
The Hanafi position also argues that the dower is a fixed shari'ah right, not negotiable.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, if a marriage is contracted with a dower below ten dirhams, it is valid but the wife is entitled to ten dirhams; under Shafi'i law, any amount suffices and marriage without dower may be invalid.
Practical consequence for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المهر أي في بيان أحكامه
صح النكاح بلا ذكره، وأقله عشرة دراهم، فإن سمى أي بلا ذكر مهر ومع نفيه المهر أي العشرة
باب المهر: [وهو حكم النكاح فإن مهر المثل يجب بالعقد فكان حكما له. (فتح)] لما فرغ من بيان ركن النكاح وشرطه وما هو في معنى الشرط كالكفاءة شرع في بيان حكمه وهو المهر وهو اسم لما تستحقه المرأة لعقد النكاح أو الوطء بشهوة، ويقال له الصداق والنحلة والأجر والفريضة والصدقة والهباء، وجاء في السنة تسميته بالعليقة والعقر، وقد سماه الله تعالى بالابتغاء. (فتح)
:
بلا ذكره أي يصح النكاح وإن لم يسم فيه مهر؛ لأن النكاح عقد انضمام وازدواج لغة، والمقصود منه التوالد دون المال، فيتم بالزوجين، ولا يشترط فيه ذكر المهر، ثم المهر واجب شرعاً إنابة لشرف المحل لكن لا يحتاج إلى ذكره لصحة النكاح، وكذا يصح النكاح مع نفي المهر، وقال مالك: لا يصح مع النفي اعتباراً بالبيع، وقال بعض الشافعية: إن تزوجها بلا مهر في الحال ولا في الاستقبال لا يصح النكاح؛ لأنها تصير كالموهوبة، ولنا: ما ذكرنا؛ ولأن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، فكذا بشرط ترك المهر بخلاف البيع. (مستخلص، فتح) عشرة دراهم وزن سبعة مثاقيل كل درهم أربعة عشر قيراطا ولا فرق بين الدين والعين ولا بين مضروبة وغير مضروبة حتى يجوز وزن عشرة تبراً، وإن كان قيمته أقل، بخلاف نصاب السرقة، وكل واحد من الأئمة قدر المهر بما هو نصاب السرقة عنده، فقال مالك: مقدر بربع دينار أو ثلاثة دراهم، وقال ابن شبرمة: أقله خمسة دراهم، وقال إبراهيم النخعي: أقله أربعون درهماً، وعنه عشرون درهماً، وقال سعيد بن جبير: أقله خمسون درهماً، وكل واحد منهم قدره بنصاب السرقة عنده، وقال الشافعي وأحمد ما جاز أن يكون ثمناً جاز أن يكون مهراً؛ لحديث جابر الله أنه عليه قال: "من أعطى في صداق امرأة ملأ كفيه سويقاً أو تمراً فقد استحل"، رواه أبو داود، ولما أن امرأة تزوجت بنعلين فأجازه علي، رواه الترمذي، ولما روي أن عبد الرحمن بن عوف أمهر زنة نواة من ذهب، ولنا ما روي في حديث جابر ه: "لا" مهر أقل من عشرة دراهم"، رواه الدار قطني. وفيه مبشر ابن عبيد وحجاج بن أرطاة وهما ضعيفان عند المحدثين، ولكن البيهقي رواه من طرق، والسهيلي رواه من طرق، والضعيف إذا روي من طرق يصير حسناً ويحتج به، ذكره النووي في شرح المهذب" عن علي له أنه قال: "أقل ما تستحل به المرأة عشرة دراهم"، ذكره البيهقي وحديث أبي داود كان في المتعة وهو منسوخ، وحديث الترمذي محمول على المعجل والنواة في حديث عبد الرحمن الذي رواه الجماعة خمسة دراهم عند الأكثر، وعند أحمد ثلاثة دراهم، وهو يزيد على دينارين فكيف يحتج به على جواز الفلس. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۷/۱] وأيضاً قال الشافعي: إن المهر حقها فيكون التقدير إليها، ولنا أنه حق الشرع وجوباً فيقدر بما له حظ في الشرع وهو نصاب السرقة، وإنما قلنا: إنه مقدر شرعا؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿قَدْ عَلِمْنَا مَا فَرَضْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِي أَزْوَاجِهِمْ ﴾ (الأحزاب: (٥٠) (مسكين، فتح، مستخلص) روي
The chapter of dower: Explanation of its rulings. Marriage is valid without mentioning it, and its minimum is ten dirhams, if he specifies it... meaning without mentioning dower and even with its negation. The dower meaning the ten. The chapter of dower: [It is the ruling of marriage, for the dower of the like is obligatory upon the contract, so it is a ruling of it (Fath)]. After finishing the explanation of the pillar of marriage and its conditions and what is like a condition such as suitability, he began explaining its ruling, which is the dower. It is a name for what the woman deserves due to the marriage contract or sexual intercourse with desire. It is also called sadaq, nahlah, ajr, faridah, sadaqah, and hiba. In the Sunnah it is called 'aliqah and 'aqr, and Allah Most High called it ibtigha' (Fath). Without mentioning it: meaning the marriage is valid even if a dower is not named in it, because marriage is a contract of joining and pairing linguistically, and its purpose is procreation, not property, so it is perfected by the spouses, and mentioning the dower is not a condition for its validity. Then the dower is obligatory by law as a substitute for the honor of the place, but it is not needed to be mentioned for the validity of the marriage. Likewise, the marriage is valid with the negation of the dower. Malik said: It is not valid with negation analogizing to sale. Some Shafi'is said: If he marries her without a dower immediately nor in the future, the marriage is not valid because she becomes like a gifted woman. Our proof: what we mentioned, and because marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions, so likewise with the condition of leaving the dower, unlike sale. (Mustakhlas, Fath) Ten dirhams by weight of seven mithqals, each dirham fourteen qirats, and there is no difference between gold and goods nor between minted and unminted, so that weighing ten pure gold pieces is permissible, even if its value is less, unlike the nisab of theft. Each of the imams estimated the dower as the nisab of theft in his view. Malik said: It is estimated as a quarter dinar or three dirhams. Ibn Shabrama said: Its minimum is five dirhams. Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said: Its minimum is forty dirhams, and from him twenty dirhams. Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: Its minimum is fifty dirhams. Each of them estimated it as the nisab of theft in his view. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: Whatever can be a price can be a dower, due to the hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever gives as a dower to a woman a handful of finely-ground barley or dates has made her lawful,' narrated by Abu Dawud, and because a woman married with two sandals and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) permitted it, narrated by al-Tirmidhi, and because it is narrated that 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf gave a dower of a date-stone weight of gold. Our proof is what is narrated in the hadith of Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him): 'No dower less than ten dirhams,' narrated by al-Daraqutni. In it is Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd and Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah, both weak according to hadith scholars, but al-Bayhaqi narrated it through multiple chains, and al-Suhayli narrated it through multiple chains, and a weak hadith if narrated through multiple chains becomes hasan and is used as evidence. Mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. And from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'The least by which a woman is made lawful is ten dirhams,' mentioned by al-Bayhaqi. And the hadith of Abu Dawud was concerning temporary marriage and is abrogated, and the hadith of al-Tirmidhi is interpreted as the prompt dower. And the date-stone in the hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman reported by the group is five dirhams according to the majority, and according to Ahmad three dirhams, and that is more than two dinars, so how can it be used as evidence to permit a dirham? [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/207] And also al-Shafi'i said: Indeed the dower is her right, so the estimation is left to her. Our proof: It is a right of the Shari'ah obligatory, so it is estimated by what has significance in the Shari'ah, which is the nisab of theft. And we only say that it is estimated by the Shari'ah due to His statement: 'Indeed, We know what We have imposed upon them concerning their wives' (al-Ahzab: 50) (Miskin, Fath, Mustakhlas). Narrated.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on dower (mahr) from a Hanafi manual. It first defines mahr as what the woman deserves due to marriage or intercourse, listing its various names in the Quran and Sunnah. The central ruling is that marriage is valid without specifying a dower, and even if the dower is explicitly negated, the marriage remains valid. This is because the essence of marriage is companionship and procreation, not a financial exchange. The Hanafi school differentiates it from sale, which requires a price. Maliki and some Shafi'i scholars object, but the Hanafi response holds that marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions, so a condition to forgo dower does not nullify the contract. The minimum dower is set at ten dirhams (weight of seven mithqals, each dirham 14 qirats). This is the nisab of theft in the Hanafi school, and the text notes that other imams set the minimum according to their own nisab of theft. The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools allow any amount that can be a price, citing hadiths of small items given as dowries. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'No dower less than ten dirhams' which, though weak, is strengthened by multiple chains. The passage also critiques the opposing evidences, showing that the hadith of handful of barley is about temporary marriage (abrogated), the sandals hadith refers to prompt dower, and the date-stone weight is interpreted as five dirhams, not a negligible amount. The argument concludes that since Allah says He knows what He imposed, the dower is a fixed obligation, not left to the woman's discretion. The last word 'ruwiya' likely introduces another narration, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): What the woman deserves due to marriage or sexual intercourse, also called sadaq, nahlah, etc.
صداق (sadaq): Another term for mahr.
نصاب السرقة (nisab al-sariqah): The minimum value for which theft entails the hadd penalty; in Hanafi school it is ten dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of dower according to the Hanafi school?
A) Five dirhams
B) Ten dirhams
C) A handful of dates
D) Whatever the woman agrees to

Key Takeaway
Marriage is a companionship contract, not a sale; thus its validity does not depend on mentioning a dower, but a minimum dower of ten dirhams is fixed by the Shari'ah.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Dower Below Minimum or Unspecified: Hanafi Rulings
Rulings on dower when specified below minimum or unspecified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on dower when the specified amount is below ten dirhams or when no dower is specified, and apply the rules of halving and mut'ah accordingly.

Core Idea
Ten dirhams is the minimum indivisible dower; if specified less, she gets ten; if unspecified, she gets mahr al-mithl or mut'ah.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rules for dower (mahr) in marriage contracts where the amount is either specified below ten dirhams or left unspecified entirely. You will learn how the school treats these scenarios across different events: consummation, death, valid seclusion, and divorce before consummation. We will also examine the basis for mahr al-mithl and mut'ah, and address the disagreements with Imam Zufar within the Hanafi school and with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage covers three main dower scenarios: (1) specified but less than ten dirhams, (2) not specified at all, (3) explicitly negated (condition for no dower). For each, determine the event: consummation, death, seclusion, or divorce before consummation.
The ruling differs based on whether the marriage was consummated or ended by death or seclusion vs. divorce.
2
Apply the rule for specified dower below ten
If the dower is specified below ten dirhams (e.g., eight), upon consummation, death, or valid seclusion, the wife gets ten dirhams—the minimum. This is because ten is indivisible; mentioning part implies the whole. Imam Zufar disagrees and says she gets mahr al-mithl.
The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is applied in fatwa.
3
Apply the rule for specified dower upon divorce
If the husband divorces before consummation, the dower is halved per Quran 2:237. Even if the specified amount was below ten, the effective dower becomes ten and then halves to five.
Zufar holds that mut'ah is due instead of half in this case.
4
Apply the rules for unspecified or negated dower
If no dower was specified (or was negated), the wife receives mahr al-mithl upon consummation or death of either spouse, and mut'ah (a consolation gift) upon divorce before consummation. The hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq is the proof for mahr al-mithl, and Quranic command for mut'ah.
The Hanafi school holds mut'ah as wajib; Malik considers it mustahabb.
5
Distinguish mut'ah conditions and disputes
Mut'ah is obligatory only if the separation comes from the husband's side (divorce, ila', li'an, impotence, etc.) and not from the wife's side. Its amount (based on the wife's or husband's status) ranges between half of mahr al-mithl and five dirhams.
The Shafi'i school denies any obligation by the contract alone; the Hanafi refutation relies on the Shari'ah's initial right.

أو دونها فلها عشرة بالوطء أو الموت أو الخلوة، وبالطلاق قبل الوطء تتنصف، وإن لم يُسمّه أو نفاه فلها مهر مثلها إن وطئ أو مات عنها والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الوطء، ولو حكماً أي موت أحدهما أو الخلوة الصحيحة أي للمرأة أو دونها: أي سمي دون العشرة كثمانية مثلا بالوطء أو الموت أي موت أحدهما، أما في التسمية؛ فلأنه سمي ما يصلح مهراً فيتأكد بالدخول وينتهي النكاح بالموت، وأما في مادون العشرة؛ فلأن العشرة في كونها مهراً لا تتجزأ، وذكر بعض ما لا يتجزأ كذكر كله كالطلاق، وقال زفر لها مهر المثل؛ لأنه سمي ما لا يصلح مهراً، فصار كأن لم يسم، وعند الثلاثة: يجب ما سمي رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٨/١] (عيني) تتنصف أي العشرة فيجب خمسة دراهم وكذالك يتنصف كل ما سمي مهراً بما فوق العشرة؛ لقوله تعالى: فَنِصْفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ (البقرة:۲۳۷) وقال زفر: تجب المتعة إذا سمي أقل من عشرة، وفي العشرة يجب النصف بلا خلاف، ولم يذكر الخلوة مع أنها كالوطء عندنا؛ لأنه ذكره فيما بعد. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۸/۱] لم يسمه: المهر تسمية صحيحة أو سكت عنها. (ط) نفاه: بأن تزوج على أن لا مهر لها. (ط) أو مات عنها : أي عن المرأة بلا دخول، وكذا إذا ماتت هي وقال الشافعي: لا يجب بنفس العقد شيء، وإنما يجب بالدخول، وبالموت عند بعضهم، لأن المهر حقها فلها نفيه ابتداء كما أن لها إسقاطه انتهاء، ولنا: أن إيجاب المهر حق الشرع ابتداء فلا تتمكن هي من نفيه، وإنما يصير حقا لها انتهاء فتملك الإبراء دون النفي، ولنا: أيضاً ما روى علقمة عن ابن مسعود له: أنه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة، ثم مات عنها، ولم يفرض لها صداقاً و لم يكن دخل بها، فقال: "أرى" لها مثل صداق نسائها، ولها الميراث وعليها العدة ، فقام أبو الجراح معقل بن سنان الأشجعي فشهد أن النبي "قضى في تزويج بروع بنت واشق الأشجعية بمثل ما قضيت"، رواه أبو داود والترمذي، وقال: حديث حسن صحيح رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۸/۱] (مستخلص) والمتعة بالرفع عطف على قوله : "فلها مهر مثلها أي ولها المتعة وهذه المتعة واجبة عندنا، وقال مالك والليث وابن أبي ليلى: مستحبة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ حَقّاً عَلَى الْمُحْسِنِينَ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٦)، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَتِّعُوهُنَّ والأمر للوجوب، وقوله : وهي "درع أي المتعة ثلاثة أشياء، وهو مروي عن عائشة وابن عباس له ويعتبر في المتعة حال الزوجة، وهو قول الكرخي، وقيل: حال الزوج، وقال صاحب الهداية: هو الصحيح، وقيل: يعتبر بحالهما، حكاه صاحب "البدائع"، وعند الثلاثة: ما يقدره الحاكم، وعن أحمد أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة، ثم هي لا تزاد على نصف مهر المثل ولا تنقص عن خمسة دراهم، ولا تجب إلا إذا حصلت الفرقة من جهة الزوج كالطلاق والإيلاء وغيرها، وإن كانت الفرقة من جهة المرأة فلا تجب كردتها وإبائها عن الإسلام، وتقبيلها ابن الزوج بشهوة، والرضاع، وخيار البلوغ وخيار العتق وعدم الكفاءة. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۹/۱] هي قبل الوطء وقبل الخلوة أو فارقها بإيلاء أو لعان أو جبّ أو عنة أو إباء منه أو تقبيل ابنتها أو أمها بشهوة. (ط)
Or less than it (the ten): she has ten dirhams upon intercourse, or death, or seclusion; and by divorce before intercourse it becomes half. And if he did not specify it or negated it, she has the mahr of the like of her if he had intercourse or died upon her, and the mut'ah if he divorces her before intercourse, even if legally (meaning death of one of them or valid seclusion). For the woman: 'or less than it' means he specified less than ten, like eight for example, upon intercourse or death (meaning death of one of them). As for specification: because he specified what is suitable as a dower, so it is confirmed by entry and the marriage ends by death. As for less than ten: because ten is indivisible as a dower, and mentioning a part of what is indivisible is like mentioning the whole, like divorce. Zufar said: She has the mahr of the like, because he specified what is not suitable as a dower, so it is as if he did not specify. According to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): what is specified is obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/208] (Ayni) It becomes half: i.e., the ten, so five dirhams become obligatory, and likewise every specified dower above ten becomes half, due to His statement: 'Then half of what you have prescribed' (al-Baqarah: 237). Zufar said: Mut'ah is obligatory if he specified less than ten, and in the case of ten, half is obligatory without disagreement. And he did not mention seclusion although it is like intercourse in our view, because he mentioned it later. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/208] 'He did not specify it': meaning the dower with a valid specification or remained silent about it. (T) 'Negated it': meaning he married on the condition that she has no dower. (T) 'Or died upon her': i.e., upon the woman without entry, and likewise if she dies. Al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is obligatory by the contract itself; rather it becomes obligatory by entry, and by death according to some, because the dower is her right, so she can negate it initially just as she can drop it eventually. Our proof: Indeed the obligation of dower is the right of the Shari'ah initially, so she cannot negate it; rather it becomes her right eventually, so she owns the right to waive it, not to negate it. And also our proof: what 'Alqamah narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): that he was asked about a man who married a woman, then died upon her, and had not prescribed a dower for her, and had not consummated with her. He said: 'I think she has the dower of the like of her women, and she has inheritance, and she must observe the waiting period.' Then Abu al-Jarrah Ma'qil ibn Sinan al-Ashja'i stood and testified that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged in the marriage of Barwa' bint Washiq al-Ashja'iyya similarly to what he judged. Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi, and he said: hasan sahih. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/208] (Mustakhlas) And 'al-mut'ah' (with raf') is a conjunction to his statement: 'she has the mahr of the like', meaning she also has the mut'ah. This mut'ah is obligatory in our school. Malik, al-Layth, and Ibn Abi Layla said: It is recommended, due to His statement: 'a right upon the doers of good' (al-Baqarah: 236). Our proof: His statement: 'And provide for them' (al-Baqarah: 236) and the command is for obligation. And his statement: 'It is a gown' meaning the mut'ah is three things, narrated from 'A'ishah and Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). And consideration is given to the wife's condition regarding mut'ah, which is the view of al-Karkhi. It is said: the husband's condition. The author of al-Hidayah said: That is the correct view. It is said: consideration is given to both conditions, narrated by the author of al-Bada'i'. According to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): what the judge estimates. From Ahmad: the least amount with which prayer is valid. Then it (mut'ah) does not exceed half of the mahr of the like and does not fall below five dirhams. And it is not obligatory unless the separation occurs from the husband's side, such as divorce, ila', and others. If the separation is from the wife's side, it is not obligatory, such as her apostasy, her refusal to accept Islam, her kissing the husband's son with desire, breastfeeding, the option of puberty, the option of emancipation, and lack of suitability. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/209] It is before intercourse and before seclusion, or if he separates from her by ila', li'an, impotence, 'innah, his refusal, or kissing her daughter or mother with desire. (T)
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage details the legal consequences for dower in various scenarios. First, if the husband specifies a dower less than ten dirhams (e.g., eight), the wife is entitled to ten dirhams upon consummation, death of either spouse, or valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah). This is because ten dirhams is the minimum dower and is indivisible; specifying a part is like specifying the whole, similar to divorce (where specifying one part implies the whole). Imam Zufar differs, arguing that since less than ten is invalid as a dower, it is as if no dower was specified, so she gets mahr al-mithl. But the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that the specified amount is validated up to the minimum, so she gets ten. Upon divorce before consummation, the dower is halved, so if ten was specified, she gets five; if more was specified, she gets half of that. This is based on Quran 2:237 'half of what you have prescribed.' Zufar again disagrees, saying mut'ah is due if less than ten was specified. The author notes that seclusion is omitted here but is treated like intercourse later. Second, if no dower is specified or the dower is explicitly negated, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) upon consummation or death of either spouse, and mut'ah if divorced before consummation. The Hanafi proof for mahr al-mithl is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud about Barwa' bint Washiq, where the Prophet judged similarly. The opposing Shafi'i view that nothing is obligatory by the contract alone is rejected because the obligation is from the Shari'ah, not from her agreement. Mut'ah is obligatory in the Hanafi school, derived from the command in Quran 2:236 'And provide for them.' The Hanafi view considers it wajib, while Malik considers it mustahabb. The value of mut'ah is based on the wife's condition (or the husband's, according to the correct view in al-Hidayah), and it cannot exceed half of mahr al-mithl nor be less than five dirhams. It is only due when separation comes from the husband, not from the wife. The passage lists causes from the husband's side: divorce, ila', li'an, impotence, 'innah, refusal, or kissing the wife's daughter/mother with desire.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower commensurate with women of similar age, beauty, family, etc., to the bride.
متعة (mut'ah): A consolation gift given to the wife upon divorce before consummation when no dower was specified.
تتنصف (tatanassaf): The dower becomes half upon divorce before consummation.
خلوة صحيحة (khalwah sahihah): Valid seclusion where the couple is alone and there is no legal or physical impediment to intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, what does a woman get if her husband divorces her before consummation without having specified any dower?
A) Nothing
B) Half of mahr al-mithl
C) Mut'ah (a consolation gift)
D) Full mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ensures a minimum dower of ten dirhams and imposes mut'ah as an obligation upon divorce without specified dower, protecting the wife's rights from the outset of the contract.

Ruling on Mahr Less Than Ten Dirhams
Ruling on mahr less than ten dirhams with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mahr specified below ten dirhams and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the three Imams and Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
A mahr less than ten dirhams is valid and halves upon divorce before consummation.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi stance on a common marriage contract scenario: a mahr specified below the ten-dirham minimum. It establishes that such a mahr is valid and, if divorce occurs before consummation, the wife receives half of the specified amount. The text also presents Imam Zufar's dissenting view, offering insight into the legal reasoning that supports the majority position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding a mahr specified as less than ten dirhams.
The mahr is valid and obligatory; upon divorce before consummation, it halves.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Zufar holds a dissenting opinion within the Hanafi school.
Zufar argues the mahr is invalid because it is below the minimum, so mahr al-mithl or mut'a is due.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Zufar's reasoning: the specified amount is not suitable as a mahr, so it is as if no mahr was specified.
His dalil is that ten dirhams is the minimum; specifying less is like specifying nothing.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the response of the three: ten dirhams is indivisible as a mahr, and mentioning part of an indivisible whole is like mentioning the whole, analogous to divorce.
They also cite Quran 2:237, which commands halving 'what you prescribed'—any prescribed amount, not just the minimum.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in outcome between the two views.
Example: for a mahr of 8 dirhams and divorce before consummation, the three give 4 dirhams; Zufar gives mahr al-mithl or mut'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو دونها فلها عشرة بالوطء أو الموت أو الخلوة، وبالطلاق قبل الوطء تتنصف، وإن العشرة المرأة دراهم ولو حكماً أي موت أحدهما أو الخلوة الصحيحة لم يُسمّه أو نفاه فلها مهر مثلها إن وطئ أو مات عنها والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الوطء، ولو حكماً أي الزوج المرأة أي للمرأة من النساء أو دونها: أي سمي دون العشرة كثمانية مثلا بالوطء أو الموت أي موت أحدهما، أما في التسمية؛ فلأنه سمي ما يصلح مهراً فيتأكد بالدخول وينتهي النكاح بالموت، وأما في مادون العشرة؛ فلأن العشرة في كونها مهراً لا تتجزأ، وذكر بعض ما لا يتجزأ كذكر كله كالطلاق، وقال زفر لها مهر المثل؛ لأنه سمي ما لا يصلح مهراً، فصار كأن لم يسم، وعند الثلاثة: يجب ما سمي رمز الحقائق: ٢٠٨/١] (عيني) تتنصف أي العشرة فيجب خمسة دراهم وكذالك يتنصف كل ما سمي مهراً بما فوق العشرة؛ لقوله تعالى: فَنِصْفُ مَا فَرَضْتُ الله (البقرة:۲۳۷) وقال زفر: تجب المتعة إذا سمي أقل من عشرة، وفي العشرة يجب النصف بلا خلاف
Or less than it (ten dirhams), so she gets ten by intercourse, death, or valid seclusion, and by divorce before intercourse it halves. And if the woman (receives) ten dirhams even legally, i.e., death of one of them or valid seclusion. If he did not specify or negated it, she gets the mahr of her peers if he had intercourse or she died, and a consolatory gift if he divorced before intercourse, even legally, i.e., the husband (died) or the woman. Or less than it: i.e., he specified less than ten, like eight, by intercourse or death, i.e., death of one. As for specification, because he specified what is suitable as a mahr, so it is confirmed by consummation and the marriage ends by death. As for less than ten, because ten is indivisible as a mahr, and mentioning part of what is indivisible is like mentioning the whole, like divorce. Zufar said: she gets mahr al-mithl, because he specified what is not suitable as a mahr, so it is as if he did not specify. According to the three (Imams), what he specified is obligatory. (Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/208) (Ayni) It halves, i.e., the ten, so five dirhams are obligatory, and likewise everything specified as mahr above ten halves due to His statement: 'So half of what you prescribed' (Quran 2:237). Zufar said: the consolatory gift is obligatory if he specified less than ten, and for ten the half is obligatory without disagreement.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on mahr when it is specified as less than ten dirhams. The base text states that if the mahr is less than ten dirhams, the woman is entitled to the full ten dirhams if there is consummation, death of either spouse, or valid seclusion (khalwah). However, if divorce occurs before consummation, the mahr is halved. The commentator explains that 'or less than it' refers to a mahr specified as less than ten dirhams, such as eight. The reason is that the amount of ten dirhams is considered the minimum for a valid mahr; specifying less is like specifying nothing because ten is indivisible as a mahr—mentioning part of an indivisible entity is like mentioning the whole, analogous to divorce. Imam Zufar disagrees: he says the woman gets mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers) because the specified amount is not suitable as a mahr, so it is as if no mahr was specified. However, the dominant position (the three: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that the specified amount is valid and obligatory, so it halves upon divorce. Zufar also holds that if the specified amount is less than ten, the woman is entitled only to mut'a (a consolatory gift), not half, because the mahr is not valid. There is no disagreement about the case of ten dirhams: it is valid and halved upon divorce.

Key Terms
العشرة (al-'asharah): The minimum amount for a valid mahr (dower) according to the Hanafi school.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr appropriate for a woman similar to the bride in status and condition, used when no valid mahr is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant Hanafi position, if a man specifies a mahr of eight dirhams and then divorces his wife before consummation, how much is she entitled to?
A) Four dirhams (half of eight)
B) Ten dirhams (the minimum mahr)
C) Mahr al-mithl)
D) A consolatory gift (mut'a)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a mahr specified as less than ten dirhams is valid and, on divorce before consummation, the wife is entitled to half of that specified amount, not mahr al-mithl.

Ruling on Unspecified Mahr and Obligation of Mut'a
Ruling on mahr and mut'a with inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on mahr when unspecified and on mut'a upon divorce before consummation, and evaluate the opposing proofs from other schools.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is due upon consummation or death; mut'a is wajib upon divorce before consummation.

This lesson explores two related rulings in Hanafi fiqh: the obligation of a proper dower (mahr al-mithl) when no mahr is fixed in the marriage contract, and the obligation of a consolatory gift (mut'a) when a marriage ends before consummation without a specified mahr. In both cases, the Hanafi school holds a position that differs from other Sunni schools, and we will examine the textual proofs and reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize the two distinct cases: marriage without specified dower (mahr), and divorce before consummation without dower. The Hanafi rulings differ for each.
In the first case, mahr al-mithl becomes due upon consummation or death. In the second, mut'a (consolatory gift) is due upon divorce.
2
State the Hanafi position on mahr and the Shafi'i counter-argument
Hanafi: Mahr al-mithl is obligatory by the contract itself, cannot be negated by the woman. Shafi'i: No mahr is due by contract; it is a right of the woman she can waive initially.
The difference stems from the nature of the right: divine (Hanafi) vs. personal (Shafi'i).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof for mahr
Examine the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq: the Prophet ruled that she receives mahr al-mithl. This is a direct precedent for obligation even without specification.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as proof by Hanafis.
4
State the Hanafi position on mut'a and the opposing view
Hanafi: Mut'a is wajib based on the imperative in Qur'an 2:236. Malik, al-Layth, Ibn Abi Layla: It is mustahabb because the verse says 'upon the doers of good'.
The dispute centers on whether the imperative indicates obligation or recommendation.
5
Examine the conditions and limits of mut'a
Mut'a is due only when separation originates from the husband (e.g., divorce, ila'), not from the wife. It consists of three items, assessed based on the husband's status (preferred view), and cannot exceed half of mahr al-mithl or be less than five dirhams.
These details are specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يسمه: المهر تسمية صحيحة أو سكت عنها. (ط) نفاه: بأن تزوج على أن لا . مهر لها. (ط) أو مات عنها : أي عن المرأة بلا دخول، وكذا إذا ماتت هي وقال الشافعي: لا يجب بنفس العقد شيء، وإنما يجب بالدخول، وبالموت عند بعضهم، لأن المهر حقها فلها نفيه ابتداء كما أن لها إسقاطه انتهاء، ولنا: أن إيجاب المهر حق الشرع ابتداء فلا تتمكن هي من نفيه، وإنما يصير حقا لها انتهاء فتملك الإبراء دون النفي، ولنا: أيضاً ما روى علقمة عن ابن مسعود له: أنه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة، ثم مات عنها، ولم يفرض لها صداقاً و لم يكن دخل بها، فقال: "أرى" لها مثل صداق نسائها، ولها الميراث وعليها العدة ، فقام أبو الجراح معقل بن سنان الأشجعي فشهد أن النبي "قضى في تزويج بروع بنت واشق الأشجعية بمثل ما قضيت"، رواه أبو داود والترمذي، وقال: حديث حسن صحيح رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۸/١] (مستخلص) والمتعة بالرفع عطف على قوله : "فلها مهر مثلها أي ولها المتعة وهذه المتعة واجبة عندنا، وقال مالك والليث وابن أبي ليلى: مستحبة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ حَقّاً عَلَى الْمُحْسِنِينَ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٦)، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَتَّعُوهُنَّ والأمر للوجوب، وقوله : وهي "درع أي المتعة ثلاثة أشياء، وهو مروي عن عائشة وابن عباس له ويعتبر في المتعة حال الزوجة، وهو قول الكرخي، وقيل: حال الزوج، وقال صاحب الهداية: هو الصحيح، وقيل: يعتبر بحالهما، حكاه صاحب "البدائع"، وعند الثلاثة: ما يقدره الحاكم، وعن أحمد أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة، ثم هي لا تزاد على نصف مهر المثل ولا تنقص عن خمسة دراهم، ولا تجب إلا إذا حصلت الفرقة من جهة الزوج كالطلاق والإيلاء وغيرها، وإن كانت الفرقة من جهة المرأة فلا تجب كردتها وإبائها عن الإسلام، وتقبيلها ابن الزوج بشهوة، والرضاع، وخيار البلوغ وخيار العتق وعدم الكفاءة. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۹/۱] هي قبل الوطء وقبل الخلوة أو فارقها بإيلاء أو لعان أو جبّ أو عنة أو إباء منه أو تقبيل ابنتها أو أمها بشهوة. (ط)
He did not specify it: the mahr (was left) without a valid specification or he remained silent about it. (T) He negated it: by marrying on the condition that there is no mahr for her. (T) Or she died: i.e., the woman without consummation, and likewise if she dies. Al-Shafi'i said: nothing is obligatory by the mere contract, but only by consummation, and by death according to some, because the mahr is her right, so she may negate it initially just as she may drop it finally. Our (Hanafi) position: The obligation of mahr is a right of the Shari'ah initially, so she cannot negate it; it becomes her right only finally, so she may acquit but not negate. We also have what 'Alqamah narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): that he was asked about a man who married a woman, then died without having fixed a dower for her and without having consummated, and he said: "I hold that she gets a dower like the dower of women of her standing, she inherits, and she must observe the waiting period." Then Abu al-Jarrah Ma'qil ibn Sinan al-Ashja'i stood and testified that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled in the marriage of Barwa' bint Washiq al-Ashja'iyyah the same as he had ruled. Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi, who said it is a hasan sahih hadith. (Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/208) (Mukhtasar) And al-mut'ah (is in the nominative) as a conjunction to his statement: "she gets mahr al-mithl" i.e., and she gets mut'a. This mut'a is obligatory in our school. Malik, al-Layth, and Ibn Abi Layla said: it is recommended (mustahabb) due to His statement: 'An obligation upon the doers of good' (Quran 2:236). Our proof is His statement: 'And provide for them' (the imperative indicates obligation), and His statement: she gets a garment, i.e., the mut'a consists of three items, which is narrated from 'A'ishah and Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). The status of the wife is considered in the mut'a; this is the view of al-Karkhi. It is said: the husband's status is considered. The author of al-Hidayah said: the correct view is that the husband's status is considered. It is said: both are considered, as reported by the author of al-Bada'i'. According to the three (Imams Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad), the judge assesses it. From Ahmad: the minimum for which prayer is valid. Then it (the mut'a) is not to exceed half of mahr al-mithl and not to be less than five dirhams. And it is not obligatory unless separation occurs from the husband's side, such as divorce, ila', etc. If separation is from the woman's side, it is not obligatory, such as her apostasy, her refusal to accept Islam, her kissing the husband's son with desire, suckling, option of puberty, option of emancipation, and lack of compatibility. [Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/209] She (is entitled to mut'a) before intercourse and before seclusion, or if he separated from her by ila', li'an, impotence, or his refusal, or his kissing her daughter or mother with desire. (T)
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the rulings on mahr when it is not specified or negated, and the obligation of mut'a (consolatory gift) upon divorce before consummation. The Hanafi position is that if no mahr is specified or it is negated, mahr al-mithl (like the dower of women of her status) becomes obligatory upon consummation or the death of either spouse. Upon divorce before consummation, the woman is entitled to mut'a, not mahr al-mithl. The Shafi'i school holds that nothing is owed merely by the contract; mahr is only obliged by consummation or death according to some. Their argument is that the mahr is the woman's right, so she can waive it initially. The Hanafi response is that the obligation of mahr is a divine right from the start, so she cannot negate it; she can only drop it after the contract. The Hanafis also cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud regarding the case of a woman whose husband died without specifying a dower; the Prophet's ruling was that she receives mahr al-mithl. Regarding mut'a, the Hanafis consider it obligatory (wajib) based on the imperative verse 'And provide for them' (Quran 2:236), whereas Malik, al-Layth, and Ibn Abi Layla consider it recommended (mustahabb) based on the verse calling it 'an obligation upon the doers of good,' suggesting a supererogatory act. The text further discusses the content of mut'a: it consists of three items (a garment, etc.), and the assessment takes into account the status of the wife or the husband, with the preferred view being the husband's status. Mut'a is restricted: it cannot exceed half of mahr al-mithl and cannot be less than five dirhams. It is only obligatory when separation originates from the husband (e.g., divorce, ila'), not from the wife (e.g., apostasy, refusal of Islam).

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a woman upon divorce before consummation when no mahr was specified.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of women similar to the bride in status, used when no valid dower is fixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is mut'a (consolatory gift) not obligatory upon divorce?
A) When the husband divorces before consummation
B) When the wife apostatizes, causing separation
C) When no mahr was specified in the contract
D) When the husband performs ila'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl upon consummation or death even if unspecified, and to wajib mut'a upon divorce before consummation.

Rulings on Mut'a, Mahr Increase, and Khalwah as Consummation
Rulings on mut'a, mahr increase, and khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on mut'a, post-contract mahr increase, and valid seclusion (khalwah), and evaluate the evidence for the equivalence of khalwah to intercourse.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a post-contract mahr increase does not halve, and valid seclusion obligates full mahr like intercourse.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers three interconnected issues: the components of mut'a, the effect of increasing mahr after the marriage contract, and the legal equivalence of valid seclusion to actual intercourse. The Hanafi school's positions are supported by distinct proofs and are contrasted with intra-school and cross-madhhab disagreements. Understanding these rulings is essential for correctly determining mahr obligations in marriage and divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
First, note the definition of mut'a (consolatory gift) as a shirt, head covering, and wrap. Second, the rule that a mahr increase after the contract does not halve upon divorce before consummation. Third, that valid seclusion (khalwah) obligates the full mahr, just like intercourse.
These are all part of a single passage.
2
Locate the Hanafi position and proof for each
For mahr increase, the Hanafi proof is that the spouses change the contract from loss to profit. For khalwah, the proof includes Quran 4:21, the hadith 'whoever uncovers the shirt...', and the consensus of Companions.
The proofs are dalil naqli (textual).
3
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on mahr increase
Abu Yusuf initially held that the increase halves, but later agreed with the majority. Zufar held the increase invalid. The relied-upon view is that the increase does not halve.
This shows development within the school.
4
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute on khalwah
The Shafi'i school holds that khalwah only obligates half mahr; full mahr requires intercourse. The Hanafi response interprets Quran 4:21 as referring to seclusion and cites hadith and consensus.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the amount of mahr due.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and conditions
The mufta bihi is that khalwah obligates full mahr, provided there are no physical, natural, or legal preventers. The increase does not halve, and mut'a is due when no mahr was specified.
The conditions for valid khalwah are detailed in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي درع وحمار وملحفة، وما فرض بعد العقد أو زيد لا يتنصف وصح حطّها، أي المتعة قميص مقنعة ط ط ط على المهر المسمي عند العقد والخلوة بلا مرض وحيضُ وإحرام وصوم فرض كالوطء بأحدهما مانع عن الوطء و نفاس أي بلا صوم وملحفة: بكسر الميم وهي ما تلتحف به من قرنها إلى قدمها رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۹/۱] بعد العقد: الخالي عن المهر سواء نفاه أو سكت عنه (ط) لا يتنصف: أي إن تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهراً أو نفاه أو تزوجها على مهر مسمى ثم زيد بعد ذلك، ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها لا يتنصف المفروض بعد العقد، ولا الذي زيد على المسمى، بل تجب المتعة في الأول ونصف المسمى عند العقد في الثاني، ويسقط الزائد، وكان أبو يوسف أولا يقول: يتنصف المفروض بعد العقد والزائد بعده وهو قول الشافعي في المفروض دون الزائد، لعدم صحة الزيادة عنده، وبه قال مالك ،وأحمد، وعن أبي يوسف أيضاً كقولهما؛ لأن هذا النكاح انعقد موجباً لمهر المثل، وهو لا يتنصف فكذا ما وقع تعييناً له، وقال زفر : ما يلزمه الزيادة؛ لأن الزيادة لا يمكن تصحيحاً مهراً؛ لأن المسمى صار في مقابلة البضع، فالزيادة لا يقابل شيئاً، ولنا أنهما يغيران العقد من صفة الخسران إلى صفة الربح، فلهما ذلك. (مستخلص، عيني) وصح حطها: أي حط المرأة من مهرها؛ لأنه خالص حقها، ولذلك إن حط الكل جاز، ولم يذكر المصنف جواز الزيادة؛ لأنه علم مما سبق ضمناً، وعند زفر والشافعي: لا تجوز الزيادة رمز الحقائق: ٢١٠/١] والخلوة الصحيحة في مكان يأمنان فيه من اطلاع الغير عليهما بلا إذنهما. (ط) وإحرام: أي بلا إحرام من أحدهما بحج فرض أو نفل أو عمرة. (ط) وصوم فرض: من أحدهما كرمضان، ولا يمنع صوم النفل والقضاء والمنذور في الصحيح، والصلاة كالصوم فرضها كفرضه ونفلها كنفله. (ط) كالوطء: أي الخلوة الصحيحة في وجوب المهر كاملاً حكمها كحكم الوطء عندنا، وعند الشافعي في الجديد: يجب نصف المهر، ولا يجب كمال المهر إلا بالوطء؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُوهُنَّ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ تَمَسُّوهُنَّ وَقَدْ فَرَضْتُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۷) (الآية) وهذا طلاق قبل المسيس، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكَيْفَ تَأْخُذُونَهُ وَقَدْ أَفْضَى بَعْضُكُمْ إِلَى بعض (النساء: ٢١) أي دخل في الفضاء وهو المكان الخالي، وقد سلمت البدل فيجب عليه كمال البدل، والخلوة قائمة مقام المسيس، فلا يكون طلاقاً قبل المسيس، وقال عليه: "من" كشف حمار امرأة ونظر إليها وجب الصداق دخل أو لم يدخل"، رواه الدار قطني، وحكى الطحاوي إجماع الصحابة في وجوب المهر بالخلوة، وشرط مالك طول المقام معها، وحده بالعام. ثم اعلم أن المانع ثلاثة أنواع :حسي وهو أن يكون معهما ثالث سواء كان بصيراً أو أعمى، يقظان أو نائماً، بالغاً أو صبياً يعقل لا المجنون والمغمى عليه والصغير الذي لا يعقل، وطبيعي ككون المرأة رتقاء أو قرناء أو صغيرة لا تطيق الجماع وشرعي: كالإحرام لحج فرض على ما ذكرنا، والحيض مانع طبعاً وشرعاً، ثم إنما تصح -
And it (mut'a) consists of a shirt, a head covering, and a wrap. (T) And what is prescribed after the contract or increased does not halve, and her reduction (of the mahr) is valid, i.e., the mut'a: a shirt, a head covering. (T) (T) (T) Upon the mahr specified at the contract. And valid seclusion (khalwah) without illness, menstruation, ihram, and obligatory fasting is like intercourse. With either (of these) preventing intercourse, and postpartum bleeding, i.e., without fasting. And 'milhafah' (wrap): with a kasra on the meem, and it is what she wraps from her head to her feet. (Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/209) After the contract: devoid of mahr, whether he negated it or remained silent. (T) It does not halve: i.e., if he married her without specifying a mahr for her, or negated it, or married her with a specified mahr then increased it after that, then divorced her before consummation, what is prescribed after the contract does not halve, nor does the increase on the specified amount. Rather, mut'a is obligatory in the first case, and half of the specified at the time of contract in the second, and the increase falls away. Abu Yusuf initially said: it halves—the prescribed after contract and the increase afterwards. And this is the saying of al-Shafi'i regarding the prescribed but not the increase, because the increase is not valid according to him. Malik and Ahmad also said this. And from Abu Yusuf also (a narration) like their view, because this marriage was contracted necessitating mahr al-mithl, and that does not halve, so likewise what occurs as its specification. Zufar said: the increase does not obligate him, because the increase cannot be validated as mahr since the specified amount is in exchange for the sexual enjoyment, so the increase does not correspond to anything. Our (Hanafi) proof: they (the spouses) change the contract from a state of loss to a state of profit, so they have that (right). The author did not mention the permissibility of increase, because it is understood implicitly from what preceded. According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, increase is not permissible. (T) And ihram: i.e., without ihram of either of them for obligatory or supererogatory Hajj or 'Umrah. (T) And obligatory fasting: of either of them, like Ramadan. And supererogatory fasting, make-up fasts, and vowed fasts do not prevent, according to the correct view. And prayer is like fasting: its obligatory is like its obligatory, its supererogatory like its supererogatory. (T) Like intercourse: i.e., valid seclusion in obligating the full mahr—its ruling is like the ruling of intercourse in our school. According to al-Shafi'i in the new (view), half the mahr is obligatory, and the full mahr is only obligatory by intercourse, due to His statement: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them and you have prescribed for them' (Quran 2:237)—and this divorce before touching. Our proof is His statement: 'And how can you take it while each of you has gone in unto the other' (Quran 4:21), i.e., entered into the empty space (al-fada'), which is the empty place. And since the compensation (mahr) has been handed over, the full compensation is incumbent. And khalwah stands in the place of touching (mass), so it is not a divorce before touching. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever uncovers the shirt of a woman and looks at her, the dower is obligatory, whether he entered or did not enter.' Reported by al-Daraqutni. And al-Tahawi reported the consensus of the Companions on the obligation of the mahr through khalwah. Malik conditioned a long stay with her, defined as a year. Then know that the preventers are of three types: physical: i.e., if there is a third with them, whether sighted or blind, awake or sleeping, adult or a child who comprehends—not the insane, unconscious, or a child who does not comprehend; natural: such as the woman being raqta' (with a barrier) or qarna' (with a growth) or too young to tolerate intercourse; and legal: such as ihram for obligatory Hajj as we mentioned, and menstruation is a preventer naturally and legally. Then it is only valid...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage covers multiple interconnected rulings. First, it defines the three items of mut'a (consolatory gift): a shirt (dir'), a head covering (qina'), and a wrap (milhafah). Then it addresses the ruling on mahr when it is increased or prescribed after the contract: if a man marries without specifying a mahr or with a specified mahr and then later increases it, and divorces before consummation, the post-contract additions do not halve. Instead, in the case of no specification, mut'a is due; in the case of a specified mahr with an increase, only half of the original specified amount is due, and the increase is dropped. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf initially held that the additions do halve, similar to the Shafi'i position on the prescribed amount, but later he reportedly agreed with the majority. Zufar held that the increase is not binding at all because it cannot be validated as part of the mahr. The Hanafi position is that the spouses can change the contract from loss to profit, so increases are valid. Next, the passage discusses khalwah sahihah (valid seclusion): it is defined as being alone in a place where they are safe from intrusion. It is equivalent to actual intercourse in obligating the full mahr upon divorce, provided there are no physical, natural, or legal preventers. This is a point of contention with the Shafi'i school, which holds that only intercourse obligates full mahr; khalwah only obligates half. The Hanafi proof includes the Quranic verse (4:21) referring to 'going in unto each other' interpreted as seclusion, a hadith from al-Daraqutni, and the reported Consensus of the Companions. The passage also details the three categories of preventers that invalidate khalwah: physical (presence of a third person of certain description), natural (e.g., the wife having a congenital barrier, being too young), and legal (e.g., ihram, menstruation, obligatory fasting).

Key Terms
الخلوة الصحيحة (al-khalwah al-sahihah): A valid seclusion between spouses in a private, secure place with no third party or legal/natural preventers, considered equivalent to intercourse in obligating full mahr.
المانع (al-mani'): A preventer that nullifies the effect of khalwah, categorized as physical, natural, or legal.
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman when no mahr was specified or when the marriage is dissolved before consummation. It typically consists of a shirt, head covering, and wrap.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a legal preventer (mani' shar'i) that invalidates khalwah according to the Hanafi school?
A) The presence of a sleeping third person
B) The wife being in ihram for Hajj
C) The husband having a non-obligatory fast
D) The wife being a minor who cannot bear intercourse

Key Takeaway
Valid khalwah is legally equivalent to intercourse in obligating the full mahr, and a post-contract mahr increase does not halve upon divorce before consummation.
