Post-Contract Mahr Increase and Wife’s Reduction
Ruling on whether post-contract mahr additions are halved and wife’s reduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that post-contract mahr additions do not become half upon divorce before consummation, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi positions.

Core Idea
A mahr increase after the marriage contract is valid but does not split on divorce before consummation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with a common scenario: what happens to the mahr (dower) when a husband adds to it after the wedding contract and then divorces before consummation? The Hanafi school has a well-defined answer that distinguishes between the original mahr and later changes. We will examine the ruling, the proof, and the internal disagreement within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the base matn ruling
Identify the key phrase 'la yatanaṣṣaf' (does not become half) and understand that the matn asserts post-contract mahr fixations and increases are not halved upon divorce before consummation.
This is the default Hanafi position.
2
Identify the disputed scenarios
Distinguish between three cases: (1) no mahr specified at contract, (2) mahr specified then increased post-contract, (3) wife reduces her mahr. The ruling differs for each.
Only the originally specified mahr is halved; later additions are dropped.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Note that Abu Yusuf initially held that post-contract fixations become half, but later retracted. This shows the evolution of the school's position.
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the proof for the Hanafi position
Understand the dalil 'they change the contract from loss to profit' – the spouses have authority to modify financial terms, so the increase is valid but not subject to halving.
This is istihsan based on spousal autonomy.
5
Contrast with Zufar’s view and opposing schools
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that post-contract increases are invalid because the original mahr already covers the vulva. The Hanafi response affirms the right to modify the contract.
The practical difference is the validity and splitting of the increase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ف س د وهي درع وخمار وملحفة، وما فرض بعد العقد أو زيد لا يتنصف وصح حطها، أي المتعة قميص مقنعة على المهر المسمى عند العقد والخلوة بلا مرض وحيض وإحرام وصوم فرض كالوطء بأحدهما مانع عن الوطء ونفاس أي بلا صوم وملحفة: بكسر الميم وهي ما تلتحف به من قرنها إلى قدمها رمز الحقائق: ۲۰۹/۱] بعد العقد: الخالي عن المهر سواء نفاه أو سكت عنه (ط) لا يتنصف: أي إن تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهراً أو نفاه أو تزوجها على مهر مسمى ثم زيد بعد ذلك، ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها لا يتنصف المفروض بعد العقد، ولا الذي زيد على المسمى، بل تجب المتعة في الأول ونصف المسمى عند العقد في الثاني، ويسقط الزائد، وكان أبو يوسف أولا يقول: يتنصف المفروض بعد العقد والزائد بعده وهو قول الشافعي في المفروض دون الزائد، لعدم صحة الزيادة عنده، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، وعن أبي يوسف أيضاً كقولهما؛ لأن هذا النكاح انعقد موجباً لمهر المثل، وهو لا يتنصف فكذا ما وقع تعييناً له، وقال زفر: ما يلزمه الزيادة؛ لأن الزيادة لا يمكن تصحيحاً مهراً؛ لأن المسمى صار في مقابلة البضع، فالزيادة لا يقابل شيئاً، ولنا أنهما يغيران العقد من صفة الخسران إلى صفة الربح، فلهما ذلك. (مستخلص، عيني) وصح حطها: أي حط المرأة من مهرها؛ لأنه خالص حقها، ولذلك إن حط الكل جاز، ولم يذكر المصنف جواز الزيادة؛ لأنه علم مما سبق ضمناً، وعند زفر والشافعي: لا تجوز الزيادة رمز الحقائق: ٢١٠/١]
Chapter on ... It is a shift, a veil, and a wrap. Whatever is fixed after the contract or increased does not become half, and her reduction of it is valid. That is, the mut'ah is a chemise, a headcover ... upon the specified dower at the time of contract. And seclusion without illness, menstruation, ihram, and obligatory fasting is like intercourse; by either of them it prevents intercourse, and puerperium meaning without fasting. And 'milhafah': with kasra on the meem, it is what she wraps from her head to her feet. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 209/1] 'After the contract': free from dower, whether he negated it or remained silent. 'Does not become half': meaning if he married her without specifying a dower, or negated it, or married her on a specified dower then increased after that, then divorced her before consummation, the dower fixed after the contract does not become half, nor does the increase on the specified one. Rather, the mut'ah is obligatory in the first case, and half of the specified dower at the time of contract in the second case, and the increase is dropped. Abu Yusuf initially said: the dower fixed after the contract becomes half, and the increase after it becomes half – and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i regarding the fixed one but not the increase, because according to him the increase is not valid. Malik and Ahmad said the same. And from Abu Yusuf also a narration like their view; because this marriage contract necessitates a dower of the like, which does not become half, so likewise what was determined as a specification for it. Zufar said: the increase is not incumbent upon him; because the increase cannot be valid as a dower; since the specified dower stands in exchange for the vulva, so the increase corresponds to nothing. And for us (Hanafis): they (the spouses) change the contract from the attribute of loss to the attribute of profit, so they have that right. (Mukhtalaf, Ayni) 'And her reduction of it is valid': meaning the wife's reduction of her dower; because it is her exclusive right. Therefore, if she reduces all of it, it is permissible. The author did not mention the permissibility of increase, because he learned it from what preceded implicitly. According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i: increase is not permissible. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 210/1]
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary. The topic is the effect of post-contract modifications to the mahr (dower) when divorce occurs before consummation. The base ruling states that anything fixed as mahr after the wedding contract, or an increase added after the original specification, does NOT become half when the wife is divorced before consummation. Instead, if no mahr was specified at all, the wife is entitled to mut'ah (a consolation gift). If a mahr was specified and then increased after the contract, upon divorce before consummation she gets only half of the originally specified mahr, and the increase is void. The commentary then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf initially agreed with the Shafi'i position that a post-contract mahr does become half, but later retracted and agreed with Abu Hanifa that it does not. Zufar held a stricter view: the increase is not even binding because the original mahr already covers the exchange. The Hanafi proof (istihsan) is that the spouses have the right to alter the contract from a loss-making situation to a profitable one, so both the post-contract fixation and the increase are valid but do not split. Additionally, the wife has the right to reduce (hitta) her own mahr since it is her exclusive right. She may remit part or all of it. Zufar and al-Shafi'i disallow increasing the mahr after the contract, but the Hanafi school permits it.

Key Terms
لا يتنصف (lā yatanaṣṣafu): It does not become half – referring to the mahr that is fixed or increased after the contract; upon divorce before consummation, it is not halved.
حطها (ḥāṭṭahā): The wife's reduction of her own mahr, whether partially or completely, which is valid because it is her exclusive right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband increases the mahr after the marriage contract and then divorces before consummation, what happens to the increase?
A) It is halved together with the original mahr
B) It is dropped entirely
C) It becomes part of the mut'ah
D) It is paid in full

Key Takeaway
Post-contract mahr additions are valid but do not split upon divorce before consummation; only the originally specified mahr is halved, and the wife may reduce her mahr at will.

Valid Seclusion (Khalwah) and Its Effect on Full Mahr
Conditions for valid khalwah and its equivalence to intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid khalwah, identify the three types of impediments, and explain why valid khalwah obligates full mahr in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Valid khalwah in a secure place with no impediments is legally equivalent to intercourse for obligating full mahr.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary establishes the Hanafi ruling on khalwah (seclusion) after marriage. You will learn what constitutes a valid khalwah, the conditions and impediments, and how the Hanafi school uses Quranic verses, hadith, and consensus to equate khalwah with actual intercourse for the purpose of full mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The matn states that valid khalwah is like intercourse in obligating full mahr. Note the conditions: no illness, menstruation, ihram, obligatory fasting.
These are the impediments that must be absent.
2
Understand the types of impediments
The passage categorizes impediments as sensory (third person), natural (physical in woman), and legal (ihram, fasting). Recognize each type and examples.
Each impediment nullifies the validity of khalwah.
3
Examine the place requirement
Valid khalwah requires a place secure from observation and intrusion. Note places that are valid (house, roof, tent) and invalid (mosque, main road, bathhouse).
Privacy is the essence of khalwah.
4
Analyze the proofs
The Hanafi school cites Quran 4:21 ('afḍā' interpreted as khalā'), hadith of the Prophet, and consensus of Companions. Understand how these prove equivalence.
These proofs have strong thubut but zanni dalala.
5
Contrast with other schools
Note the Shafi'i position (half mahr) and Maliki (requires a year). Understand the basis of ikhtilaf and the Hanafi tarjih.
The practical consequence is the amount of mahr owed.

Source Text

(ط) وإحرام: أي بلا إحرام من أحدهما بحج فرض أو نفل أو عمرة. (ط) وصوم فرض: من أحدهما كرمضان، ولا يمنع صوم النفل والقضاء والمنذور في الصحيح، والصلاة كالصوم فرضها كفرضه ونفلها كنفله. (ط) كالوطء: أي الخلوة الصحيحة في وجوب المهر كاملاً حكمها كحكم الوطء عندنا، وعند الشافعي في الجديد: يجب نصف المهر، ولا يجب كمال المهر إلا بالوطء؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ طَلَّقْتُمُوهُنَّ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ تَمَسُّوهُنَّ وَقَدْ فَرَضْتُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۳۷) وهذا طلاق قبل المسيس، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكَيْفَ تَأْخُذُونَهُ وَقَدْ أَفْضَى بَعْضُكُمْ إِلَى بعض﴾ (النساء: ٢١) أي دخل في الفضاء وهو المكان الخالي، وقد سلمت البدل فيجب عليه كمال البدل، والخلوة قائمة مقام المسيس، فلا يكون طلاقاً قبل المسيس، وقال عليه السلام: "من كشف حمار امرأة ونظر إليها وجب الصداق دخل أو لم يدخل"، رواه الدار قطني، وحكى الطحاوي إجماع الصحابة في وجوب المهر بالخلوة. وشرط مالك طول المقام معها، وحده بالعام. ثم اعلم أن المانع ثلاثة أنواع: حسي وهو أن يكون معهما ثالث سواء كان بصيراً أو أعمى، يقظان أو نائماً، بالغاً أو صبياً يعقل لا المجنون والمغمى عليه والصغير الذي لا يعقل، وطبيعي ككون المرأة رتقاء أو قرناء أو صغيرة لا تطيق الجماع، وشرعي: كالإحرام لحج فرض على ما ذكرنا، والحيض مانع طبعاً وشرعاً، ثم إنما تصح الخلوة إذا كانا في مكان يأمنان من اطلاع غيرهما عليهما أو تهجم كالدار والبيت ولا تصح في المسجد والطريق الأعظم والحمام والمفازة من غير خيمة، وكذا في الجبل، وفي البيت غير المسقف تصح، وكذا على سطح الدار. رمز الحقائق: ٢١٠/١]
And valid seclusion without illness, menstruation, ihram, and obligatory fasting is like intercourse; by either of these barriers intercourse is prevented, and puerperium, meaning without fasting. Valid seclusion is in a place where they are secure from being seen by others without their permission. (T) 'Ihram': meaning without one of them being in ihram for obligatory or supererogatory Hajj or 'Umrah. (T) 'Obligatory fasting': from one of them, like Ramadan; supererogatory fasting, make-up fasting, and vowed fasting are not preventative in the correct view. Prayer is like fasting; its obligatory is like its obligatory and its supererogatory like its supererogatory. (T) 'Like intercourse': meaning valid seclusion in obligating full mahr, its ruling is like the ruling of intercourse according to us (Hanafis). According to al-Shafi'i in the new view: half of the mahr is obligatory, and full mahr is not obligatory except by intercourse; due to His saying: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them and you have already specified for them...' (2:237) This is divorce before touching. And for us (Hanafis) His saying: 'And how could you take it while you have gone in unto each other?' (4:21) meaning he entered into the space, which is the empty place. And the consideration has been delivered, so full consideration is due upon him. And seclusion stands in the place of touching, so it is not divorce before touching. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever uncovers the veil of a woman and looks at her, the dower is obligatory, whether he entered or not,' narrated by al-Daraqutni. And al-Tahawi reported the consensus of the Companions on the obligation of mahr through seclusion. Malik conditioned a long stay with her, and defined it as a year. Then know that the impediments are of three types: sensory (Hissi) – that a third person is with them, whether sighted or blind, awake or asleep, adult or discerning child, but not the insane, unconscious, or non-discerning child; natural (Tabi'i) – like the woman being ra'ta' (vaginal obstruction) or qarna' (bony obstruction) or a minor unable to bear intercourse; and legal (Shar'i) – like ihram for obligatory Hajj as we mentioned, and menstruation as an impediment both naturally and legally. Then seclusion is only valid if they are in a place where they are secure from the sight of others or from intrusion, like a house or home, and it is not valid in a mosque, a major road, a bathhouse, or a desert without a tent. Similarly in a mountain. In a house without a roof it is valid, and likewise on the roof of a house. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 210/1]
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the conditions and ruling of khalwah (seclusion) in marriage. The matn states that valid seclusion—free from illness, menstruation, ihram, and obligatory fasting—is like actual intercourse in that it obligates the full mahr if divorce occurs afterward. The commentary details each condition and the impediments. The Hanafi position is that valid khalwah in a secure private place, with no third person present and no natural or legal impediment to intercourse, results in the full mahr becoming due, exactly as if actual intercourse had occurred. This is supported by the Qur'anic verse 'and how could you take it while you have gone in unto each other?' (4:21), which is interpreted as entering into the empty space (khalā'), and by a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) requiring the dower if a man uncovers a woman's veil. The passage contrasts this with the Shafi'i view that only half the mahr is due upon divorce after khalwah unless actual intercourse occurred. The Hanafi school bases its ruling on the consensus of the Companions as reported by al-Tahawi and on istihsan. Three types of impediments prevent valid khalwah: sensory (a third person), natural (physical impediments in the woman), and legal (ihram, fasting, etc.). Valid places for khalwah are those where the couple is secure from observation and intrusion, such as a house, a roof, or a tent in the desert, but not a mosque, main road, bathhouse, or open desert without a tent.

Key Terms
الخلوة الصحيحة (al-khalwah al-ṣaḥīḥah): Valid seclusion where the couple is alone in a place secure from observation and there are no impediments preventing intercourse.
مانع حسي (māniʿ ḥissī): Sensory impediment: the presence of a third person, even if blind, asleep, or a minor who understands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a husband divorces his wife immediately after a valid khalwah (without intercourse) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Half of the specified mahr is due
B) Full mahr is due
C) Only mut'ah is due
D) No mahr is due

Key Takeaway
Valid khalwah in Hanafi fiqh is treated as actual intercourse for the purpose of mahr and 'iddah, provided all conditions of seclusion and absence of impediments are met.

Khalwah with an Incapable Husband and 'Iddah Obligation
Ruling on khalwah with an incapable husband and 'iddah after invalid khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi on mahr after khalwah with a castrated husband and explain why 'iddah is obligatory even after invalid khalwah.

Core Idea
Even an invalid khalwah triggers 'iddah, but full mahr requires her submission and the possibility of intercourse.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two related rulings: the effect of khalwah (seclusion) with a husband who is incapable of intercourse due to castration (majbūb), impotence ('inīn), or being a eunuch (khaṣiyy), and the obligation of 'iddah after such a khalwah. On the first issue, there is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. The second issue extends the precautionary principle to protect lineage, even when the seclusion is legally defective. Mastering these rulings clarifies how the Hanafi school balances property rights (mahr) with social rights (lineage).

Guided Path
1
State the rule on mahr after khalwah with a majbūb
Identify Abu Hanifa's position: full mahr is due upon khalwah even with a castrated husband. The wife has submitted to the act (saḥq) and the possibility of lineage exists.
The text begins with 'ولو مجبوباً' indicating the ruling extends to castrated husbands.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that only half mahr is due, because the husband's incapacity is absolute, rendering khalwah invalid. They analogize to a sick person whose khalwah is invalid.
The Sahibayn use a qiyās (analogy) argument, while Abu Hanifa focuses on the wife's act of submission.
3
Analyze the reasoning of each side
Abu Hanifa: the wife has performed her duty; if a child is born, lineage is established, proving intercourse was possible. The Sahibayn: since intercourse is absolutely impossible, the khalwah has no effect; only half mahr as in invalid khalwah by a sick person.
The text gives the Sahibayn's analogy: 'لأن عجزه فوق عجز المريض' – his incapacity is greater than a sick person.
4
Determine the mufta bihi for mahr
The text follows Abu Hanifa's view ('وهذا عند الإمام') and considers it the relied position. For impotent and eunuch, there is consensus on full mahr.
The passage also notes that the preferred view on lineage is that if a child is born, lineage is established even if the husband is castrated.
5
Apply the same analysis to 'iddah
The text then moves to 'iddah: it is obligatory after any khalwah (valid or invalid) as a precaution to protect the rights of the Law and the child. This contrasts with mahr, which is property and thus requires valid khalwah.
There is a difference of opinion on 'iddah: if the impediment is real (e.g., minority), some say no 'iddah; but the mufta bihi is that 'iddah is always obligatory ('الأول أولى بالفتوى').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مجبوباً أو عتيناً أو خصياً وتجب العدة فيها، وتستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة دخل بها أو لم يدخل كاملاً بالخلوة أي على المرأة ولو مجبوباً من الجبب بمعنى القطع، وهو من قطع ذكره وخصيتاه، والمعنى أن المهر يجب الصحيحة ولو كان الزوج محبوباً، وهذا عند الإمام، وقالا إذا كان محبوباً وطلّق بعد الخلوة يجب عليه نصف المهر؛ لأن عجزه فوق عجز المريض؛ لأن الوطء متوقع من المريض بزوال مرضه ولا توقع في المحبوب أصلاً، فلما لم يصح خلوة المريض فلأن لا تصح خلوة المحبوب أولى، ولأبي حنيفة أن المستحق على المرأة التسليم في حق السحق وقد أتت به، ولو جاءت بولد ثبت نسبه واستحقت كمال المهر بالاتفاق، قيل: هذا إن علم أنه ينزل، وإن علم أنه لا ينزل لا يثبت النسب منه، والأول أحسن، وقوله: "أو عنيناً أو خصياً"; لأن الحكم يدار على سلامة الآلات وقد وجد، وقد يكون ذلك لمرض أو ضعف في خلقته أو كبر في سنه، وفي خلوة العنين والخصي يجب المهر الكامل بالاتفاق. (عيني ومستخلص وفتح) أو عنيناً: وهو الذي في آلته فتور. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] أو خصياً: الذي قلعت خصيتاه [رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] وهو وتجب العدة: أي تجب على المرأة العدة في جميع هذه المسائل في الطلاق بعد الخلوة سواء كانت الخلوة صحيحة أو فاسدة بالموانع المذكورة احتياطا؛ لتوهم الشغل؛ ولأن العدة حق الشرع والولد فلا يتصادقان في إبطال حق الغير، بخلاف المهر حيث لا يجب إلا إذا صحت الخلوة؛ لأنه مال فيحتاط في إيجابه، وقيل: إن كان المانع شرعيا تجب العدة؛ لثبوت التمكن حقيقة وإن كان حقيقيا كالمرض والصغر لا تجب العدة؛ لانعدام القدرة حقيقة والأول أولى بالفتوى
And even if (the husband is) castrated, or impotent, or a eunuch, and 'iddah is obligatory in her case, and mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman, whether he entered or not, fully by seclusion – i.e., upon the woman. Even if he is castrated (majbūb) from al-jabb meaning cutting, and he is one whose penis and testicles are cut. The meaning is that the mahr is obligatory fully even if the husband is castrated. This is with Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: if he is castrated and divorces after seclusion, half the mahr is obligatory upon him; because his incapacity is greater than that of a sick person; because intercourse may be expected from a sick person when his illness goes away, but from a castrated person there is no expectation at all. Therefore, just as the seclusion of a sick person is not valid, so the seclusion of a castrated person is more proper not to be valid. For Abu Hanifa: what is due from the woman is submission to the act of covering (saḥq), and she has done that. If she were to produce a child, his lineage would be established and she would deserve full mahr by agreement. It is said: this is if it is known that he emits semen; if it is known that he does not emit, then lineage from him is not established. The first is better. His saying: 'or impotent or eunuch'; because the ruling revolves around the integrity of the organs, and that has been found, and that may be due to illness or weakness in his constitution or advanced age. In the seclusion of the impotent and eunuch, full mahr is obligatory by consensus. (Ayni, Mustakhlas, Fath) 'Or impotent ('inīn)': he is one in whose organ there is flaccidity. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 211/1] 'Or eunuch (khaṣiyy)': one whose testicles have been removed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 211/1] And 'iddah is obligatory: meaning that 'iddah is obligatory upon the woman in all these cases in divorce after seclusion, whether the seclusion was valid or invalid due to the mentioned impediments, as a precaution; because a possibility of occupation (of the womb) is imagined; and because 'iddah is the right of the Law and of the child, so they cannot collude to invalidate the right of another. Unlike the mahr, which is only obligatory if seclusion is valid; because it is property, so caution is taken in imposing it. It is said: if the impediment is legal (shar'i), 'iddah is obligatory because actual possibility is established; if it is real (ḥaqīqī) like illness or minority, 'iddah is not obligatory because the ability is nonexistent in reality. The first is more worthy of fatwa.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage addresses two separate rulings: (1) the effect of khalwah with a husband who is incapable of intercourse due to castration (majbūb), impotence ('inīn), or being a eunuch (khaṣiyy), and (2) the obligation of 'iddah after khalwah. On the first issue, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that full mahr is due, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only half the mahr is due if the husband is castrated, because his incapacity is absolute and thus khalwah is not valid. Abu Hanifa's argument is that the wife has performed her duty of submission—she has made herself available—and if a child could possibly be born (if the husband emits), lineage would be established, proving the possibility of intercourse. For the impotent and eunuch, there is consensus that full mahr is due. On the second issue, 'iddah is obligatory even after an invalid khalwah (one with impediments), as a precaution to protect lineage and because 'iddah is a right of the Law and the child. This is in contrast to mahr, which only becomes obligatory with valid khalwah because it is a property right and caution is applied in imposing it. There is a difference of opinion whether 'iddah is obligatory when the impediment is real (like illness or minority); the preferred view (muftā bihi) is that it is obligatory regardless.

Key Terms
مجبوب (majbūb): A man whose penis and testicles have been cut; completely incapable of intercourse.
العدة (al-ʿiddah): The waiting period after divorce or death, imposed to ensure the womb is clear and to protect lineage.
عنين (ʿinīn): A man with flaccidity in his organ; impotent.
خصي (khaṣiyy): A man whose testicles have been removed; eunuch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, is 'iddah obligatory after a khalwah that was invalid due to the wife being a minor who cannot bear intercourse?
A) Yes, 'iddah is obligatory in all cases
B) No, 'iddah is not obligatory because there is no real possibility of pregnancy
C) Yes, but only if the husband is capable
D) No, 'iddah is only obligatory after valid khalwah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, full mahr is due after khalwah with any husband (including castrated) per Abu Hanifa, and 'iddah is obligatory after any khalwah as a precaution.

Mut'ah for Divorced Women: Four Categories and Rulings
Ruling on mut'ah for divorced women depending on their category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of divorced women regarding mut'ah and identify which category imposes an obligation (wajib) vs. recommendation (sunnah) based on the Qur'anic evidence.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is only obligatory for a divorced woman with no consummation and no mahr; for all others, it is a recommended act of piety.

The passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq initially says mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman. The commentary then refines this into four categories based on sexual consummation and mahr specification. Understanding which category triggers obligation versus recommendation requires careful attention to the two Qur'anic verses cited. This lesson will walk you through the classification and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
The commentary divides divorced women into four types based on two factors: consummation (or seclusion) and mahr specification.
2
Determine the ruling for each category
For category 1 (no consummation, no mahr), mut'ah is wajib. For categories 2-4, it is recommended (sunnah). Note that category 2 has a difference of opinion.
3
Examine the Qur'anic evidence
Verse 2:236 uses the imperative 'matti'ūhunna' which indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul. Verse 2:241 uses 'haqqan 'ala al-muttaqīn' which indicates recommendation because it addresses only the God-fearing.
4
Apply the principle: al-amr yufīdu al-wujūb
The imperative form in 2:236 makes the mut'ah obligatory. The absence of such imperative in 2:241 makes it recommended.
5
Note the exception: al-mufawwaḍah
The author excepts the mufawwadah (delegated mahr) from the general rule; her case is covered by a separate ruling (half of mahr al-mithl).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة دخل بها أو لم يدخل كاملاً بالخلوة أي على المرأة وتستحب المتعة: اعلم أن المطلقات أربعة مطلقة لم توطأ ولم يسم لها مهر فتجب لها المتعة، وهي التي ذكرها المصنف بالاستثناء إلا للمفوضة، ومطلقة لم توطأ وقد سمي لها مهر، وهي التي اختلف في استحباب المتعة لها، ومطلقة وطئت ولم يسم لها مهر ومطلقة وطئت وقد سمي لها مهر فهاتان يستحب لها المتعة والدليل على وجوب المتعة للأولى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَتِّعُوهُنَّ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٦) بصيغة الأمر، والأمر للوجوب، ودليل الاستحباب في حق غيرها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلْمُطَلَّقَاتِ مَتَاعٌ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ حَقًّا عَلَى الْمُتَّقِينَ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٤١) أي وللمطلقات التي لهن المهر متعة
And mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman, whether he entered or did not enter, fully by seclusion, i.e., upon the woman. And mut'ah is recommended: Know that divorced women are four types: (1) A woman who was not penetrated and no mahr was specified for her – mut'ah is obligatory for her. She is the one the author mentioned by exception except for the mufawwadah (delegated marriage). (2) A woman who was not penetrated but a mahr was specified for her – there is a difference of opinion regarding the recommendation of mut'ah for her. (3) A woman who was penetrated and no mahr was specified, and (4) a woman who was penetrated and a mahr was specified – for these two, mut'ah is recommended. The evidence for the obligation of mut'ah for the first is His statement: 'And give them a gift' (2:236) in the imperative form, and the imperative indicates obligation. The evidence for recommendation in the case of others is His statement: 'And for divorced women, a provision in kindness – a duty upon those who fear Allah' (2:241), i.e., for divorced women who had a mahr, mut'ah is a duty upon the pious.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on mut'ah (a post-divorce consolation gift) for different categories of divorced women. The matn initially states that mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman, but the commentary refines this into four categories based on whether the woman was touched (actual intercourse) and whether a mahr was specified. The first category (no consummation, no mahr) has obligatory mut'ah based on the imperative in verse 2:236. The second category (no consummation, but mahr specified) has a difference on recommendation. The third and fourth (consummation, with or without mahr) have recommended mut'ah based on verse 2:241, which addresses the muttaqīn (God-fearing). The Hanafi school holds that mut'ah is mandatory only for the first case; for others it is a recommended act of piety, not legally obligatory. The term 'mufawwadah' refers to a marriage where the mahr is delegated to be fixed later; the author excepts her from the general rule.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mutʿah): A post-divorce consolation gift given by the husband to the wife; its nature and amount vary by circumstance.
المفوضة (al-mufawwaḍah): A woman married without a specified mahr (tafwīḍ al-mahr), where the mahr is delegated to be fixed later. She is excepted from the general rule of mut'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A woman divorced before consummation with a specified mahr
C) A woman divorced before consummation without any mahr specified
D) A woman divorced after consummation without a mahr specified

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is obligatory only for a woman divorced before consummation without a mahr; for all other divorced women, it is a recommended act of piety.

Khilwah and Mahr for a Handicapped Husband
Ruling on full mahr despite husband's physical deficiency after valid seclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on full mahr after valid seclusion for a majbub husband and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion obligates full mahr even if the husband is permanently incapable — the wife's submission is what matters.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in nikah: what happens to the mahr when a husband with a permanent physical deficiency (majbub) has valid seclusion (khilwah) with his wife and then divorces? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa says full mahr is due, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say only half is due. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how khilwah functions as a legal substitute for intercourse and how the school resolves differences between its founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Valid seclusion (khilwah) between a husband and wife. The ruling: full mahr becomes obligatory? But note the condition: husband's physical state.
The matn states: 'ولو مجبوباً... يجب المهر الصحيح' meaning even if majbub, full mahr is obligatory according to Imam.
2
State the opposing positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: full mahr. Sahibayn: half mahr for majbub after khilwah. For 'innin and khasiy, all agree on full mahr.
The dispute is only for majbub, not for impotent or castrated.
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil)
Imam's proof: the wife has submitted (sallamat) and if a child is born, lineage is established, indicating consummation. Sahibayn's proof: qiyas from a sick person (marid) whose seclusion is invalid because incapacity is temporary; a majbub is permanently incapable, so even more invalid.
Sahibayn use an a fortiori argument (awlā).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if khilwah occurs and then divorce, under Imam, full mahr; under Sahibayn, half mahr for majbub. For 'innin and khasiy, full mahr by agreement.
This shows the difference matters in litigation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih
The commentator says 'al-awwal ahsan' (the first is better), i.e., Imam's view is preferred and is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah; Imam's position is stronger due to the wife's submission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو محبوباً أو عتيناً أو خصياً وتجب العدة فيها، وتستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة = أي على المرأة دخل بها أو لم يدخل كاملاً بالخلوة الخلوة إذا كانا في مكان يأمنان من اطلاع غيرهما عليهما أو تهجم والحيض مانع طبعاً وشرعاً، ثم إنما تصح الخلوة إذا كانا في مكان يأمنان من اطلاع غيرهما عليهما أو تهجم كالدار والبيت ولا تصح في المسجد والطريق الأعظم والحمام والمفازة من غير خيمة، وكذا في الجبل، وفي البيت غير المسقف تصح، وكذا على سطح الدار. رمز الحقائق: ٢١٠/١] ولو مجبوباً من الجبب بمعنى القطع، وهو من قطع ذكره وخصيتاه، والمعنى أن المهر يجب الصحيحة ولو كان الزوج محبوباً، وهذا عند الإمام، وقالا إذا كان محبوباً وطلّق بعد الخلوة يجب عليه نصف المهر؛ لأن عجزه فوق عجز المريض؛ لأن الوطء متوقع من المريض بزوال مرضه ولا توقع في المحبوب أصلاً، فلما لم يصح خلوة المريض فلأن لا تصح خلوة المحبوب ،أولى، ولأبي حنيفة أن المستحق على المرأة التسليم في حق السحق وقد أتت به، ولو جاءت بولد ثبت نسبه واستحقت كمال المهر بالاتفاق، قيل: هذا إن علم أنه ينزل، وإن علم أنه لا ينزل لا يثبت النسب منه، والأول أحسن، وقوله: "أو عنينا أو خصياً"؛ لأن الحكم يدار على سلامة الآلات وقد وجد، وقد يكون ذلك لمرض أو ضعف في خلقته أو كبر في سنه، وفي خلوة العنين والخصي يجب المهر الكامل بالاتفاق. عيني ومستخلص وفتح) أو عنيناً : وهو الذي في آلته فتور. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] أو خصياً : الذي قلعت خصيتاه رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] وهو
And even if (the husband is) amputated or impotent or castrated, and the waiting period is obligatory in it, and consolatory gift is recommended for every divorced woman. = Meaning upon the woman, whether he entered or not, complete by seclusion. Seclusion is when they are in a place where they are safe from others' sight or intrusion, and menstruation is a natural and legal barrier. Then seclusion is valid only if they are in a place safe from others' sight or intrusion, like a house or room, and is not valid in a mosque, main road, bathhouse, or desert without a tent, and likewise on a mountain, and in an uncovered house it is valid, and likewise on a roof. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/210] And even if (the husband is) amputated (majbub) from al-jabb meaning cutting, and he is one whose penis and testicles are cut off. The meaning is that the full dower is obligatory even if the husband is amputated, and this is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If he is amputated and divorces after seclusion, half the dower is obligatory upon him, because his incapacity is greater than that of a sick person, because intercourse is expected from a sick person with the removal of his illness, but there is no expectation from an amputated person at all. Since the seclusion of a sick person is not valid, then the seclusion of an amputated person is even more not valid. And for Abu Hanifa is that what is due from the woman is submission in terms of intercourse and she has performed it. And if she gives birth to a child, his lineage is established and she deserves full dower by agreement. It is said: This is if it is known that he emits (semen); if it is known that he does not emit, lineage is not established from him, and the first is better. And His statement: "or impotent or castrated" because the ruling revolves around the soundness of organs, and it exists, and that may be due to illness or weakness in creation or old age. And in the seclusion of an impotent or castrated man, full dower is obligatory by agreement. ('Ayni, Mustakhlas, and Fath) Or impotent ('innin): he whose organ has weakness. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] Or castrated (khasiy): he whose testicles are removed. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] And he is
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the effect of valid seclusion (khilwah) on the obligation of the full dower (mahr) when the husband has a physical deficiency preventing intercourse. The matn states the ruling, and the sharh explains the conditions of valid seclusion and then the dispute. The passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute. The author first defines valid seclusion, listing places where it is valid and invalid. Then he addresses three types of husbands: majbub (amputated), 'innin (impotent), and khasiy (castrated). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, even if the husband is majbub, valid seclusion obligates the full mahr, because the wife has fulfilled her duty of submission. The two associates (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that seclusion is not valid for a majbub since he is permanently incapable, so only half mahr is due, similar to divorce before seclusion. However, Abu Hanifa reasons that the wife has enabled intercourse, and if a child is born, lineage is established, proving consummation. For 'innin and khasiy, all agree that full mahr is due after seclusion. This lesson teaches the Hanafi principle that khilwah substitutes for actual intercourse in certain legal effects, and the intra-madhhab difference in its application to permanent incapacities.

Key Terms
خلوة (khilwah): Valid seclusion between husband and wife in a private place where they are safe from intrusion, which legally substitutes for actual intercourse in certain effects.
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis and testicles are cut off, permanently incapable of intercourse.
مهر (mahr): The bridal gift (dower) obligatory upon the husband to the wife, whether specified or default (mahr al-mithl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the mahr obligation if a majbub husband divorces his wife after valid seclusion?
A) No mahr because seclusion is invalid
B) Half mahr
C) Full mahr
D) Mahr al-mithl only

Key Takeaway
Valid seclusion obligates full mahr for all husbands, including majbub, according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Obligation of 'Iddah after Valid or Invalid Seclusion
Ruling on 'iddah after valid or invalid seclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that 'iddah is wajib after any seclusion (valid or invalid) and explain why it differs from mahr, citing the principle of ihtiyat.

Core Idea
'Iddah is obligatory after any seclusion because it is a right of Allah and the child, not a financial right like mahr.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, as explained in Ramz al-Haqa'iq, establishes a key Hanafi principle: 'iddah (waiting period) is obligatory after divorce if the marriage was consummated through valid seclusion (khilwah sahihah) or even invalid seclusion (khilwah fasidah). The ruling is based on caution (ihtiyat) to protect lineage and the rights of the Shari'ah. In contrast, the dower (mahr) is only obligatory after valid seclusion because it is a financial right. The passage also lists the effects where valid seclusion substitutes for actual intercourse and notes the Shafi'i disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is 'iddah after divorce following seclusion. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
'Iddah is the waiting period; here the obligation arises after any seclusion, not just intercourse.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil) for obligation
The text gives two reasons: (1) precaution due to possibility of pregnancy (توهم الشغل), and (2) 'iddah is a right of Allah and the child, so the spouses cannot agree to nullify it.
This contrasts with mahr, which is a financial right (right of the wife) and requires caution only when seclusion is valid.
3
Distinguish between legal and physical barriers
If the seclusion barrier is legal (e.g., fasting, ihram), 'iddah is obligatory because there was still real ability. If the barrier is physical (e.g., illness, young age), some say no 'iddah, but the preferred view is that it is still obligatory.
The phrase 'al-awwal awla bil-fatwa' indicates the first opinion (obligation in all cases) is mufta bihi.
4
List the effects where valid seclusion substitutes for intercourse
Our companions (أصحابنا) established valid seclusion as equivalent to intercourse in nine matters (confirmation of mahr, lineage, 'iddah, maintenance, prohibition of marrying sister, etc.) and not in five matters (ihsan, prohibition of daughters, etc.).
This shows the comprehensive nature of the Hanafi position on khilwah.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i does not require 'iddah after mere seclusion without actual intercourse. The Hanafi school responds with the precaution principle and the right of the child.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is taken for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتجب العدة: أي تجب على المرأة العدة في جميع هذه المسائل في الطلاق بعد الخلوة سواء كانت الخلوة صحيحة أو فاسدة بالموانع المذكورة احتياطا؛ لتوهم الشغل؛ ولأن العدة حق الشرع والولد فلا يتصادقان في إبطال حق الغير، بخلاف المهر حيث لا يجب إلا إذا صحت الخلوة؛ لأنه مال فيحتاط في إيجابه، وقيل: إن كان المانع شرعيا تجب العدة؛ لثبوت التمكن حقيقة وإن كان حقيقيا كالمرض والصغر لا تجب العدة؛ لانعدام القدرة حقيقة والأول أولى بالفتوى ثم اعلم أن أصحابنا أقاموا الخلوة الصحيحة بمقام الوطء في موا مواضع وهي : تأكد المهر، وثبوت النسب، والعدة والنفقة والسكنى في هذه العدة، ونكاح أختها وأربع سواها، وحرمة نكاح ا الأمة، ومراعاة وقت الطلاق في حقها، ولم يقيموها في مواضع وهي حق الإحصان وحرمة ،البنات وحلها للأول، والرجعة، والميراث، وعند الشافعي: لا تجب العدة في الخلوة رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۱/۱] (مستخلص)
And the waiting period is obligatory: i.e., it is obligatory upon the woman in all these cases in divorce after seclusion, whether the seclusion was valid or invalid due to the mentioned barriers, as a precaution due to the possibility of occupation (with pregnancy); and because the waiting period is a right of Allah and of the child, so they cannot mutually agree to nullify the right of a third party, contrary to the dower where it is not obligatory unless seclusion is valid, because it is property so caution is taken in imposing it. And it is said: if the barrier is legal (shar'i), the waiting period is obligatory due to the proven ability in reality; if it is physical like illness or childhood, the waiting period is not obligatory due to the lack of ability in reality. And the first is worthier for fatwa. Then know that our companions established valid seclusion as equivalent to intercourse in several places: confirmation of dower, establishment of lineage, waiting period, maintenance and housing during this waiting period, prohibition of marrying her sister and four others, prohibition of marrying a slave-girl, and observance of the time of divorce in her right. And they did not establish it in other places: the right of ihsan (for stoning), prohibition of his daughters, her becoming lawful for the first husband, return (raj'ah), and inheritance. And according to al-Shafi'i, the waiting period is not obligatory in seclusion. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage clarifies the obligation of 'iddah (waiting period) after divorce that follows any form of seclusion, whether the seclusion was valid or invalid due to a barrier (like menstruation). The principle is that 'iddah is a right of Allah and the potential child, so it cannot be waived by the spouses' agreement. The text distinguishes between legal barriers (e.g., fasting, ihram) where 'iddah is still obligatory, and physical barriers (e.g., illness, young age) where some scholars say 'iddah is not required, but the preferred opinion is that it is obligatory anyway. The passage then lists nine effects where valid seclusion substitutes for actual intercourse, and five where it does not. It also notes that Imam al-Shafi'i does not require 'iddah after mere seclusion. This shows the Hanafi approach of caution (ihtiyat) in matters of lineage and Shari'ah rights.

Key Terms
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying, to ensure no pregnancy.
خلوة فاسدة (khilwah fasidah): Seclusion that is legally invalid due to a barrier, yet still triggers 'iddah as a precaution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the husband may have had intercourse secretly
B) Because it is a precaution to protect lineage and the rights of Shari'ah
C) Because the wife is still under the husband's authority
D) Because invalid seclusion is equivalent to valid seclusion in all effects

Key Takeaway
'Iddah is wajib after any seclusion (valid or invalid) as a precaution because it is a right of Allah and the potential child, not a financial right like mahr.

Classification and Ruling of Mut'ah for Divorced Women
Ruling on consolatory gift for divorced women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify divorced women into four categories and state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah (wajib, mustahabb, sunnah, or not recommended) for each, citing the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib only for the mufawwidah divorced before consummation; for others it is recommended or not needed.

Mut'ah (consolatory gift) is a means of comforting a divorced woman, but its obligation varies. The Hanafi school, drawing from two Quranic verses, establishes a precise classification based on whether the marriage was consummated and whether a dower was specified. This lesson unpacks that classification, the evidence, and the nuance provided by later scholars like al-'Ayni. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly advising on post-divorce rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Categories
From the passage, list the four categories of divorced women based on two factors: whether consummation occurred and whether a dower was specified.
Use the text's dichotomy of 'not touched' vs 'touched' and 'no mahr specified' vs 'mahr specified'.
2
Determine the Ruling for Each Category
For each category, state the ruling on mut'ah: wajib, mustahabb, sunnah, or not recommended.
Note that the third and fourth categories both involve consummation; the difference is in the presence of a specified mahr affecting the degree of recommendation.
3
Analyze the Quranic Evidence
Examine the two Quranic verses (2:236 and 2:241) and explain how each supports the ruling for the respective categories.
The imperative in 2:236 indicates wujub for the first category; the phrase 'duty upon the righteous' in 2:241 indicates recommendation.
4
Understand al-'Ayni's Refinement
Al-'Ayni adds a fourth category: divorced before consummation with specified mahr – here mut'ah is not recommended because half the mahr suffices.
Al-'Ayni's classification refines the initial two categories into four, clarifying the exceptions.
5
Define 'Mufawwidah'
Define the term 'mufawwidah' and explain its relevance to the obligation of mut'ah.
She is the woman who marries without a specified dower; she is the subject of the first category before consummation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتستحب المتعة : اعلم أن المطلقات أربعة مطلقة لم توطأ ولم يسم لها مهر فتجب لها المتعة، وهي التي ذكرها المصنف بالاستثناء إلا للمفوضة، ومطلقة لم توطأ وقد سمي لها مهر، وهي التي اختلف في استحباب المتعة لها، ومطلقة وطئت ولم يسم لها مهر ومطلقة وطئت وقد سمي لها مهر فهاتان يستحب لها المتعة والدليل على وجوب المتعة للأولى قوله تعالى: وَمَتَّعُوهُنَّ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٣٦) بصيغة الأمر، والأمر للوجوب، ودليل الاستحباب في حق غيرها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلْمُطَلَّقَاتِ مَتَاعٌ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ حَقًّا عَلَى الْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٤١) أي وللمطلقات التي لهن المهر متعة = سمي أيضاً بطريق الاستحباب حقاً على . كان متقياً، فليس هذا بواجب، لكن من شروط التقوى التبرع بهذه تطييباً من لقلوبهن، كذا في "المستخلص" و"الفتح"، وقال العيني: المتعة على أربعة أقسام : واجبة للمفوضة، ومستحبة: للمرأة التي طلقها بعد الدخول ولم يسم لها مهراً، وسنة للتي طلقها بعد الدخول وقد سمي لها مهراً؛ لأنه أوحشها بالطلاق بعد ما سلمت إليه البضع فيسن أن يعطيها شيئاً زائداً على الواجب والرابعة ليست بواجبة ولا سنة ولا مستحبة للتي طلقها قبل الدخول وقد سمي لها مهراً؛ لأن نصف المهر قام في حقها مقام المتعة. [رمز الحقائق: ٢١١/١] للمفوضة بكسر الواو وهي التي فوضت نفسها إلى زوجها يعني زوجها منه بلا مهر. (ع) الوطء: أي إذا طلقت المرأة المفوضة قبل الوطء تجب لها المتعة. (ع)
And the consolatory gift is recommended. Know that divorced women are four: A woman who has not been touched nor a dower specified for her, so mut'ah is obligatory for her, and she is the one the author mentioned by exception except for the mufawwidah. And a woman who has not been touched but a dower was specified for her, and there is dispute about the recommendation of mut'ah for her. And a woman who has been touched but no dower was specified for her, and a woman who has been touched and a dower was specified for her, so for these two mut'ah is recommended. The evidence for the obligation of mut'ah for the first is His statement: 'And give them a gift [of compensation]' (al-Baqarah 2:236) in the imperative form, and the imperative indicates obligation. And the evidence for recommendation for others is His statement: 'And for divorced women is a provision according to what is acceptable, a duty upon the righteous' (al-Baqarah 2:241), meaning for divorced women who have a dower, mut'ah is also by way of recommendation, a duty upon the righteous. So this is not obligatory, but from the conditions of righteousness is to donate this to soothe their hearts. This is in al-Mustakhlas and al-Fath. And al-'Ayni said: Mut'ah has four categories: obligatory for the mufawwidah, recommended for the woman who is divorced after consummation without a specified dower, sunnah for the one divorced after consummation with a specified dower because he has saddened her by divorce after she surrendered the private part to him, so it is sunnah for him to give her something extra beyond the obligatory, and the fourth is neither obligatory nor sunnah nor recommended for the woman divorced before consummation with a specified dower, because half the dower stands in place of mut'ah for her. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/211] Mufawwidah: with kasra on the waw, she who delegated herself to her husband, meaning he married her without a dower. (Ayni) Before intercourse: meaning if the mufawwidah woman is divorced before intercourse, mut'ah is obligatory for her. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage classifies divorced women into four categories regarding the ruling on mut'ah (consolatory gift). It is a ruling statement with textual proof from the Quran. The first category is a woman divorced before consummation without a specified mahr: mut'ah is wajib (obligatory) based on the imperative in Quran 2:236. The second is a woman divorced before consummation with a specified mahr: there is ikhtilaf on recommendation. The third and fourth are women divorced after consummation (with or without specified mahr): mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) based on Quran 2:241, which describes it as a duty upon the righteous, not an absolute obligation. Then the text quotes al-'Ayni's more detailed classification: (1) wajib for mufawwidah (woman married without mahr), (2) mustahabb for those divorced after consummation without specified mahr, (3) sunnah for those divorced after consummation with specified mahr (as extra comfort), and (4) not recommended for those divorced before consummation with specified mahr, because half the mahr already serves as consolation. The mufawwidah is defined as a woman who delegates herself to her husband without a dower; if she is divorced before consummation, mut'ah is wajib.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given by the husband to a divorced woman to comfort her, varying in obligation depending on circumstances.
مفوضة (mufawwidah): A woman who marries without a specified dower, delegating the dower to her husband's discretion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) A woman divorced after consummation without a specified mahr
D) A woman divorced before consummation with a specified mahr

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is wajib only for the mufawwidah (no mahr, divorced before consummation); otherwise it is recommended or not needed.

Ruling on Shighar Marriage and Mahr al-Mithl
Inter-madhhab dispute on shighar marriage validity and mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shighar marriage and explain why mahr al-mithl is obligatory.

Core Idea
Shighar marriage is valid in Hanafi school, but each wife receives mahr al-mithl.

Shighar marriage involves two men exchanging daughters or sisters without a monetary dower, each woman's private part serving as dower for the other. This practice was common in pre-Islamic times. The Hanafi school holds that the marriage contracts are valid, but the condition of exchanging private parts as dower is invalid, so each wife is entitled to a customary dower (mahr al-mithl). The Shafi'i school, based on a hadith prohibition, considers such marriages invalid. In this lesson, we examine the arguments behind the Hanafi position and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, understand what the Hanafi school rules: both marriage contracts are valid, but each woman gets mahr al-mithl because the specified 'dower' (the other woman) is not valid property.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i school declares the contracts invalid (batil). Their proof is the hadith forbidding shighar and the reasoning that half the private part is made dower and half is the object of marriage – an impossible scenario.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith
The Hanafi school interprets the prohibition as either referring to the pre-Islamic custom where no dower at all was given, or as indicating karahah (dislike) rather than outright prohibition (tahrim).
They rely on the principle that marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions.
4
Examine the Hanafi legal analogy (qiyas)
The Hanafi school draws an analogy with cases where a non-property item (like blood or pig) is specified as dower: the marriage remains valid, and mahr al-mithl is due. Similarly, here the specified dower is invalid but the marriage stands.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi, the marriages are valid and each wife gets mahr al-mithl. In Shafi'i, the marriages are void and must be annulled. This affects whether any dower is due or only mahr al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الشغار [ أي في نكاح الشغار وهو أن يزوج الرجل بنته أو أخته على أن يزوجه الآخر بنته أو أخته على أن يكون بضع كل واحدة منهما صداقا للأخرى فالعقدان جائزان ويجب مهر المثل لكل منهما. (ط)] في الصحاح يقال : شغر الكلب إذا رفع إحدى رجليه للبول، وسمي هذا العقد به؛ لأنهما بهذا الشرط كأنهما رفعا المهر وأخليا ،البضع أو مأخوذ من قولهم بلدة شاغرة أي خالية، والمراد أن يكون في العقدين بضع كل واحدة منهما صداقا للأخرى ولا يكون المهر فيهما سوى هذا، فالعقدان جائزان عندنا، ويجب لكل منهما مهر المثل، وقال الشافعي: يبطل العقدان؛ لحديث نافع عن ابن عمر لما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن الشغار وليس بينهما صداق"، رواه الجماعة وعن عبد بن عمر لهما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا شغار في الإسلام"، رواه مسلم؛ ولأنه جعل نصف البضع مهراً والنصف منكوحاً، ولا اشتراك في هذا الباب فيبطل به الإيجاب. الله ولنا أن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة ألا ترى أنه لا يفسد بتسمية ما ليس بمال كالدم والخنزير ولا بترك التسمية بالكلية، والنهي الوارد فيه إنما كان من أجل إخلائه عن تسمية المهر من غير أن يجب فيه شيء آخر على ما كانت عليه عادتهم في الجاهلية أو هو محمول على الكراهة ولا وجه لجعله نصف البضع مهرا والنصف منكوحا؛ لأنه لم يجتمع النكاح والصداق في بضع واحد؛ لعدم صلاحية البضع صداقاً، فلا يتصور الاشتراك مع عدم الاستحقاق فيجب مهر المثل؛ لأنه سمي ما لا يصلح مهرا، وأجمعوا أنه لو قال: زوجتك ابنتي على أن تزوجني ابنتك، ولم يقل: على أن يكون بضع كل واحدة منهما صداقاً للأخرى جاز النكاح ولا يكون شغاراً، ويجب مهر المثل أيضاً. (عيني، فتح)
On shighar: meaning the marriage of shighar, which is that a man marries his daughter or sister to another on condition that the other marries his daughter or sister to him, such that the private part of each one is the dower for the other. Both contracts are valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory for each. (Tahawi) In al-Sihah it is said: 'shaghara' the dog when he raises one leg to urinate, and this contract is named thus because with this condition it is as if they have raised the dower and vacated the private part; or it is taken from their saying 'baldah shaghirah' meaning empty. The intent is that in both contracts the private part of each woman is the dower for the other, and there is no dower besides this. So both contracts are valid according to us, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory for each. Al-Shafi'i said: Both contracts are invalid due to the hadith of Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ forbade shighar and there is no dower between them, narrated by the group (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.), and from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar from the Prophet ﷺ: 'No shighar in Islam', narrated by Muslim; and because he made half the private part as dower and half as the object of marriage, and there is no partnership in this chapter, so the offer is invalid. And our evidence is that marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions; do you not see that it is not invalidated by specifying something that is not property like blood or pig, nor by leaving specification entirely. The prohibition mentioned is only due to its being devoid of specifying a dower without anything else being obligated, as was their custom in pre-Islamic times, or it is interpreted as makruh. And there is no basis for making half the private part as dower and half as the object of marriage, because marriage and dower are not combined in a single private part, due to the private part not being suitable as dower. So partnership is not conceivable along with lack of entitlement; thus mahr al-mithl is obligatory because something that is not suitable as dower was specified. And all agree that if he said: 'I marry my daughter to you on condition that you marry your daughter to me', and did not say 'such that the private part of each is the dower for the other', the marriage is valid and it is not shighar, and mahr al-mithl is also obligatory. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage addresses the shighar marriage, where two men exchange daughters/sisters in marriage with each other's private parts as dower. It is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i. The Hanafi school holds that such contracts are valid (ja'iz), but each woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the customary dower) because the specified 'dower' (the right to marry the other woman) is not valid as property. The Shafi'i school declares the contracts invalid (batil) based on hadith forbidding shighar and the reasoning that it involves half the private part being dower and half being the object of sale, which is impossible. The Hanafi response argues that marriage is not invalidated by a corrupt condition; the prohibition is about avoiding the absence of a real dower, but here mahr al-mithl is still due, so the contracts are valid. The lesson highlights the Hanafi principle that marriage contracts are valid unless a core pillar is violated, and corrupt conditions can be removed by substituting mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms
شغار (shighar): A marriage contract where two men exchange daughters or sisters with each other's private parts as dower, i.e., no monetary dower is specified.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary dower of a woman similar to the one being married, determined by her family status, age, beauty, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a shighar marriage contract?
A) The contract is invalid (batil) and must be annulled
B) The contract is valid but each wife gets half the specified mahr
C) The contract is valid and each wife gets mahr al-mithl
D) The contract is valid but only the first wife gets mahr

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, shighar marriage is valid and the wives are entitled to mahr al-mithl, illustrating the principle that marriage is not nullified by corrupt conditions.

Marriage with Condition of Husband's Service: Mahr Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on service as mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when marriage is contracted on condition of husband's service and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between the two shaykhs and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Service is not property; it cannot be mahr; the wife gets mahr al-mithl.

When a marriage contract includes a condition that the husband will serve his wife for a specified period instead of paying a dower, a key question arises: can service be considered valid property (mal) for mahr? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. This lesson examines the positions of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the basis for the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Condition
Consider the scenario: a man marries a woman on the condition that he serves her for one year. What is the legal effect on the mahr obligation?
The condition is specified in place of a monetary dower.
2
Determine the Dispute
Recognize that the dispute is about the nature of service: is it property (mal) that can serve as mahr, or not? The two shaykhs say no; Muhammad says yes.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the three main students.
3
Analyze Each Position's Proof
For the two shaykhs: service is not property (ghayr mal), so the specified condition is invalid, and mahr al-mithl is wajib. For Muhammad: service is property (because it has value) but the husband cannot deliver it fully, so the value of the service is due.
The text also alludes to a qiyas argument comparing service to something else, but it is truncated.
4
Identify the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the two shaykhs: mahr al-mithl is obligatory. This is because the condition of service is void, and the wife is entitled to the mahr like women of her status.
The text implies preference for the two shaykhs by stating their view first.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a marriage contract includes a condition that the husband will serve his wife (e.g., work as a servant) for a specified period in lieu of mahr. It presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the specified service is not property (mal), so it is invalid as dower, and thus mahr al-mithl is wajib. Muhammad al-Shaybani says that the service is property (since it has value) but the husband is incapable of delivering it because it would turn him into a slave-like figure; so the value of the service must be given. Then the text mentions 'the three' (all of them) saying that service is 'loved' (perhaps meaning it is valid? The OCR is unclear). The last part seems cut off, but the gist is that there is disagreement on whether service can be a valid mahr. The relied-upon view (the two shaykhs) is that mahr al-mithl is obligatory because service is not property suitable as mahr. This shows the Hanafi requirement that mahr must be property (mal) with value and deliverable.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): Service (e.g., manual labor) specified as a condition in a marriage contract in lieu of dower.
غير مال (ghayr mal): Not considered property in Islamic law; thus cannot be used as dower.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of women similar to the wife in social status, age, beauty, etc., used when no mahr is specified or when the specified mahr is invalid.

In Hanafi fiqh, service cannot be mahr because it is not property; the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

The Four Categories of Mut'ah in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines mut'ah and its four categories with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of mut'ah and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine which category applies to a given divorce scenario.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib only for the mufawwidah divorced before consummation; otherwise it is recommended, sunnah, or not required.

In Hanafi marriage law, a woman divorced may receive a consolatory gift called mut'ah. However, not every divorce entitles her to it. Imam al-Ayni's classification from Fath al-Qadir divides mut'ah into four distinct categories based on the presence of dower specification and the timing of divorce. This lesson unpacks that classification and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
Based on two variables: dower specified (mahr) or not, and divorce before or after consummation. List all four combinations.
The mufawwidah is the woman married without dower specification.
2
Determine the hukm for each scenario
From al-Ayni: wajib for mufawwidah before consummation; mustahabb for no dower after consummation; sunnah for dower after consummation; none for dower before consummation.
Half the dower already compensates in the last case.
3
Understand the rationale
Why is mut'ah sunnah in one case and not required in another? The pain of divorce after intimacy is greater, so extra gift is encouraged; but half dower suffices if divorce occurred before consummation with dower.
4
Define mufawwidah
Linguistically and legally: a woman who delegates herself to her husband without a specified mahr.
Kasra on the waw: mufawwidah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[رمز الحقائق: ٢١١/١] للمفوضة بكسر الواو وهي التي فوضت نفسها إلى زوجها يعني زوجها منه بلا مهر. (ع) الوطء: أي إذا طلقت المرأة المفوضة قبل الوطء تجب لها المتعة. (ع)
And the mut'ah (consolatory gift) is for the mufawwidah (woman married without dower) before intercourse. And it is obligatory to give the dower of the like in shighar and the service of a free husband for the dower. Also by way of recommendation truly upon... He was God-fearing, so this is not obligatory, but among the conditions of piety is to donate this to please their hearts. Thus in al-Mustakhlas and al-Fath. And al-Ayni said: Mut'ah is of four types: obligatory for the mufawwidah, recommended for the woman divorced after consummation without dower specification, Sunnah for the one divorced after consummation with dower specification because he caused her pain by divorce after she surrendered the vulva, so it is Sunnah to give her something extra beyond the obligatory, and the fourth is neither obligatory nor Sunnah nor recommended for the one divorced before consummation with dower specification because half the dower takes the place of mut'ah. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 211/1] For the mufawwidah with kasra of the waw, she is the one who delegated herself to her husband, meaning he married her without dower. (al-Ayni) Intercourse: meaning if the mufawwidah woman is divorced before intercourse, mut'ah is obligatory for her. (al-Ayni)
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with commentary on the categories of mut'ah (consolatory gift) in Hanafi fiqh. The primary ruling is that mut'ah is wajib for a mufawwidah—a woman married without specifying a dower—who is divorced before consummation. The commentary from al-Ayni then expands this into four categories: (1) wajib: for the mufawwidah divorced before consummation; (2) mustahabb: for a woman divorced after consummation when no dower was specified; (3) sunnah: for a woman divorced after consummation when a dower was specified, because divorce after intimacy causes her grief, so the husband is encouraged to give something extra; (4) neither wajib, sunnah, nor mustahabb: for a woman divorced before consummation when a dower was specified, because half the dower already serves the purpose of mut'ah. The passage also defines mufawwidah linguistically and reiterates the obligation of mut'ah in her case.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift (compensation) given by a husband to a wife upon divorce, as prescribed in the Quran.
المفوّضة (al-mufawwidah): A woman who is married without a specified dower (mahr), i.e., the marriage contract includes no mention of mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Shighar Marriage: Validity and Mahr al-Mithl
Defines shighar, presents dispute with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on shighar marriage, identify the Shafi'i counterargument, and state the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Shighar marriage is valid in Hanafi but invalid in Shafi'i; the Hanafi school assigns mahr al-mithl due to the invalid condition.

Shighar is an exchange marriage where two men marry each other's female relatives, with each woman's vulva serving as the dower for the other. This practice existed in pre-Islamic times and was forbidden by the Prophet (ﷺ). The Hanafi school interprets the prohibition as relating to the absence of a proper dower, not the structure itself, thus ruling the marriage valid but disliked (makruh) and requiring mahr al-mithl. This lesson examines the proofs and rebuttals between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Guided Path
1
Define shighar
Understand the precise definition: each man gives a female relative in marriage in exchange for the other's female relative, with the vulva being the dower.
The term derives from a dog lifting its leg or an empty land.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that both contracts are valid (ja'iz) but makruh, and each woman receives mahr al-mithl instead of the specified vulva.
The ruling is mufta bihi (relied upon).
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i rules the contracts invalid, citing the hadith 'No shighar in Islam' and the logical issue of making part of the vulva dower and part the object of marriage.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and others.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions (e.g., naming blood as dower), and the prohibition is either a disliked (makruh) practice or a ban on the Jahili custom of leaving dower unspecified. The vulva cannot be dower, so mahr al-mithl is due.
The partnership argument is rejected because the vulva is unfit to be dower.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in Hanafi, the marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl must be paid; in Shafi'i, the marriage is invalid and must be annulled.
This affects whether the couple may continue living together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الشغار [ أي في نكاح الشغار وهو أن يزوج الرجل بنته أو أخته على أن يزوجه الآخر بنته أو أخته على أن يكون بضع كل واحدة منهما صداقا للأخرى فالعقدان جائزان ويجب مهر المثل لكل منهما. (ط)] في الصحاح يقال : شغر الكلب إذا رفع إحدى رجليه للبول، وسمي هذا العقد به؛ لأنهما بهذا الشرط كأنهما رفعا المهر وأخليا البضع أو مأخوذ من قولهم بلدة شاغرة أي خالية، والمراد أن يكون في العقدين بضع كل واحدة منهما صداقا للأخرى ولا يكون المهر فيهما سوى هذا، فالعقدان جائزان عندنا، ويجب لكل منهما مهر المثل، وقال الشافعي: يبطل العقدان؛ لحديث نافع عن ابن عمر لما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن الشغار وليس بينهما صداق"، رواه الجماعة وعن عبد بن عمر لهما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا شغار في الإسلام"، رواه مسلم؛ ولأنه جعل نصف البضع مهراً والنصف منكوحاً، ولا اشتراك في هذا الباب فيبطل به الإيجاب. ولنا أن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة ألا ترى أنه لا يفسد بتسمية ما ليس بمال كالدم والخنزير ولا بترك التسمية بالكلية، والنهي الوارد فيه إنما كان من أجل إخلائه عن تسمية المهر من غير أن يجب فيه شيء آخر على ما كانت عليه عادتهم في الجاهلية أو هو محمول على الكراهة ولا وجه لجعله نصف البضع مهرا والنصف منكوحا؛ لأنه لم يجتمع النكاح والصداق في بضع واحد؛ لعدم صلاحية البضع صداقاً، فلا يتصور الاشتراك مع عدم الاستحقاق فيجب مهر المثل؛ لأنه سمي ما لا يصلح مهرا، وأجمعوا أنه لو قال: زوجتك ابنتي على أن تزوجني ابنتك، ولم يقل: على أن يكون بضع كل واحدة منهما صداقاً للأخرى جاز النكاح ولا يكون شغاراً، ويجب مهر المثل أيضاً. (عيني، فتح)
Regarding shighar: [Meaning the marriage of shighar, which is that a man gives his daughter or sister in marriage on condition that the other gives his daughter or sister in marriage to him, on the basis that the vulva of each one is the dower for the other. Both contracts are valid and each woman is entitled to the dower of the like. (Tahawi)] In al-Sihah it is said: 'Shaghara al-kalb' when the dog lifts one leg for urination, and this contract is named after it because by this condition they have, as it were, raised the dower and vacated the vulva. Or it is derived from their saying 'baldah shaghirah' meaning empty. The intent is that in the two contracts, the vulva of each woman is the dower for the other, and there is no dower other than this. So both contracts are valid in our school, and each woman is entitled to the dower of the like. Al-Shafi'i said: The contracts are invalid, due to the hadith of Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade shighar and there is no dower between them, narrated by the group (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.), and from 'Abd ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (ﷺ): 'No shighar in Islam', narrated by Muslim; and because he has made half the vulva as dower and half as the married object, and there is no partnership in this chapter, so the offer becomes void. Our proof: Marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions; do you not see that it is not invalidated by naming something that is not property like blood or pork, nor by omitting the dower altogether. The prohibition in it is only because of its being devoid of naming a dower without anything else being obligatory, as was their custom in Jahiliyyah, or it is interpreted as makruh. There is no basis for making half the vulva dower and half married, because marriage and dower do not combine in one vulva due to the vulva's unfitness to be dower. So partnership is inconceivable with lack of entitlement, therefore the dower of the like is obligatory because he named what is not suitable as dower. And they have agreed that if one says: 'I marry my daughter to you on condition that you marry your daughter to me', without saying 'on condition that the vulva of each is the dower for the other', the marriage is valid and it is not shighar, and the dower of the like is also obligatory. (al-Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding shighar marriage. Shighar is defined as an exchange marriage where each man gives his female relative in marriage to the other, with the vulva of each serving as the dower for the other. The Hanafi position (presented first) holds that both contracts are valid (ja'iz) and each woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) instead of the specified vulva. Al-Shafi'i argues that the contracts are invalid due to the explicit prophetic prohibition and the logical issue of making part of the vulva dower and part the subject of marriage. The Hanafi response is that marriage contracts are not invalidated by invalid conditions, as evidenced by the permissibility of naming something non-property as dower or omitting dower entirely. The prohibition is either because of the Jahili practice of leaving dower unspecified, or it is interpreted as makruh (disliked) rather than invalid. The claim of splitting the vulva is rejected because the vulva cannot be valid dower. Therefore, since an unsuitable dower was named, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The Hanafis also note that if the condition is phrased without specifying vulva as dower, the marriage is valid and not considered shighar, but mahr al-mithl is still required.

Key Terms
الشغار (al-shighar): An exchange marriage where a man marries a woman to another man on condition that the other man marries his female relative, with the vulva of each being the dower.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of the like: the appropriate dower for a woman based on her family, status, and similar considerations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on shighar marriage?
A) The marriage is invalid
B) The marriage is valid and each woman receives what was agreed
C) The marriage is valid and each woman receives mahr al-mithl
D) The marriage is makruh and no mahr is due

Key Takeaway
Shighar marriage is valid in the Hanafi school, but the invalid condition is replaced by mahr al-mithl.
