Return of Mahr upon Divorce Before Consummation After Gift Back
Explains three scenarios of mahr return when wife gifts mahr back and is divorced before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for three scenarios of mahr return when the wife gifts back the mahr and divorce occurs before consummation, and explain the differences between Abu Hanifa and his disciples.

Core Idea
When mahr is gifted back before divorce, istihsan may prevent the husband from recovering anything, but strict qiyas allows recovery.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents three scenarios of mahr (dower) return when a wife gifts back the mahr and then divorce occurs before consummation. The Hanafi school has internal disagreements on each scenario, involving principles of qiyas and istihsan. Understanding these rulings clarifies the interplay between equity and strict analogy in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The text discusses three distinct cases based on whether the mahr was received, partially received, or was a specific commodity. Identify each case:
Case 1: Mahr not received but gifted. Case 2: Half received and gifted. Case 3: Specific commodity received and gifted.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling for each
For each case, state Abu Hanifa's ruling. In case 1: no return; case 2: no return; case 3: passage incomplete, but likely he would also apply istihsan.
Abu Hanifa's view is based on istihsan: the husband's objective of being released from half the mahr is achieved.
3
Identify the opposing views
Identify who disagrees: for case 1, Zufar; for case 2, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; for case 3, Zufar. State their ruling: they would require the husband to return half (or half value).
The opposing view is based on qiyas: the wife's gift does not cancel the obligation to return half.
4
Analyze the legal principles
Understand that the dispute hinges on whether the gift (hibah) is treated as a separate transaction or as part of the original mahr contract. Abu Hanifa treats it separately, so the husband's liability is already discharged. The disciples see it as integrated.
This is a classic tension between istihsan (equity) and qiyas (strict analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قبضت أي لو تزوج امرأة على ألف وقبضت المرأة (ط) له أي للزوج ألف المهر الذي قبضته. (ع) رجع عليها بالنصف [ أي بنصف الألف الذي هو المهر وهو خمس مائة درهم. (ع)] لأنه طلاق قبل الدخول، فلا يجب إلا نصف المهر والدراهم والدنانير لا يتعينان في العقود والفسوخ عندنا، فصار كهبة مال آخر، وعند الثلاثة: لا يرجع [رمز الحقائق: ٢١٢/١] فإن لم تقبض وهذه ثلاث مسائل: الأولى : أنه تزوجها على ألف وطلقها قبل الدخول و لم تقبض الألف، بل وهبتها، فلا يرجع الزوج عليها بشيء استحساناً؛ لأنه حصل له مقصوده، وهو براءة ذمته عن نصف الصداق بالطلاق قبل الدخول، وفي القياس يرجع عليها بنصف الألف، وبه قال زفر؛ لأن المهر قد سلم له للإبراء، فلا تبرئ هي عما يستحقه هو بالطلاق قبل الدخول. والمسألة الثانية: ما ذكرها المصنف بقوله : "أو قبضت "النصف" أي المرأة قبضت خمس مائة من المهر ثم وهبت له المقبوض وغير المقبوض، ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لم يرجع أحدهما على الآخر بشيء عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: يرجع عليها الزوج بنصف ما قبضت كما إذا قبضت الكل، اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، ولأبي حنيفة أن مقصود الزوج قد حصل، وهو سلامة نصف المهر له بلا عوض والحط لا يلتحق بأصل العقد في النكاح عنده، وعندهما: يلتحق. والمسألة الثالثة: أنه تزوجها على عرض كحيوان أو ثوب مثلاً، فقبضت ثم وهبت له ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها، بشيء، والقياس أن أحدهما على الآخر يرجع عليها الزوج بنصف قيمة العرض، وهو قول زفر؛ لأن الواجب رد عين نصف المهر وهذا العرض ليس بعين المهر؛ لأن المهر دين في الألف وهذا عين، فكان عوضه ، =
And if she received: meaning if a man marries a woman for one thousand (dirhams) and the woman received (the thousand) and gifted it to him (the husband), then he divorces her before consummation, he takes back half (of the thousand, i.e., five hundred dirhams) because it is divorce before consummation, so only half the dower is due. And dirhams and dinars are not determined (specific) in contracts and dissolutions according to us, so it becomes like a gift of other property. And according to the three: he does not take back [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 212/1]. If she did not receive: and there are three cases: The first: that he married her for one thousand and divorced her before consummation and she did not receive the thousand, but rather she gifted it (to him), then the husband does not take anything from her by istihsan, because his objective is achieved, which is the discharge of his liability for half the dower by divorce before consummation. In qiyas, he would take back half the thousand, and Zufar said that, because the dower was given to him for discharge (from liability), so she cannot discharge what he is entitled to by divorce before consummation. The second case: what the author mentioned by his saying: 'or she received half': meaning the woman received five hundred of the dower, then she gifted to him what she received and what she did not receive, then he divorced her before consummation; according to Abu Hanifa, neither takes anything from the other; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the husband takes half of what she received, just as if she received the whole, by analogy of the part to the whole. For Abu Hanifa, the husband's objective is achieved, which is the safety of half the dower for him without compensation, and remission (hatt) does not attach to the original contract in marriage according to him, but according to them it does attach. The third case: that he married her for a commodity like an animal or a garment, for example, she received it, then gifted it to him, then he divorced her before consummation; by qiyas, one of them... the husband takes back half the value of the commodity, and this is the saying of Zufar, because the obligation is to return the specific half of the dower, and this commodity is not the specific dower; because the dower is a debt in the thousand and this is a specific item, so it becomes its substitute... =
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the return of mahr when the woman gifts the mahr back to the husband and then divorce occurs before consummation. The text discusses three distinct cases. The first case: the woman never received the mahr (a sum of 1000 dirhams) but gifted it to the husband. By istihsan (equity), since the husband's liability for half the mahr is discharged by the divorce, he does not recover anything. By qiyas, he would recover half, as Zufar argues. The second case: the woman received half the mahr (500 dirhams) and then gifted both the received and unreceived portions to the husband. Abu Hanifa rules no one recovers anything, as the husband's objective (release from half the mahr) is achieved. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) rule that the husband recovers half of what she received (i.e., 250 dirhams), treating the partial gift like the full gift by analogy. The third case concerns a specific commodity (e.g., animal or garment) as mahr; the woman received it and gifted it back, then divorce before consummation. The qiyas (according to Zufar) is that the husband recovers half the value, because the obligation is to return the specific half of the commodity, but since it was gifted, it is no longer in her possession, so he gets its value. The passage cuts off, but the Hanafi relied-upon position likely follows Abu Hanifa in the first two cases and gives the commodity case to Zufar or the two?

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juridical preference: departing from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling.
الهبة (al-hibah): Gift: transfer of ownership without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman marries for 1000 dirhams, never receives it, gifts it to her husband, and then he divorces her before consummation, what does the husband recover according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) 500 dirhams
B) 1000 dirhams
C) Nothing
D) 250 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a wife gifts back the mahr before divorce, istihsan may protect the husband from returning anything, while qiyas would require return of half.

Teaching Quran as Mahr: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on teaching Quran as mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on teaching Quran as mahr, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Teaching is not property; a marriage contracted on that basis is valid but the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

The dower (mahr) in marriage must be property (mal) according to the Hanafi school. But what if the husband stipulates teaching the Quran as the dower? This lesson examines the ruling and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who cites a famous hadith. Understanding the Hanafi position and its proof is essential to correctly apply the law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the marriage contract is valid but the stipulated dower (teaching) is not valid. The wife receives mahr al-mithl (the proper dower of her peers).
The contract is not invalidated by an invalid dower stipulation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that teaching the Quran is a valid dower, based on the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd.
The hadith is reported in Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'I have married her to you for what you have of the Quran.' This is the Shafi'i dalil.
They interpret 'what you have' as teaching or the Quran itself as the dower.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the hadith does not explicitly make the Quran a dower; rather it indicates the man's virtue. Analogous to Abu Talha's marriage upon his Islam, which is not a valid dower.
The phrase 'what you have' refers to his Quranic knowledge, not a transferable property.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, the wife gets mahr al-mithl (monetary). Under Shafi'i, she gets teaching the Quran. This is the practical consequence of the dispute.
Both schools consider the marriage valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعليم القرآن [ أي يجب مهر المثل أيضاً في التزويج على تعليم القرآن؛ لأن التعليم ليس بمال. (ع)] يعني لو تزوج امرأة على أنه يعلمها القرآن فالعقد صحيح ولها مهر مثلها وقال الشافعي لها تعليم القرآن كما في حديث سهل ابن سعد الساعدي: هل معك شيء من القرآن ؟ قال: نعم، فقال عليه: "قد ملكتكها بما معك من القرآن"، رواه أبو داود، قلنا: ليس فيه دلالة على أن القرآن جعله مهراً، ولهذا لم يشترط أن يعلمها، وإنما ركة ما معك أو لأجل أنك من أهل القرآن فكان كتزوج أبي طلحة على إسلامه، وهو لا يصلح صداقاً للبضع.
And teaching the Quran: that is, mahr al-mithl is obligatory also in marriage upon teaching the Quran because teaching is not property. Meaning if a man marries a woman on condition that he teaches her the Quran, the contract is valid and she gets her mahr al-mithl. Al-Shafi'i said she gets teaching the Quran as per the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi: 'Do you have anything of the Quran?' He said 'Yes.' He said: 'I have married her to you for what you have of the Quran.' Reported by Abu Dawud. We say: there is no indication in it that the Quran was made a dower; for this reason he did not stipulate that he teach her, but rather [the phrase] 'what you have' or because you are among the people of the Quran, so it is like the marriage of Abu Talha upon his Islam, and that is not valid as a dower for the vulva.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of making teaching the Quran a dower (mahr). The Hanafi position is that teaching is not considered property (mal), so the contract is valid but the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the proper dower of her peers), not the teaching itself. The Shafi'i school, citing the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd where the Prophet married a woman to a man for what he knew of the Quran, holds that teaching the Quran is a valid dower. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the hadith does not expressly make the Quran the dower; rather, it was due to the man's stature as a Quran bearer, akin to Abu Talha's marriage upon his Islam, which is not a valid dower. Thus, teaching is not a property that can serve as dower.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to that of women of her status, due when the specified dower is invalid or not mentioned.
صداق (sadaq): Synonym for mahr (dower). In this context, the dower given by the husband to the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a man marries a woman on condition that he teaches her the Quran?
A) The marriage is invalid.
B) The contract is valid and she gets teaching of Quran as dower.
C) The contract is valid and she gets mahr al-mithl.
D) The contract is valid but no dower is due.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, teaching is not property; a marriage contracted on that basis is valid but the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

Service of a Slave as Valid Dower (Mahr)
Ruling on slave's service as valid dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's service as mahr and distinguish it from a free man's service.

Core Idea
A slave's service is property; a free man's service is not.

In Hanafi fiqh, the dower (mahr) must be property (mal). This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies that the service of a slave husband qualifies as property because the slave himself is owned. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between what is valid and invalid as mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that a woman is entitled to the service of her husband if he is a slave and the marriage contract stipulated such service. This is valid mahr.
The ruling is specific to slaves; free men are treated differently.
2
Analyze the reason (ta'lil)
The commentator explains that a slave's service is property because it involves the surrender of his person (raqabah). Since the slave is owned, his labor is a commodity.
The key concept is raqabah — ownership of the slave's entire being.
3
Distinguish the free man
A free man's service cannot be mahr because a free person is not property. His service is not considered mal in the sense required for mahr.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولها خدمته لو عبداً : أي لو تزوج عبد على أن يخدم المرأة سنة مثلا فللمرأة أخذ الخدمة منه؛ لأن الخدمة مال لما فيه من تسليم رقبته بخلاف الحر.
And she has his service if he is a slave: that is, if a slave marries on condition that he serves the woman for a year, for example, the woman may take the service from him because the service is property as it involves surrender of his person, unlike a free man.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn: a woman is entitled to the service of her husband if he is a slave and the marriage contract stipulated such service. The commentator explains that a slave's service is considered property (mal) because it involves the surrender of his person (i.e., his labor and ownership), unlike a free man whose service is not property because a free person cannot be owned. Thus, a slave can validly promise his service as mahr.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): Service or labor; in this context, the work a slave does for his owner or, by stipulation, for his wife.
رقبة (raqabah): The person of a slave, which is owned as property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the service of a slave valid as mahr according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because all labor is property.
B) Because the slave's service involves surrender of his person (raqabah), which is property.
C) Because the woman can force a free man to serve her.
D) Because the slave's service is equivalent to money.

Key Takeaway
A slave's service is valid mahr because it is property (mal) derived from ownership of his person; a free man's service is not.

Waiver of Mahr Before Consummation: Three Images
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr waiver before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling in each of the three images of mahr waiver before consummation and explain the istihsan principle that supports the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a wife waives the mahr before or after receipt and is divorced before consummation, Abu Hanifa holds that the husband takes nothing—his objective is achieved, overriding strict qiyas.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a wife's waiver of the mahr (dower) before or after receipt, followed by divorce before consummation. The central question is whether the husband can reclaim any portion of the mahr after such a waiver. The text presents three distinct images, each with differing views among Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Zufar. The mufta bihi position, based on istihsan, is that the husband does not take back anything in any of the three images. By working through these scenarios, you will understand how the Hanafi school balances qiyas with istihsan in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Images
The passage presents three distinct factual scenarios involving waiver of mahr before consummation. Distinguish them: (1) wife waives entire mahr before receipt, (2) wife receives half and waives all, (3) mahr is a specific commodity, received and waived. Note the key variables: receipt, amount, and type of mahr.
Focus on the timing of waiver relative to receipt and the nature of the mahr (cash vs. commodity).
2
State the Ruling for Each Image by Imam
For each image, state the ruling of Abu Hanifa, then the opposing view (Sahibayn or Zufar). In Image 1: Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn agree: husband takes nothing; Zufar disagrees: husband takes back half. Image 2: Abu Hanifa: husband takes nothing; Sahibayn: husband takes back half of what she received. Image 3: Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn: husband takes nothing; Zufar: husband takes back half the value.
Note the pattern: Abu Hanifa consistently holds the husband takes nothing; the disagreement is only in Images 2 and 3, and with different opponents.
3
Understand the Dalil: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Abu Hanifa's ruling is based on istihsan: the husband's objective (safety of half the mahr) is achieved through the waiver, even though the mechanism differs from the default rule of returning half. The opponents (Sahibayn, Zufar) rely on qiyas: since the wife received part or all of the mahr, she should return half of what she received, because the default rule after divorce before consummation is that the wife keeps half and the husband is entitled to half. Analyze why istihsan overrides qiyas here.
The key concept is that waiver (hiba) and discharge (ibra') are not strictly analogous to the original obligation; the law favors achieving the husband's objective.
4
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The practical difference between Abu Hanifa's position and the opponents is whether the husband can reclaim anything after the waiver. Under Abu Hanifa, the husband gets nothing; under the opponents, he gets back half of what the wife received (in Image 2) or half the value (in Image 3). This affects the financial outcome for both parties.
The dispute is ultimately about the enforceability of the waiver when the default right to half arises.
5
Confirm the Mufta Bihi
The text concludes that in all three images, the husband does not take back anything. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa, following Abu Hanifa's view supported by istihsan.
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopt this as the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قبضت ألف المهر ووهبت له فطلقت قبل الوطء رجع عليها بالنصف، فإن لم تقبض وهذه ثلاث مسائل: الأولى : أنه تزوجها على ألف وطلقها قبل الدخول و لم تقبض الألف، بل وهبتها، فلا يرجع الزوج عليها بشيء استحساناً؛ لأنه حصل له مقصوده، وهو براءة ذمته عن نصف الصداق بالطلاق قبل الدخول، وفي القياس يرجع عليها بنصف الألف، وبه قال زفر؛ لأن المهر قد سلم له للإبراء، فلا تبرئ هي عما يستحقه هو بالطلاق قبل الدخول. والمسألة الثانية: ما ذكرها المصنف بقوله : "أو قبضت "النصف" أي المرأة قبضت خمس مائة من المهر ثم وهبت له المقبوض وغير المقبوض، ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لم يرجع أحدهما على الآخر بشيء عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: يرجع عليها الزوج بنصف ما قبضت كما إذا قبضت الكل، اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، ولأبي حنيفة أن مقصود الزوج قد حصل، وهو سلامة نصف المهر له بلا عوض والحط لا يلتحق بأصل العقد في النكاح عنده، وعندهما: يلتحق. والمسألة الثالثة: أنه تزوجها على عرض كحيوان أو ثوب مثلاً، فقبضت ثم وهبت له ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها، بشيء، والقياس أن أحدهما على الآخر يرجع عليها الزوج بنصف قيمة العرض، وهو قول زفر؛ لأن الواجب رد عين نصف المهر وهذا العرض ليس بعين المهر؛ لأن المهر دين في الألف وهذا عين، فكان عوضه . الألف أو قبضت النصف ووهبت الألف أو ما بقي أو وهبت عرض المهر قبل القبض أو بعده فطلقت قبل الوطء لم يرجع عليها بشيء
And if she received the thousand dower and gifted it to him and he divorced her before intercourse, he takes back from her half. But if she did not receive—and there are three issues: The first: he married her for one thousand and divorced her before entry and she did not receive the thousand but gifted it, then the husband does not take back anything from her by istihsan because he obtained his objective, which is freedom of his liability from half the dower due to divorce before entry. By qiyas he would take back half the thousand, and this is the saying of Zufar because the dower was given to him for release, so she cannot release what he is entitled to by divorce before entry. The second issue: what the author mentioned by his saying 'or she received half'—that is, the woman received five hundred of the dower, then gifted to him what she received and what she did not receive, then he divorced her before entry—neither takes back anything from the other according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: the husband takes back from her half of what she received, as if she received all, treating part like whole. For Abu Hanifa, the husband's objective is obtained, which is safety of half the dower for him without compensation, and reduction does not attach to the original marriage contract according to him. According to them, it attaches. The third issue: he married her for a specific commodity like an animal or garment, for example, she received it, then gifted it to him, then he divorced her before entry—[he takes back?] something. By qiyas, one takes back from the other, the husband takes back half the value of the commodity, and this is the saying of Zufar because the obligation is to return the exact half of the dower, and this commodity is not the exact dower because the dower is a debt in the thousand, and this is a specific item, so it is its substitute. The thousand or she received half and gifted the thousand or what remained or she gifted the commodity dower before or after receipt, then divorced before intercourse—he does not take back anything from her.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute detailing three images where a wife waives the mahr (dower) before or after receipt and is then divorced before consummation. The core principle is that after divorce before consummation, the wife is entitled to half the mahr, but if she has waived it, the husband's right to reclaim varies.

Image One: Wife waives the entire mahr before receiving it. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the husband does not take back anything (istihsan), because he obtains his objective—freedom from liability for half the mahr. Zufar says he takes back half by qiyas, since the mahr was released to him for ibra', and she cannot release what he is entitled to.

Image Two: Wife receives half the mahr (500), then waives the entire mahr (both received and unpaid). After divorce before entry, Abu Hanifa says neither party takes anything from the other (his objective obtained). The Sahibayn say husband takes back half of what she received (250), likening partial receipt to full receipt.

Image Three: Mahr is a specific commodity (e.g., animal or cloth). Wife receives it, then waives it to husband. After divorce before entry, Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn say husband takes back nothing (his objective of having half the mahr safe is achieved because the commodity is specific property). Zufar says he takes back half the value because the obligation is to return the exact half, and this commodity is not the exact mahr (since mahr is a debt in the thousand, not a specific item). The text concludes that in all three images, if after waiver and divorce before entry, the husband does not take back anything. This is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding strict qiyas for reason of maslaha or custom. Here used to prefer the husband's objective being met.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning. Zufar and Sahibayn use qiyas demanding return of half.
براءة الذمة (bara'at al-dhimmah): Freedom from liability; here the husband's liability for half the mahr is discharged by the divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second image (woman receives half of the mahr then waives all), what is Abu Hanifa's ruling?
A) The husband takes back half of what she received.
B) The husband takes back nothing.
C) The husband takes back the full half.
D) The wife must return the entire mahr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that in all cases of mahr waiver before consummation, the husband takes nothing, based on istihsan that his objective of securing half the mahr is attained.
